\section*{What can now be rigorously closed}

We isolate the strongest statements that can be proved \emph{without overclaiming} from the uploaded Math15 draft together with the previously established Math10--13 structure.

\subsection*{Setup}

Consider the minimal complex-triplet Brazovskii wave equation
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi,
\qquad
Z<0,\quad Y>0,\quad g>0,
\end{equation}
and a locked single-shell background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=A e^{iG\cdot x} z_0,
\qquad
|G|=q_*,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y},
\qquad
z_0^\dagger z_0=1.
\end{equation}
Let the transverse fluctuation be
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_\perp(x,t)=A e^{iG\cdot x}\chi(x,t),
\qquad
\chi(x,t)\in Q_{z_0}:=(\mathbb C z_0)^\perp,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger\chi=0.
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Theorem 1. Linearized quartic no-go}

\begin{theorem}
At linear order in the fluctuation, the quartic term
\(
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
\)
does not directly generate any enriched first-order operator of the form
\[
(\partial_i\Psi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Expand
\begin{equation}
\Psi=\Psi_0+\delta\Psi.
\end{equation}
Then, to first order,
\begin{equation}
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi
=
g\Bigl[
(\Psi_0^\dagger\Psi_0)\delta\Psi
+
(\Psi_0^\dagger\delta\Psi)\Psi_0
+
(\delta\Psi^\dagger\Psi_0)\Psi_0
\Bigr]
+
O(\delta\Psi^2).
\end{equation}
Now decompose
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi=\delta\Psi_\parallel+\delta\Psi_\perp,
\qquad
\delta\Psi_\parallel=\delta\rho\,z_0,
\qquad
\delta\Psi_\perp\in Q_{z_0}.
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
z_0^\dagger\delta\Psi_\perp=0,
\end{equation}
the mixed terms
\(
(\Psi_0^\dagger\delta\Psi)\Psi_0
\)
and
\(
(\delta\Psi^\dagger\Psi_0)\Psi_0
\)
depend only on the longitudinal amplitude fluctuation \(\delta\rho\), while
\(
(\Psi_0^\dagger\Psi_0)\delta\Psi=A^2\delta\Psi
\)
is a local mass-type term.

Therefore the linearized quartic contribution contains only zeroth-order operators in derivatives acting on \(\delta\Psi\), and in particular contains no term bilinear in
\[
\partial_i\Psi_0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\partial_j\chi.
\]
Hence it does not directly produce an enriched first-order tensor
\(
N_{ij}^a
\).
\end{proof}

\subsection*{Theorem 2. Exact shell cancellation of the isotropic kinetic first-order term}

\begin{theorem}
For the minimal isotropic kinetic operator
\[
Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4,
\]
the shell-projected first-order transport term in the envelope \(\chi\) vanishes exactly at the Brazovskii shell
\(
q_*^2=-Z/(2Y)
\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Write
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_\perp=A e^{iG\cdot x}\chi.
\end{equation}
Introduce the shifted differential operator
\begin{equation}
D_G:=\nabla+iG.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\nabla(e^{iG\cdot x}\chi)=e^{iG\cdot x}D_G\chi,
\qquad
\nabla^2(e^{iG\cdot x}\chi)=e^{iG\cdot x}D_G^2\chi,
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
D_G^2
=
\nabla^2+2iG\cdot\nabla-|G|^2
=
\nabla^2+2iG\cdot\nabla-q_*^2.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
(Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4)\delta\Psi_\perp
=
A e^{iG\cdot x}
\Bigl[
Z D_G^2 - Y(D_G^2)^2
\Bigr]\chi.
\end{equation}
Retain only terms up to first order in the slow envelope derivative \(\nabla\chi\). Since
\begin{equation}
D_G^2
=
-q_*^2 + 2iG\cdot\nabla + O(\nabla^2),
\end{equation}
we get
\begin{align}
(D_G^2)^2
&=
\bigl(-q_*^2 + 2iG\cdot\nabla + O(\nabla^2)\bigr)^2
\\
&=
q_*^4 - 4iq_*^2\,G\cdot\nabla + O(\nabla^2).
\end{align}
Therefore
\begin{align}
Z D_G^2 - Y(D_G^2)^2
&=
\Bigl(-Zq_*^2-Yq_*^4\Bigr)
+
2i\Bigl(Z+2Yq_*^2\Bigr)\,G\cdot\nabla
+
O(\nabla^2).
\end{align}
Now impose the shell condition
\begin{equation}
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
Z+2Yq_*^2
=
Z+2Y\Bigl(-\frac{Z}{2Y}\Bigr)
=
0.
\end{equation}
Hence the entire first-order transport coefficient vanishes:
\begin{equation}
2i\Bigl(Z+2Yq_*^2\Bigr)G\cdot\nabla = 0.
\end{equation}
Thus the minimal isotropic kinetic operator produces no nonzero first-order shell transport term at the exact Brazovskii shell.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{Theorem 3. Locked cross-shell quartic projection vanishes at zeroth order}

\begin{theorem}
In the exactly polarization-locked background, the zeroth-order projected cross-shell quartic term vanishes identically on \(Q_{z_0}\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Consider a second shell mode with internal direction \(u_{**}\). The projected cross-shell quartic contribution has the form
\begin{equation}
\Pi_0\Bigl[(u_{**}^\dagger\chi)\,u_{**}\Bigr].
\end{equation}
In the locked background,
\begin{equation}
u_{**}=z_0.
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\Pi_0\Bigl[(z_0^\dagger\chi)\,z_0\Bigr]
=
(z_0^\dagger\chi)\,\Pi_0 z_0
=
0,
\end{equation}
because \(\chi\in Q_{z_0}\) implies \(z_0^\dagger\chi=0\), and also \(\Pi_0 z_0=0\).

Hence the locked zeroth-order cross-shell quartic projection is exactly zero.
\end{proof}

\subsection*{Corollary. What is actually closed now}

\begin{corollary}
For the minimal locked isotropic complex-triplet Brazovskii equation, the following statement is rigorously established:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the enriched Pauli-sector shell tensor }N_{ij}^a
\text{ is \emph{not yet derived} from the minimal locked single-mode calculation alone.}
}
\end{equation}
More precisely:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the linear quartic term gives no direct enriched first-order source;
\item the isotropic kinetic first-order shell term cancels exactly at \(q_*\);
\item the locked zeroth-order cross-shell quartic projection vanishes.
\end{enumerate}
Therefore any genuine nonzero shell-enriched tensor must come from \emph{additional structure}, such as:
\begin{enumerate}
\item a full 12-mode BCC gradient-expansion calculation beyond the locked single-mode truncation,
\item polarization unlocking,
\item or an explicit Class II mediator / enriched UV channel.
\end{enumerate}
\end{corollary}

\subsection*{What remains honestly open}

The remaining microscopic witness problem is therefore not solved by the present Math15 derivation. What remains open is the explicit production of the three shell witnesses
\[
g_\parallel,\qquad g_I,\qquad g_J
\]
(or equivalently \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\))
from the \emph{actual} full microscopic TECT linearization.

Thus the corrected honest status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{minimal locked isotropic PDE alone is insufficient,}
}
\end{equation}
whereas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the Class II-enriched route remains a mathematically consistent explicit mechanism}
}
\end{equation}
for generating
\(
\delta N_{ij}^a\neq 0
\)
at shell-reduced level.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Corrected closure after Math15}
}
\]

\[
\text{Closed rigorously:}
\]

\begin{enumerate}
\item The linearized quartic term does not directly generate
\[
(\partial_i\Psi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]

\item For the minimal isotropic Brazovskii operator,
\[
Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4,
\]
the first-order shell transport coefficient is
\[
2i(Z+2Yq_*^2)G\cdot\nabla,
\]
hence vanishes exactly at
\[
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\]

\item In the exactly locked background, the zeroth-order cross-shell quartic projection onto
\[
Q_{z_0}
\]
vanishes identically.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the minimal locked isotropic PDE does not yet by itself close the }N_{ij}^a\text{ witness problem.}
}
\]

What remains open is the explicit microscopic generation of
\[
g_\parallel,\qquad g_I,\qquad g_J
\]
from one of the following:
\[
\text{full 12-mode BCC Bloch linearization},
\qquad
\text{polarization unlocking},
\qquad
\text{or explicit Class II mediation}.
\]

Hence the honest current status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Dirac emergence remains theorem-level / shell-reduced closed,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{full microscopic closure in complete TECT is still open.}
}
\]

\section*{Next rigorous step in the TECT proof chain}

\paragraph{Principle.}
The next step is \emph{not} to re-prove the reduced Weyl/Dirac theorem.
That part is already closed once the shell witnesses
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
are nonzero in the required pattern.
The actual remaining microscopic task is to prove that the \emph{full microscopic TECT transport space}
contains the required seed directions.

\paragraph{Microscopic transport space.}
Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\]
denote the symmetry-allowed microscopic transport tensor space obtained by linearizing the full TECT dynamics around the relevant defect/BCC background.

Let the explicit shell-adapted seed subspace be
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\Bigl\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\Bigr\}.
\]

For a general seed combination
\[
N
=
c_\parallel N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_E N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
+
c_O N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\]
the reduced witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:nextstep_seed_eval}
\end{equation}

Assuming
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
one immediately gets the exact nondegeneracy criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0)
}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\ \ (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:nextstep_seed_criterion}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Immediate consequence.}
Therefore the reduced Weyl witness problem is already closed \emph{inside the explicit seed ansatz space}.
So the remaining task is not to prove that such seeds \emph{could} work.
The remaining task is to prove that the actual microscopic transport space contains them:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{seed}}\subset V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\quad\text{or at least}\quad
V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\text{ contains one longitudinal and one transverse seed direction.}
}
\label{eq:nextstep_embedding_goal}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Carrier-audit completion criterion.}
Equivalently, let
\[
T^{(\parallel)},\qquad T^{(\perp,E)},\qquad T^{(\perp,O)}
\]
be the corresponding target covectors/witness channels.
Then the carrier audit succeeds iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}T^{(\parallel)}\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\bigl(P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}T^{(\perp,E)},P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}T^{(\perp,O)}\bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nextstep_projection_test}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Why the longitudinal channel is the true bottleneck.}
Suppose the transverse odd-gradient extraction has already been shown to survive microscopically.
Then the transverse condition
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
is no longer the open part of the problem.
The only remaining microscopic carrier question becomes the survival of the primitive longitudinal channel producing
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

Hence the sharp next theorem to prove is:

\begin{theorem}[Longitudinal primitive-channel survival theorem: target form]
Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) be the full microscopic transport tensor space obtained from the true TECT linearization around the physically relevant background.
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse carrier channel survives in \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\);
\item the microscopic transport sector contains one admissible primitive longitudinal direction whose reduced projection onto the seed covector \(T^{(\parallel)}\) is nonzero.
\end{enumerate}
Then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
and therefore the local shell-reduced Weyl symbol is nondegenerate.
Consequently the local Dirac reduction theorem applies.
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{After this step.}
Once the carrier audit is closed, the next microscopic tasks are:
\begin{enumerate}
\item remote-label mismatch audit implying \(V(0)=0\),
\item remote-gap positivity audit giving \(\Delta>0\),
\item exact residual valley symmetry audit giving mass protection,
\item only afterwards the full derivative-anisotropy/FRG closure.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the correct proof order is
\[
\boxed{
\text{carrier audit}
\;\to\;
V(0)=0
\;\to\;
\Delta>0
\;\to\;
\text{mass protection}
\;\to\;
M_Z\text{/FRG}.
}
\]

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Correct next step in the TECT proof chain}
}
\]

The reduced Weyl/Dirac witness theorem is already closed inside the explicit Class II seed space:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\]
so nondegeneracy holds iff
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Therefore the true remaining microscopic task is not to re-prove the seed theorem, but to prove that the full microscopic TECT transport space contains the required seed directions:
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}\subset V_{\mathrm{mic}}
\quad\text{or at least one longitudinal and one transverse seed direction.}
\]

Because the transverse carrier channel is already largely solved, the main bottleneck is the survival of the primitive longitudinal channel:
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

Hence the correct proof order is
\[
\boxed{
\text{longitudinal carrier audit}
\;\to\;
V(0)=0
\;\to\;
\Delta>0
\;\to\;
\text{mass protection}
\;\to\;
M_Z\text{/FRG}.
}
\]

\section*{Longitudinal primitive-channel theorem: exact symmetry form and nonzero witness criterion}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the part of the longitudinal problem that \emph{can} be closed rigorously at the present stage:

\begin{enumerate}
\item identify the exact symmetry type of the longitudinal primitive channel;
\item prove that, once this channel survives with a nonzero microscopic coefficient, the reduced witness satisfies
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

This does \emph{not} yet prove that the full complete microscopic TECT linearization actually generates the channel.
It proves the sharp theorem-level statement:
\[
\text{if the longitudinal primitive carrier survives microscopically, then the longitudinal witness is automatically nonzero.}
\]

\subsection*{A. Residual singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition}

For the explicit local defect representative
\[
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
one has
\[
\partial_\xi z_B(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)e_1(\xi).
\]
Therefore the rank-two fiber splits as
\[
Q_B=\mathbb C e_1\oplus \mathbb C e_2,
\]
and the traceless Hermitian sector decomposes under the residual axial \(U(1)\) as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]
At the same time, the worldvolume momentum side decomposes as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\}.
\]
Hence both sides carry the same residual
\[
\text{singlet}\oplus\text{doublet}
\]
pattern:
\[
p_\parallel \leftrightarrow \sigma_3,
\qquad
(p_1,p_2)\leftrightarrow (\sigma_1,\sigma_2).
\]

\paragraph{Consequence.}
The longitudinal channel must transform as the singlet-to-singlet intertwiner.
Because both source and target singlet spaces are one-dimensional,
\[
\dim \mathrm{Hom}_{U(1)_{\mathrm{res}}}
\bigl(\mathbb R\,p_\parallel,\mathbb R\,\sigma_3\bigr)=1.
\]
Therefore the symmetry-allowed longitudinal primitive channel is unique up to an overall scalar coefficient.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Any symmetry-allowed primitive longitudinal transport channel is proportional to }n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:long_unique_singlet}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{B. Canonical geometric realization of the singlet channel}

Let
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Inside the explicit seed representative one has
\begin{equation}
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\label{eq:T2tr_long}
\end{equation}
Hence the canonical odd first-order longitudinal transport seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Vparallel_closed}
\end{equation}

This proves that the explicit primitive longitudinal seed is exactly the unique residual-singlet channel picked out by the defect geometry.

\subsection*{C. General microscopic longitudinal sector and projection criterion}

Let \(V_{\mathrm{mic}}\) be the true microscopic first-order transport space obtained from the full TECT linearization around the relevant defect background.

By the residual singlet/doublet decomposition, any microscopic transport field splits uniquely as
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
=
V^\mu_{\mathrm{sing}}(\xi)+V^\mu_{\mathrm{dbl}}(\xi),
\]
where
\[
V^\mu_{\mathrm{sing}}(\xi)\in
\mathrm{span}\{n^\mu\sigma_3\},
\qquad
V^\mu_{\mathrm{dbl}}(\xi)\in
\mathrm{span}\{E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\ J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\}.
\]

Because the longitudinal intertwiner space is one-dimensional, every admissible microscopic longitudinal primitive term has the form
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{long}}(\xi)
=
c_\parallel\,
\theta'(\xi)
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}(\xi),
\label{eq:Vlong_general}
\end{equation}
where \(V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}\) is any component orthogonal to the longitudinal target covector under the reduced projection.

Using \eqref{eq:T2tr_long},
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\mathrm{long}}(\xi)
=
\frac12 c_\parallel\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}(\xi).
\label{eq:Vlong_expanded}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{D. Reduced witness evaluation}

Inside the explicit seed space, the reduced witness coefficients are
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]
For the explicit longitudinal seed one has
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0.
\label{eq:Itheta3_nonzero_closed}
\end{equation}
Therefore, for the general microscopic longitudinal component \eqref{eq:Vlong_general},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_general_closed}
\end{equation}

Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), it follows immediately that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:long_nonzero_implication}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{E. Sharp theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Longitudinal primitive-channel theorem]
Consider the explicit CP\(^2\) defect representative with residual axial splitting
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}=\mathbb R\,p_\parallel\oplus\mathbb R^2_\perp,
\qquad
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}=\mathbb R\,\sigma_3\oplus\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the symmetry-allowed primitive longitudinal channel is unique up to an overall scalar and is represented by the singlet intertwiner
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3;
\]

\item geometrically, the canonical seed representative is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3;
\]

\item if the true microscopic TECT transport space contains this primitive channel with coefficient \(c_\parallel\neq 0\), then the reduced longitudinal witness is automatically nonzero:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Part (1) follows from the residual \(U(1)\) singlet/doublet decomposition and the one-dimensionality of the singlet intertwiner space.
Part (2) follows from the explicit identity
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]
Part (3) follows by substitution into the reduced witness formula together with
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
\end{proof}

\subsection*{F. Honest closure statement}

Thus the longitudinal frontier is no longer ambiguous.
It is reduced to exactly one finite microscopic coefficient test:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_{V_{\mathrm{mic}}}T^{(\parallel)}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:long_final_finite_test}
\end{equation}

What remains open is only the first implication:
\[
\text{does the complete microscopic TECT linearization actually produce }c_\parallel\neq 0\ ?
\]
The rest of the longitudinal witness chain is now closed.

\subsection{Summary}

\[
\boxed{
\textbf{Closed part of the longitudinal problem}
}
\]

Residual axial symmetry gives
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathbb R^2_\perp,
\qquad
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]

Hence the primitive longitudinal channel is the unique singlet-to-singlet intertwiner:
\[
\boxed{
\text{longitudinal primitive channel}\ \propto\ n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

In the explicit defect representative,
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
\]
so the canonical longitudinal seed is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\]

Its reduced witness is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

Therefore:
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

So the longitudinal frontier is reduced to one finite microscopic test:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete microscopic TECT transport space actually generate }c_\parallel\neq 0?
}
\]

Everything after that implication is now closed.

\section{Longitudinal Carrier Classification in the TECT Dirac Program}

\paragraph{Goal.}
The remaining carrier frontier is no longer the full witness problem.
The transverse carrier has already been fixed explicitly, while the only unresolved part is the microscopic survival of the primitive longitudinal channel:
\[
\lambda_\parallel \neq 0.
\]
Our task is therefore to classify which microscopic operator classes can, and which cannot, generate the required longitudinal carrier.

\paragraph{Target longitudinal structure.}
The shell-reduced local symbol has the form
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Hence the longitudinal sector requires a singlet-to-singlet carrier between
\[
p_\parallel
\quad\text{and}\quad
\sigma_3.
\]
In the explicit defect representative, the canonical primitive internal channel is
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\]
Therefore the actual longitudinal primitive seed must be of the form
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Its witness is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
So any microscopic class can close the longitudinal sector only if it can generate a nonzero coefficient
\[
c_\parallel
\]
in front of this primitive odd singlet channel.

\section{Necessary Structural Conditions}

\paragraph{Condition 1: an \((i,a)\)-carrier is mandatory.}
The shell-enriched target coupling has schematic form
\[
\delta L_{\mathrm{enr}}
=
N^a_{ij}(\partial_i\phi_0)(-i\partial_j)\otimes s^a.
\]
Therefore any UV/microscopic source able to induce the longitudinal witness must simultaneously carry:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item one internal shell-relevant label \(a\),
\item one derivative acting on the test/low sector,
\item one shell/background derivative factor.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, it must contain an \((i,a)\)-type carrier.

\paragraph{Condition 2: the longitudinal singlet must be odd.}
A naive singlet built only from
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\propto
\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3
\]
is insufficient.
Indeed, the corresponding overlap would be
\[
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
and because
\[
f_+ \text{ is even},\qquad
f_- \text{ is odd},\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^2 \text{ is even},
\]
the integrand is odd, hence
\[
\int d\xi\, f_+f_-\,\theta'^2 = 0.
\]
Therefore the longitudinal carrier must include one additional odd prefactor, giving precisely
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3.
\]

\section{Exclusion Theorem for Insufficient Classes}

\begin{theorem}[Structural exclusion of non-carriers]
The following microscopic correction types cannot generate the required longitudinal primitive witness:
\begin{enumerate}
\item pure scalar potential corrections,
\item pure projector derivative corrections,
\item amplitude-only derivative corrections,
\item the primitive projector channel \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\) by itself,
\item the naive even singlet channel proportional only to \(\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
We check each case.

\paragraph{(i) Pure scalar potentials.}
Terms such as
\[
(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)^3,\qquad
(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)(\partial_iP\partial_iP),\qquad
((\partial_iP\partial_iP))^2
\]
carry no shell-relevant internal tangent label \(a\), or produce no linear shell--projector mixing around the locked background.
Hence they do not generate an \((i,a)\)-carrier.

\paragraph{(ii) Pure projector derivative terms.}
Terms built only from \(P\) and its derivatives remain internal/projector-sector terms.
They do not couple linearly to the shell/test derivative sector, so they cannot induce the required first-order enriched mixed symbol.

\paragraph{(iii) Amplitude-only derivative terms.}
If a term depends only on \(\rho\) and its derivatives, it has no internal Pauli/triplet label and therefore cannot produce the traceless shell-relevant \(\sigma_3\) carrier.

\paragraph{(iv) Primitive projector tensor \(3P-\mathbf 1_3\).}
On the rank-two fiber \(Q_B\), this reduces to the identity and is therefore too coarse to generate the shell Pauli triplet.
In particular, by itself it does not isolate the required primitive longitudinal witness as a nontrivial traceless channel.

\paragraph{(v) Naive quadratic commutator singlet.}
The commutator-square channel gives
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]
But without an extra odd factor \(\theta'(\xi)\), its low-mode overlap vanishes by parity:
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]
So the naive even singlet does not contribute to \(\lambda_\parallel\).

Thus none of these classes can close the longitudinal carrier problem.
\end{proof}

\section{Admissible Microscopic Classes}

We now classify the three minimal viable local classes.

\subsection*{Class I: direct shell--projector derivative coupling}

A representative form is
\[
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(I)}
=
\Lambda^a_{ij}
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi\,
(T_a\partial_j P)
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\]
This class can work in principle because it explicitly inserts the needed \((i,a)\)-carrier tensor.
Hence Class I is \emph{admissible}.

However, it is less explanatory microscopically because the carrier tensor
\[
\Lambda^a_{ij}
\]
is inserted directly by hand rather than generated dynamically.

\subsection*{Class II: heavy auxiliary internal vector mediator}

Introduce an auxiliary mediator
\[
X_i^a
\]
carrying simultaneously a spatial index \(i\) and an internal index \(a\).
This is precisely the minimal type of field able to couple the shell-derivative structure to the internal tangent/projector sector and then, after elimination, induce the required first-order enriched tensor.

Inside the seed decomposition, Class II naturally splits into:
\[
X_i^3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal singlet seed},
\]
\[
X_i^1 \leftrightarrow \text{transverse-even seed},
\qquad
X_i^2 \leftrightarrow \text{transverse-odd seed}.
\]
Hence the explicit seed basis
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\}
\]
is exactly the local realization of the Class II carrier decomposition.

Therefore Class II is not merely allowed.
It is the minimal UV carrier structure matching the final reduced witness problem.

\subsection*{Class III: connection/gauge-like mediator}

A connection-like mediator \(A_i^a\) is also structurally plausible, since it carries the same index type \((i,a)\).
Therefore it is not excluded by symmetry.

However, in the present derivation chain it is less explicit than Class II.
So it remains a secondary candidate rather than the current closure route.

\section{Priority Theorem for the Longitudinal Carrier Problem}

\begin{theorem}[Current priority ordering]
For the present TECT longitudinal carrier problem, the viable microscopic classes are ordered by explanatory strength as
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II} \;>\; \text{Class I} \;>\; \text{Class III}.
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Class II generates the required \((i,a)\)-carrier dynamically through the auxiliary mediator and matches exactly the explicit shell-level seed decomposition.
Class I can also realize the carrier, but only by inserting the carrier tensor directly at the microscopic level.
Class III is structurally admissible but currently less explicit in the established derivation chain.

Therefore Class II is the strongest current candidate for closing the longitudinal carrier sector.
\end{proof}

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The longitudinal primitive witness problem is now reduced to the following finite microscopic yes/no test:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the true complete TECT microscopic transport space contain a nonzero Class II-type longitudinal seed?}
}
\]

More explicitly, it is sufficient to find
\[
N_\parallel\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\]
such that
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_\parallel\rangle\neq 0.
\]
Equivalently, one needs
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
Once this happens,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
because
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

Thus the current theorem-level closure is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{all insufficient carrier classes are excluded, and Class II is the minimal natural surviving candidate.}
}
\]

What remains open is not the reduced witness logic, but only the final microscopic realization question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does complete TECT actually realize this nontrivial Class II longitudinal sector?}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary of the Longitudinal Carrier Classification Step}

\paragraph{What is now closed.}
The longitudinal witness requires the primitive odd singlet channel
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
Therefore
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{What is excluded.}
The following cannot generate the required longitudinal carrier:
\[
\text{pure scalar corrections},
\quad
\text{pure projector corrections},
\quad
\text{amplitude-only derivative corrections},
\]
because they do not provide the required \((i,a)\)-carrier.
Also,
\[
3P-\mathbf 1_3
\]
is too coarse on \(Q_B\), and the naive even singlet
\[
\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3
\]
fails by parity:
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]

\paragraph{What remains viable.}
Among the minimal viable local microscopic classes:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II} \;>\; \text{Class I} \;>\; \text{Class III}.
}
\]
Class II is the minimal natural carrier because it dynamically realizes the same three seed directions:
\[
X_i^3 \leftrightarrow \text{longitudinal seed},
\qquad
X_i^1,X_i^2 \leftrightarrow \text{transverse seeds}.
\]

\paragraph{Exact current frontier.}
The remaining longitudinal question is reduced to one finite microscopic test:
\[
\boxed{
\exists\,N_\parallel\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\text{ such that }
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_\parallel\rangle\neq 0.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]
Once this is true, the longitudinal witness is automatically nonzero:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Honest status.}
So the current proof chain has established:
\[
\boxed{
\text{insufficient classes are excluded, and Class II is the minimal surviving longitudinal carrier candidate.}
}
\]
What is still open is only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{whether the complete microscopic TECT dynamics actually realizes that nonzero Class II longitudinal seed.}
}
\]

\section{Generic Nonvanishing of the Longitudinal Class II Carrier}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now prove the strongest honest statement that can be closed at this stage:
once the actual microscopic TECT transport space contains one admissible longitudinal Class II seed,
the longitudinal witness is generically nonzero.
This does \emph{not} yet prove that complete microscopic TECT realizes the Class II sector.
It proves that, \emph{if such a sector is realized}, then the surviving longitudinal coefficient is not a fine-tuned accident.

\section{Ambient Setup and the Longitudinal Functional}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{micro}}\subset W
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic transport tensor space extracted from the full TECT linearization around the relevant defect background.

Let
\[
T^{(\parallel)}\in W^*
\]
be the longitudinal witness covector. Define the longitudinal linear functional
\[
L_\parallel(N):=\langle T^{(\parallel)},N\rangle,
\qquad N\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}.
\]
By construction,
\[
L_\parallel(N)=0
\iff
\text{the reduced projection of }N\text{ has zero longitudinal component.}
\]

Inside the explicit shell-reduced seed basis,
\[
N
=
c_\parallel B_\parallel+c_I B_I+c_J B_J,
\]
one has
\[
L_\parallel(N)=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,
\]
and therefore
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

Hence the longitudinal problem is exactly the problem of whether
\[
L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}
\]
is identically zero or not.

\section{Seed Existence Implies Generic Nonvanishing}

\begin{theorem}[Longitudinal seed criterion]
Assume that the actual microscopic transport space \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) contains one admissible longitudinal seed
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\]
such that
\[
L_\parallel\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0.
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}\not\equiv 0\);
\item the bad set
\[
Z_\parallel
:=
\{N\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}:L_\parallel(N)=0\}
\]
is a proper hyperplane in \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\);
\item its complement
\[
U_\parallel
:=
V_{\mathrm{micro}}\setminus Z_\parallel
\]
is open, dense, and full measure;
\item therefore the longitudinal witness is generically nonzero:
\[
L_\parallel(N)\neq 0
\quad\text{for generic }N\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(L_\parallel\) is linear, its zero set is either the entire space or a hyperplane.
Because there exists \(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) with
\[
L_\parallel\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
the functional \(L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}\) is not identically zero.
Therefore its zero locus
\[
Z_\parallel=\ker\bigl(L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}\bigr)
\]
is a proper linear hyperplane in \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\).

A proper hyperplane is closed, has empty interior relative to \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\), and Lebesgue measure zero in any finite-dimensional affine coordinate system.
Hence its complement is open, dense, and full measure.
This proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Immediate corollary.}
Because
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\,c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
the same theorem implies:
\[
\boxed{
\text{if one admissible longitudinal seed exists, then }\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\text{ generically.}
}
\]

\section{Canonical Minimal Class II Basis}

Inside the canonical Class II parametrization, choose
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\]
together with
\[
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]
Then the induced shell-level coefficients satisfy
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]

In this basis, the witness functionals are diagonal:
\[
L_\parallel(N)=\mu_\parallel c_\parallel,
\qquad
L_I(N)=\mu_I c_I,
\qquad
L_J(N)=\mu_J c_J,
\]
with
\[
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad \mu_I\neq 0,\qquad \mu_J\neq 0.
\]
Therefore the exact longitudinal completion criterion is simply
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{One-Parameter Canonical Family}

For the smallest concrete Class II realization, define
\[
\mu:=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m.
\]
Then the induced shifts are
\[
\delta A=-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\mu c_J,
\]
and the effective coefficients are
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]
The shell Weyl determinant becomes
\[
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
\bigl(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2\bigr).
\]

Assume the full-support condition
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(A_{\mathrm{eff}}=0\) is one linear equation in \(\mu\), hence yields at most one isolated bad value;
\item \(B_{\mathrm{eff}}=0\) and \(C_{\mathrm{eff}}=0\) simultaneously is at worst a finite condition in \(\mu\), hence again gives at most finitely many isolated bad values.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the bad set in the one-parameter \(\mu\)-space is finite, and the good Weyl region is open, dense, and full measure.

\begin{theorem}[Canonical one-parameter genericity]
Assume
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0).
\]
Then in the canonical one-parameter Class II family, the set
\[
U_{\mathrm{Weyl}}
=
\{\mu:\,A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,\ (B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0)\}
\]
is the complement of at most finitely many isolated values of \(\mu\).
In particular, it is open, dense, and full measure in \(\mu\)-space.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Directly from the affine formulas for \(A_{\mathrm{eff}},B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}}\).
The equation \(A_{\mathrm{eff}}=0\) has at most one solution.
The simultaneous vanishing of \((B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\) gives at most finitely many isolated solutions in one real parameter.
Hence the bad set is finite.
\end{proof}

\section{Purely Induced Regime}

A particularly important special case is
\[
A_0=B_0=C_0=0.
\]
Then
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\mu c_J.
\]
Therefore, if
\[
\mu\neq 0,
\qquad
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
one immediately gets
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0),
\qquad
\det M\neq 0.
\]

So in the purely induced regime, once the three Class II seed directions are present, any nonzero \(\mu\) already gives a Weyl-good local symbol.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We have now closed the following theorem-level statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{If the actual microscopic TECT transport space contains one admissible longitudinal Class II seed,}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{then the longitudinal witness is generically nonzero, and its bad set is a proper hyperplane.}
}
\end{equation}

Moreover, in the canonical one-parameter Class II family:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the bad parameter set is at most finite.}
}
\end{equation}

What remains open is only the embedding question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does complete microscopic TECT actually realize this Class II longitudinal seed in the physical defect background?}
}
\]
That is the only place where the present proof chain is still conditional.

\section{Final Summary of the Generic Longitudinal Class II Step}

\paragraph{What is now rigorously closed.}
Let
\[
L_\parallel(N)=\langle T^{(\parallel)},N\rangle
\]
be the longitudinal witness functional on the actual microscopic transport space
\[
V_{\mathrm{micro}}.
\]
If there exists one admissible longitudinal seed
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\]
such that
\[
L_\parallel\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\bigr)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{micro}}}\not\equiv 0.
\]
Hence the bad set
\[
Z_\parallel=\{N\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}:L_\parallel(N)=0\}
\]
is a proper hyperplane, and therefore its complement is open, dense, and full measure.

\paragraph{Equivalent witness statement.}
Since
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\]
this is equivalent to:
\[
\boxed{
\text{one admissible longitudinal seed } \Longrightarrow \lambda_\parallel\neq 0 \text{ generically.}
}

\paragraph{Canonical Class II basis.}
In the canonical Class II coordinates,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J,
\]
so the exact longitudinal condition is simply
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0.

\paragraph{One-parameter canonical family.}
For the smallest Class II realization with
\[
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m,
\]
the effective coefficients are
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J.
\]
Thus, under
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
the bad set in \(\mu\)-space is at most finite.
Hence the Weyl-good set is open, dense, and full measure.

\paragraph{Honest current frontier.}
So the proof chain has now reduced the longitudinal issue to a single finite embedding question:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Does complete microscopic TECT actually contain one admissible longitudinal Class II seed?}
}

Everything after that implication is now closed.

\section{Why the Longitudinal Seed $B_\parallel$ Is Not Symmetry-Forbidden}

\paragraph{Goal.}
The next rigorous step is to separate two logically distinct statements:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(A) }B_\parallel\text{ is not forbidden by the residual shell symmetry;}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(B) the actual complete microscopic TECT space }V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\text{ really contains }B_\parallel.
}
\end{equation}

At the present stage, statement (A) can be proved.
Statement (B) still requires the finite microscopic carrier audit.

\section{Residual Symmetry and the Unique Longitudinal Intertwiner}

Let the shell direction be
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and choose an orthonormal frame
\[
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Under the residual shell symmetry
\[
H_{\mathrm{sh}}\cong SO(2)_\perp,
\]
the worldvolume momentum sector decomposes as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{wv}}
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\},
\]
while the traceless internal fiber sector decomposes as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]
Thus both sides carry the same
\[
\text{singlet}\oplus\text{doublet}
\]
splitting. The most general local symmetry-compatible reduced symbol is therefore
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
This is exactly the natural local \(S^2\)-branch symbol. In particular, the longitudinal channel is the singlet-to-singlet intertwiner
\[
p_\parallel \longleftrightarrow \sigma_3,
\]
and this intertwiner is one-dimensional. Therefore the longitudinal primitive tensor is unique up to scale.

Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the residual symmetry does not eliminate the longitudinal channel;}
}
\]
it selects it uniquely.

\section{Minimal Allowed Tensor Space and Explicit Non-Forbiddance}

Inside the minimal shell-enriched projector ansatz, the allowed shell-relevant tensor space is exactly
\[
V_{\min}
=
\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}.
\]
Equivalently, in component form the explicit invariant basis is
\[
N^3_{ij}=g_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
\[
N^1_{ij}=g_I \hat n_i e_{1j}-g_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
\[
N^2_{ij}=g_I \hat n_i e_{2j}+g_J \hat n_i e_{1j}.
\]
The associated exact witness functionals satisfy
\[
W_\parallel[N]=g_\parallel,\qquad
W_I[N]=g_I,\qquad
W_J[N]=g_J.
\]

Therefore, at the level of the minimal shell-allowed symmetry class,
\[
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,\qquad
P_VT^{(I)}\neq 0,\qquad
P_VT^{(J)}\neq 0.
}
\]
So none of the three reduced shell channels is symmetry-forbidden.

In particular,
\[
\boxed{
B_\parallel\text{ is an allowed invariant tensor direction.}
}
\]

\section{Exact Dichotomy: Forbidden vs. Generically Nonvanishing}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic transport space extracted from the complete TECT linearization around the chosen defect background.

For the longitudinal channel define the target covector
\[
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}=e_{\parallel i}G_{*j}u^{(\parallel)}_a,
\]
and the linear witness functional
\[
L_\parallel(N):=\langle T^{(\parallel)},N\rangle.
\]
Then the exact finite-dimensional dichotomy is
\[
L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_VT^{(\parallel)}=0.
\]
Hence exactly one of the following holds:

\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}=0,
\]
so the longitudinal channel is symmetry-forbidden in the actual microscopic space;

\item
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\]
so the longitudinal channel is generically nonvanishing on an open dense full-measure subset of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the real remaining question is finite:
\[
\text{compute }P_VT^{(\parallel)}\text{ or find one admissible seed with nonzero overlap.}
\]

\section{Minimal Sufficient Condition for Actual Survival}

A practical sufficient condition is the existence of one explicit admissible microscopic tensor
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
such that
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\rangle\neq 0.
\]
Then automatically
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\]
hence the channel survives generically.

Inside the minimal Class II parametrization, the canonical longitudinal seed is represented by
\[
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\]
which gives
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel.
\]
Therefore, once such a seed belongs to the actual microscopic space,
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
g_c\neq 0
\]
and hence the longitudinal witness survives generically.

\section{Why Vanishing Would Require More Than Residual Symmetry}

The above proves that residual shell symmetry alone does not force
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}=0.
\]
So if the longitudinal channel vanishes in the actual microscopic realization, the reason cannot be the basic
\[
SO(2)_\perp
\]
residual shell symmetry by itself.

Instead, vanishing would require at least one of the following:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional microscopic symmetry not contained in the minimal shell residual symmetry;
\item a dynamical cancellation among the actual basis tensors of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\);
\item the absence of any genuine \((i,a)\)-carrier sector in the full microscopic linearization.
\end{enumerate}

This is structurally analogous to the mirror-lifting scalar-overlap problem, where the established stabilizer symmetry by itself does not force vanishing, and any vanishing requires extra dynamical or involutive cancellation structure.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We can now state the strongest honest theorem of this step:

\begin{theorem}[Non-forbiddance of the longitudinal shell channel]
At the shell-reduced symmetry level, the longitudinal channel \(B_\parallel\) is not symmetry-forbidden.
More precisely, in the minimal shell-allowed tensor space
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
one has
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0.
\]
Therefore residual shell symmetry selects \(B_\parallel\) as the unique singlet longitudinal intertwiner rather than excluding it.
\end{theorem}

\begin{corollary}
If the actual complete microscopic TECT transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) contains one admissible longitudinal seed with nonzero overlap against \(T^{(\parallel)}\), then the longitudinal witness is generically nonzero.
\end{corollary}

\paragraph{What remains open.}
What is still not automatic is the actual embedding statement
\[
B_\parallel\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\quad\text{or at least}\quad
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0
\]
for the full complete microscopic TECT linearization.
That remains a finite overlap / basis audit.

\section{Final Summary of the Non-Forbiddance Step}

\paragraph{What is now closed.}
At the shell-reduced symmetry level, the residual symmetry
\[
H_{\mathrm{sh}}\cong SO(2)_\perp
\]
does not forbid the longitudinal channel.
Instead, it selects a unique singlet-to-singlet intertwiner
\[
p_\parallel \longleftrightarrow \sigma_3.
\]

In the minimal shell-allowed tensor space,
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
all three channels survive:
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,\qquad
P_VT^{(I)}\neq 0,\qquad
P_VT^{(J)}\neq 0.
\]
Hence
\[
\boxed{
B_\parallel \text{ is not symmetry-forbidden.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Exact logical meaning.}
For the actual complete microscopic TECT transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\),
\[
L_\parallel|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\iff
P_VT^{(\parallel)}=0.
\]
So the real remaining question is finite-dimensional:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }P_VT^{(\parallel)}\text{ or exhibit one admissible seed with nonzero overlap.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Minimal sufficient condition for actual survival.}
If there exists
\[
N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
such that
\[
\langle T^{(\parallel)},N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\parallel)}\rangle\neq 0,
\]
then automatically
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0,
\]
so the longitudinal witness is generically nonzero.

\paragraph{Honest current frontier.}
Thus the present proof chain has established:
\[
\boxed{
\text{non-forbiddance is closed,}
}
\]
but still leaves open:
\[
\boxed{
\text{actual embedding of the longitudinal Class II seed into the complete microscopic TECT space.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
Therefore any failure of the longitudinal channel would have to come from
\[
\text{additional microscopic symmetry,}
\quad
\text{or dynamical cancellation,}
\quad
\text{or absence of a genuine }(i,a)\text{-carrier sector,}
\]
not from the basic residual shell symmetry itself.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Finite Basis-Level Audit Theorem for the Actual Microscopic TECT Space}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now reduce the remaining microscopic carrier problem to an explicitly computable finite-dimensional basis audit.
The objective is not yet to prove that the complete TECT linearization already contains the required seed space.
Rather, we prove that once a basis of the actual microscopic transport space is chosen, the carrier audit becomes a finite overlap test.

\section{Ambient Finite-Dimensional Formulation}

Let
\[
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the ambient shell-enriched tensor space, and let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual symmetry-allowed microscopic transport tensor space obtained by linearizing the complete TECT dynamics around the chosen defect/BCC background.

Fix shell data
\[
G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal}.
\]
For the three required reduced channels define the shell target covectors
\[
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}=e_{\parallel i}G_{*j}u^{(\parallel)}_a,
\qquad
T^{(I)}_{ija}=e_{1i}G_{*j}u^{(1)}_a+e_{2i}G_{*j}u^{(2)}_a,
\qquad
T^{(J)}_{ija}=e_{2i}G_{*j}u^{(1)}_a-e_{1i}G_{*j}u^{(2)}_a,
\]
and the corresponding linear witness functionals
\[
L_\alpha(N):=\langle T^{(\alpha)},N\rangle,
\qquad
\alpha\in\{\parallel,I,J\}.
\]

Then the exact carrier criterion is
\[
L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0,
\]
where \(P_V:W\to V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) is the orthogonal projector.
Equivalently,
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\]
means that the actual microscopic TECT linearization contains a shell-relevant nontrivial carrier direction in channel \(\alpha\).

\section{Basis-Level Operational Audit}

Choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^{d}
\]
of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), where \(d=\dim V_{\mathrm{TECT}}<\infty\).
Write
\[
N=\sum_{A=1}^{d}x_AE_A.
\]
Then
\[
L_\alpha(N)=\sum_{A=1}^{d}x_A\,\ell_{\alpha A},
\qquad
\ell_{\alpha A}:=\langle T^{(\alpha)},E_A\rangle.
\]

Hence the entire carrier audit becomes the computation of the three overlap vectors
\[
\ell_\parallel=(\ell_{\parallel 1},\dots,\ell_{\parallel d}),
\qquad
\ell_I=(\ell_{I1},\dots,\ell_{Id}),
\qquad
\ell_J=(\ell_{J1},\dots,\ell_{Jd}).
\]

The exact dichotomy is:

\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\ell_{\alpha A}=0\ \text{ for all }A,
\]
and
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A\ \text{ such that }\ell_{\alpha A}\neq 0.
\]

Therefore the surviving-carrier problem is finite and explicit.

\section{Shell-Adapted Decomposition of Basis Elements}

Let
\[
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
be the minimal shell-adapted witness subspace.
Each basis element \(E_A\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\) can be decomposed as
\[
E_A
=
a_A B_\parallel
+
b_A B_I
+
c_A B_J
+
R_A,
\]
where
\[
R_A\perp V_{\min}.
\]

Because the witness functionals are linear and vanish on the orthogonal complement \(R_A\), we get
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\]
\[
\ell_{IA}=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle=\mu_I b_A,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle=\mu_J c_A,
\]
with nonzero constants
\[
\mu_\parallel\neq 0,\qquad \mu_I\neq 0,\qquad \mu_J\neq 0
\]
in the shell-adapted normalization.

Hence:

\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
a_A\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
(\ell_{IA},\ell_{JA})\neq (0,0)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0).
\]

So the actual microscopic test becomes:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:basis_audit_condition}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact Basis-Level Completion Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Basis-level carrier-audit theorem]
Let \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W\) be the actual microscopic transport space and let \(\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d\) be any basis.
For each basis element define the overlap coefficients
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\]
Then the microscopic carrier audit succeeds if and only if:

\begin{enumerate}
\item there exists at least one basis element \(E_A\) with
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0;
\]

\item there exists at least one basis element \(E_B\) with
\[
(\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the carrier audit succeeds if and only if
\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\bigl(P_VT^{(I)},P_VT^{(J)}\bigr)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the basis expansion,
\[
L_\alpha(N)=\sum_A x_A\ell_{\alpha A}.
\]
Thus \(L_\alpha|_{V_{\mathrm{TECT}}}\equiv 0\) if and only if every coefficient \(\ell_{\alpha A}\) vanishes.
Therefore
\[
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0
\]
is equivalent to the existence of at least one basis vector with nonzero overlap in channel \(\alpha\).

For the full Weyl/Dirac witness problem, the longitudinal channel and at least one transverse channel must survive.
So the stated two conditions are necessary and sufficient.
\end{proof}

\section{Immediate Reduced Dirac Consequence}

Once the basis-level carrier audit succeeds, the shell-reduced witness coefficients satisfy
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\]
with
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
Therefore the reduced symbol is nondegenerate exactly when
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
\]

Equivalently, in the shell tensor form
\[
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
the local Weyl condition is
\[
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
\]
So after the basis audit, the PDE problem is completely reduced to a finite coefficient check.

\section{Practical Audit Algorithm}

A concrete operational version is as follows.

\paragraph{Step 1.}
Linearize the complete microscopic TECT equation around the chosen defect/BCC background and extract the first-order transport kernel
\[
L_1=-iV^\mu(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

\paragraph{Step 2.}
Choose a basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
for the resulting finite-dimensional symmetry-allowed transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).

\paragraph{Step 3.}
For each basis element, compute the overlaps
\[
\ell_{\parallel A},\qquad \ell_{IA},\qquad \ell_{JA}.
\]

\paragraph{Step 4.}
If there exists at least one \(A\) with
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\]
then the longitudinal carrier survives generically.

\paragraph{Step 5.}
If there exists at least one \(B\) with
\[
(\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0),
\]
then the transverse carrier survives generically.

\paragraph{Step 6.}
If both checks pass, then the local Weyl witness audit is complete.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We have now reduced the remaining microscopic problem to the finite-dimensional statement:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\]
This is the exact basis-level completion criterion.

Thus the strongest honest status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual microscopic carrier problem is no longer an uncontrolled PDE problem;}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is a finite basis-overlap audit on }V_{\mathrm{TECT}}.
}
\]

What remains open is the execution of this audit for the final complete microscopic TECT linearization.

\section{Final Summary of the Basis-Level Carrier Audit Step}

\paragraph{What is now closed.}
Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual microscopic transport space and choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^{d}.
\]
For the shell target covectors \(T^{(\parallel)},T^{(I)},T^{(J)}\), define
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle.
\]

Then:

\[
P_VT^{(\parallel)}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
\bigl(P_VT^{(I)},P_VT^{(J)}\bigr)\neq (0,0)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
\]

Therefore the exact basis-level completion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (\ell_{IB},\ell_{JB})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

\paragraph{Equivalent shell-adapted statement.}
If
\[
E_A=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp \mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
then
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\mu_I b_A,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\mu_J c_A,
\]
with
\[
\mu_\parallel,\mu_I,\mu_J\neq 0.
\]
So the audit is equivalent to
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

\paragraph{Dirac consequence.}
Once this basis audit succeeds, the reduced witness coefficients satisfy
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\]
hence the local Weyl condition becomes
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
Equivalently, in shell tensor form,
\[
\boxed{
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

\paragraph{Honest status.}
So the remaining microscopic frontier is no longer conceptual:
\[
\boxed{
\text{it is the explicit execution of a finite basis-overlap audit for the final complete TECT linearization.}
}
\]


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Residual Axial Representation Decomposition of Actual Microscopic Basis Elements}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now turn the carrier audit into a canonical representation-theoretic decomposition.
The aim is to prove that every shell-projected microscopic first-order basis element admits a unique invariant decomposition into one longitudinal singlet coefficient and one transverse doublet pair:
\[
E_A \longmapsto (a_A,b_A,c_A).
\]
This is the exact structural step needed before the final explicit microscopic overlap audit.

\section{Residual Axial Symmetry and the Invariant Coupling Space}

Let the selected shell direction be
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and choose an orthonormal frame
\[
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Under the residual axial symmetry \(H_\perp\) (the connected \(SO(2)_\perp\) piece, or equivalently the \(O(2)_\perp\) invariant classification), the worldvolume momentum sector decomposes as
\[
V_p
=
\mathbb R\,p_\parallel \oplus E_\perp,
\qquad
E_\perp=\mathrm{span}\{p_1,p_2\},
\]
while the shell-relevant traceless internal sector decomposes as
\[
V_{\mathrm{int}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3 \oplus \Sigma_\perp,
\qquad
\Sigma_\perp=\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]

Thus both source and target carry the same
\[
1 \oplus 2
\]
decomposition.

Define the invariant first-order shell coupling space
\[
\mathrm{Inv}
:=
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\perp}(V_p,V_{\mathrm{int}}).
\]

\begin{theorem}[Dimension and canonical basis of the invariant space]
The invariant coupling space is exactly three-dimensional:
\[
\dim \mathrm{Inv}=3.
\]
A canonical basis is given by
\[
B_\parallel:\quad p_\parallel \mapsto \sigma_3,
\]
\[
B_I:\quad (p_1,p_2)\mapsto (\sigma_1,\sigma_2),
\]
\[
B_J:\quad (p_1,p_2)\mapsto (-\sigma_2,\sigma_1).
\]
Equivalently, the most general symmetry-compatible reduced symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
a\,p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
b\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
c\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Because
\[
V_p \cong 1 \oplus 2,
\qquad
V_{\mathrm{int}} \cong 1 \oplus 2,
\]
one has
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\perp}(V_p,V_{\mathrm{int}})
\cong
\mathrm{Hom}(1,1)\oplus \mathrm{Hom}(2,2),
\]
since the mixed blocks
\[
\mathrm{Hom}(1,2),\qquad \mathrm{Hom}(2,1)
\]
vanish by inequivalence of irreducible sectors.

Now
\[
\dim \mathrm{Hom}(1,1)=1.
\]
For the real transverse doublet representation,
\[
\mathrm{End}_{H_\perp}(2)=\mathrm{span}\{\mathbf 1_2,J\},
\]
where \(J\) is the planar complex structure
\[
J(p_1,p_2)=(-p_2,p_1).
\]
Hence
\[
\dim \mathrm{Hom}(2,2)=2.
\]
Therefore
\[
\dim \mathrm{Inv}=1+2=3,
\]
and the stated basis follows.
\end{proof}

\section{Projection of Actual Microscopic Basis Elements onto the Invariant Sector}

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset W
\]
be the actual microscopic first-order transport space produced by the complete TECT linearization, and choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d.
\]

Not every \(E_A\) is itself already written in shell-adapted invariant form.
However, only its invariant shell-reduced component contributes to the reduced Weyl witness problem.
Therefore define the invariant projection
\[
P_{\mathrm{inv}}:W\to \mathrm{Inv}.
\]
For each basis element, set
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}:=P_{\mathrm{inv}}E_A.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Unique shell-adapted decomposition]
For every microscopic basis element \(E_A\), there exists a unique triple
\[
(a_A,b_A,c_A)\in \mathbb R^3
\]
such that
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the previous theorem,
\[
\mathrm{Inv}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}
\]
is a three-dimensional vector space with the displayed basis.
Therefore every element of \(\mathrm{Inv}\), and in particular \(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}\), admits a unique expansion in that basis.
\end{proof}

So the actual microscopic carrier audit is reduced to the coefficient map
\[
E_A \longmapsto (a_A,b_A,c_A).
\]

\section{Dual Witness Extraction of the Coefficients}

Let
\[
W_\parallel,\qquad W_I,\qquad W_J
\]
be the dual witness functionals normalized by
\[
W_\parallel(B_\parallel)=1,\qquad W_\parallel(B_I)=W_\parallel(B_J)=0,
\]
\[
W_I(B_I)=1,\qquad W_I(B_\parallel)=W_I(B_J)=0,
\]
\[
W_J(B_J)=1,\qquad W_J(B_\parallel)=W_J(B_I)=0.
\]

Then for
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J,
\]
one gets immediately
\[
a_A=W_\parallel(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}),
\qquad
b_A=W_I(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}),
\qquad
c_A=W_J(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}).
\]

Equivalently, in shell target-covector form,
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}:=\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}:=\langle T^{(I)},E_A\rangle,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}:=\langle T^{(J)},E_A\rangle,
\]
there exist fixed nonzero normalization constants
\[
\mu_\parallel,\mu_I,\mu_J\neq 0
\]
such that
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\mu_\parallel a_A,
\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\mu_I b_A,
\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\mu_J c_A.
\]

Hence:
\[
a_A\neq 0
\iff
\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
(b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0)
\iff
(\ell_{IA},\ell_{JA})\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{Representation-Theoretic Audit Criterion}

We may now state the exact executable criterion.

\begin{theorem}[Representation decomposition audit theorem]
Let \(\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d\) be any basis of the actual microscopic TECT transport space \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
For each \(A\), let
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J
\]
be its unique invariant shell-reduced decomposition.
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal carrier survives if and only if
\[
\exists A \text{ such that } a_A\neq 0;
\]

\item the transverse carrier survives if and only if
\[
\exists A \text{ such that } (b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the full local Weyl witness audit succeeds if and only if
\[
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This follows immediately from the dual-witness extraction formulas above.
If all \(a_A=0\), then every invariant basis component lacks the longitudinal singlet and thus
\[
W_\parallel(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}})=0
\quad\forall A,
\]
so the longitudinal witness vanishes identically on \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Conversely, if at least one \(a_A\neq 0\), then the longitudinal witness is not identically zero.

The transverse statement is identical, using \((b_A,c_A)\) and the two transverse dual witnesses.
\end{proof}

\section{Relation to the Reduced Dirac Conditions}

Inside the shell-adapted reduced witness space, the exact nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
With the seed parametrization,
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\]
where
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0,
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
\]
Thus, once the basis-level representation audit finds
\[
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0),
\]
the reduced Weyl symbol is nondegenerate generically.

So the remaining microscopic problem is no longer abstract:
it is exactly the computation of the invariant coordinates
\[
(a_A,b_A,c_A)
\]
for the actual complete TECT basis elements.

\section{Sharp Honest Status}

What has been closed here is the representation-theoretic reduction:
\[
\boxed{
E_A \mapsto (a_A,b_A,c_A)
\text{ is a canonical and unique shell-reduced decomposition.}
}
\]

What remains open is only the final execution:
\[
\boxed{
\text{for the actual complete TECT basis, exhibit at least one }A\text{ with }a_A\neq 0
\text{ and at least one }B\text{ with }(b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
That is the last microscopic carrier audit in executable finite-dimensional form.

%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the Representation Decomposition Step}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
Under the residual axial shell symmetry, both the worldvolume momentum sector and the shell-relevant internal sector decompose as
\[
1\oplus 2.
\]
Hence the invariant first-order shell-coupling space is
\[
\mathrm{Inv}=\mathrm{Hom}_{H_\perp}(V_p,V_{\mathrm{int}}),
\qquad
\dim \mathrm{Inv}=3.
\]
A canonical basis is
\[
B_\parallel,\qquad B_I,\qquad B_J.
\]

\paragraph{Canonical decomposition of actual basis elements.}
For every actual microscopic basis element \(E_A\in V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), its invariant shell-reduced part satisfies
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=P_{\mathrm{inv}}E_A
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J,
\]
with a unique coefficient triple
\[
(a_A,b_A,c_A)\in\mathbb R^3.
\]

\paragraph{Exact extraction.}
The dual witnesses recover these coefficients exactly:
\[
a_A=W_\parallel(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}),\qquad
b_A=W_I(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}),\qquad
c_A=W_J(E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}).
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=\mu_\parallel a_A,\qquad
\ell_{IA}=\mu_I b_A,\qquad
\ell_{JA}=\mu_J c_A,
\]
with
\[
\mu_\parallel,\mu_I,\mu_J\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Executable carrier criterion.}
Therefore the actual microscopic audit succeeds if and only if
\[
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
\]

\paragraph{Dirac consequence.}
Once these two conditions hold, the reduced shell witness satisfies
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\]
hence the local shell-reduced Weyl symbol is nondegenerate generically.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
So the remaining microscopic problem is no longer conceptual.
It is exactly this finite audit:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }(a_A,b_A,c_A)\text{ for the actual complete TECT basis elements.}
}
\]



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Class-by-Class Coefficient Audit Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now classify the symmetry-allowed microscopic operator classes by the invariant coefficient pattern they can contribute to the shell-reduced basis
\[
\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}.
\]
For each microscopic basis element \(E_A\), recall the unique invariant decomposition
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}
=
a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J.
\]
The purpose of this section is to determine, class by class, which of the three coordinates
\[
a_A,\qquad b_A,\qquad c_A
\]
must vanish identically, and which may survive.

\section{Reference Invariant Basis and Witness Dictionary}

The shell-reduced invariant first-order operator space is
\[
\mathrm{Inv}
=
\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\},
\]
with canonical basis
\[
B_\parallel:\quad p_\parallel \sigma_3,
\]
\[
B_I:\quad p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2,
\]
\[
B_J:\quad -p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2.
\]
Equivalently, in tensor form,
\[
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
and the shell witnesses read
\[
\lambda_\parallel\propto A,
\qquad
\alpha\propto B,
\qquad
\beta\propto C.
\]

Thus the coefficient audit is exactly the problem of deciding, for each microscopic class, whether it can produce:
\[
a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
(b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{Excluded Classes: No \((i,a)\)-Carrier}

\begin{theorem}[Type 0 exclusion theorem]
Suppose \(E_A\) belongs to one of the following classes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Type 0A: pure scalar potential corrections;
\item Type 0B: pure projector derivative corrections;
\item Type 0C: amplitude-only derivative corrections.
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=0,
\qquad\text{hence}\qquad
(a_A,b_A,c_A)=(0,0,0).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Any shell-relevant first-order enriched tensor must carry simultaneously:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one spatial derivative index \(i\) or \(j\),
\item one internal reduced-shell/tangent index \(a\),
\item one derivative acting on the test mode sector,
\item one shell/background derivative factor.
\end{enumerate}

Pure scalar potentials are polarization-blind or start only at quadratic order in the tangent fluctuation.
Pure projector derivative terms remain internal/projector-sector terms and do not produce a linear shell--test mixed source.
Amplitude-only derivative terms contain no internal Pauli/tangent label \(a\).

Therefore none of these classes can contribute to the first-order shell-enriched mixed tensor, so their projection to \(\mathrm{Inv}\) vanishes identically.
\end{proof}

\section{Even Singlet No-Go}

\begin{theorem}[Naive even singlet no-go]
Consider the naive longitudinal singlet source
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{naive}}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Then its projected longitudinal witness vanishes:
\[
a_A=0.
\]
More precisely, its mixed low-mode overlap is zero by parity.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For a reflection-symmetric defect,
\[
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\qquad
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi),
\]
so \(\theta'(\xi)^2\) is even.
The relevant mixed overlap is proportional to
\[
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
where \(f_+\) is even and \(f_-\) is odd.
Hence the integrand is odd, so the integral vanishes:
\[
\int d\xi\, f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]
Therefore the naive even singlet does not contribute to the first-order mixed symbol, and thus gives no longitudinal coefficient.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Consequence.}
A longitudinal singlet source must carry one additional odd prefactor.
So the minimal viable longitudinal class is not \(\theta'^2\sigma_3\), but an odd-upgraded primitive channel.

\section{Pure Transverse Doublet Class}

\begin{theorem}[Pure transverse class]
Consider the canonical transverse doublet source
\[
V^\mu_{\perp}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr],
\qquad a=1,2.
\]
Then its invariant coefficient pattern is
\[
a_A=0,
\qquad
(b_A,c_A)\propto (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]
In particular, this class can generate the transverse channels \(B_I,B_J\), but not the longitudinal singlet \(B_\parallel\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The source takes values only in the transverse doublet sector \((\sigma_1,\sigma_2)\), and its worldvolume factor is likewise purely transverse.
Therefore it transforms in the doublet-to-doublet intertwiner sector \(\mathrm{Hom}(2,2)\), not in the singlet-to-singlet sector \(\mathrm{Hom}(1,1)\).

Hence no \(B_\parallel\) component is present, while the two transverse invariant coordinates are exactly the even/odd coefficients \(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\), up to fixed normalization.
\end{proof}

\section{Primitive Longitudinal Odd Singlet Class}

Let
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
Write its Pauli decomposition as
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Primitive longitudinal class]
Consider the odd-upgraded primitive transport kernel
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if \(s_3(\xi)\equiv 0\), then \(a_A=0\);
\item if \(s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0\) and the projected overlap
\[
J_\parallel
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)
\]
is nonzero, then
\[
a_A\neq 0;
\]
\item in the pure longitudinal adapted frame, if \(S_\xi\propto \sigma_3\), then
\[
b_A=c_A=0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first statement is immediate: the longitudinal witness probes the \(\sigma_3\)-singlet component.
If \(s_3\equiv 0\), there is no singlet projection.

For the second statement, \(\theta'(\xi)\) is odd and \(S_\xi\) is even when built from quadratic response data.
Hence the transport kernel is odd, exactly as required to couple even and odd low modes.
If the scalar overlap \(J_\parallel\) is nonzero, then the projected longitudinal coefficient is nonzero.

The third statement follows because in the adapted singlet frame the primitive class lies entirely in the \(\sigma_3\)-sector and therefore has no transverse doublet projection.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Explicit seed representative.}
In the explicit representative,
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\]
so
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and
\[
a_A\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
This is the canonical longitudinal seed.

\section{Class I, II, III: Admissible \((i,a)\)-Carrier Classes}

\begin{theorem}[Admissible carrier classes]
At lowest derivative order, the minimal viable local microscopic classes are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Class I: direct shell--projector derivative couplings;
\item Class II: heavy auxiliary internal vector mediators \(X_i^a\);
\item Class III: connection-like mediators \(A_i^a\).
\end{enumerate}

Each is symmetry-admissible because each introduces an effective \((i,a)\)-carrier.
However, their audit status differs.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Any microscopic class capable of generating the reduced shell tensor must introduce an object carrying both a spatial derivative index and an internal tangent index.
Classes I, II, III all satisfy this structural requirement, so none is excluded by symmetry.

Their difference is not admissibility but explicitness:
Class I inserts the carrier tensor directly by hand,
Class II generates it dynamically through mediator elimination,
and Class III is structurally plausible but less explicit in the present derivation chain.
\end{proof}

\section{Class II as the Fully Explicit Three-Coordinate Class}

\begin{theorem}[Class II coordinate theorem]
In the Class II interpretation, the three mediator directions correspond exactly to the three shell-reduced invariant coordinates:
\[
X_i^3 \leftrightarrow B_\parallel,
\qquad
X_i^1 \leftrightarrow B_I,
\qquad
X_i^2 \leftrightarrow B_J.
\]
Equivalently, in the explicit seed basis
\[
V_{\mathrm{seed}}
=
\mathrm{span}\{
N^{(\parallel)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}}
\},
\]
one has
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
\]
Thus Class II is the unique currently explicit microscopic class that realizes all three coefficient directions \((a,b,c)\) at once.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The longitudinal seed is represented by the \(X_i^3\)-channel, while the transverse even/odd seeds are represented by the \(X_i^1\)- and \(X_i^2\)-channels respectively.
After projection to the reduced defect/shell sector, these induce the three independent coefficients \(g_c,g_E,g_O\), which are exactly the shell witness coordinates.
Therefore the Class II mediator decomposition is isomorphic to the invariant basis decomposition.
\end{proof}

\section{Class-by-Class Audit Table}

The result of the classification can be summarized as follows.

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Microscopic class} & \text{Possible invariant coordinates} & \text{Audit status}\\
\hline
\text{Type 0A / 0B / 0C} & (0,0,0) & \text{excluded}\\
\text{Naive even singlet } \theta'^2\sigma_3 & a=0 & \text{excluded by parity}\\
\text{Pure transverse doublet} & a=0,\ (b,c)\neq (0,0)\text{ possible} & \text{explicitly allowed}\\
\text{Primitive odd longitudinal singlet} & a\neq 0\text{ possible},\ b=c=0 & \text{minimal longitudinal mechanism}\\
\text{Class I} & a,b,c\text{ all possible in principle} & \text{admissible, less explicit}\\
\text{Class II} & a,b,c\text{ explicitly realizable} & \text{strongest current class}\\
\text{Class III} & a,b,c\text{ possible in principle} & \text{plausible, less explicit}
\end{array}
\]

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The final coefficient audit problem is now sharply reduced.

\begin{enumerate}
\item Pure scalar/projector/amplitude classes are removed completely.
\item A naive even singlet is removed by parity.
\item The transverse doublet class is already explicitly realized.
\item The longitudinal primitive odd singlet is the minimal surviving longitudinal mechanism.
\item Class II is the only currently explicit microscopic class that packages all three invariant coordinates in one unified carrier structure.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the remaining microscopic frontier is no longer broad.
It is the explicit yes/no audit:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Does the complete TECT linearization realize at least one nonzero primitive longitudinal seed,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{together with the already available transverse seed, inside the actual microscopic transport space?}
}
\]

Equivalently, the final executable target is:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
