\section{Final Summary of the Class-by-Class Coefficient Audit}

\paragraph{Closed classification.}
For each actual microscopic basis element \(E_A\), its invariant shell-reduced part
\[
E_A^{\mathrm{inv}}=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J
\]
falls into one of the following coefficient patterns:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
\text{Class} & \text{Coefficient pattern}\\
\hline
\text{Type 0A / 0B / 0C} & (a_A,b_A,c_A)=(0,0,0)\\
\text{Naive even singlet } \theta'^2\sigma_3 & a_A=0\\
\text{Pure transverse doublet} & a_A=0,\ (b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0)\text{ possible}\\
\text{Primitive odd longitudinal singlet} & a_A\neq 0\text{ possible},\ b_A=c_A=0\\
\text{Class I} & a_A,b_A,c_A\text{ admissible in principle}\\
\text{Class II} & a_A,b_A,c_A\text{ explicitly realizable}\\
\text{Class III} & a_A,b_A,c_A\text{ admissible in principle}
\end{array}
\]

\paragraph{Key structural conclusions.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Pure scalar/projector/amplitude-only classes are completely excluded.
\item A naive even longitudinal singlet is excluded by parity.
\item The transverse witness sector is already explicitly realized by the canonical odd transverse doublet source.
\item The minimal surviving longitudinal mechanism is the primitive odd singlet
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu,
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
\item Class II is the strongest explicit microscopic carrier class because
\[
X_i^3\leftrightarrow B_\parallel,\qquad
X_i^1\leftrightarrow B_I,\qquad
X_i^2\leftrightarrow B_J.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{Exact remaining frontier.}
Therefore the final microscopic audit is reduced to:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
Since the transverse half is already explicitly available, the only genuinely unresolved microscopic question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the complete TECT linearization realize at least one nonzero primitive longitudinal seed?}
}
\]


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Longitudinal Primitive 3-Step Audit Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now convert the remaining longitudinal carrier question into an explicit finite audit.
The objective is to isolate a practical sufficient-and-necessary chain for the survival of the primitive longitudinal channel in the shell-reduced Dirac witness problem.

\section{Setup}

Fix the defect/projector data
\[
P_B(\xi),\qquad Q_B(\xi)=\mathbf 1-P_B(\xi),
\qquad e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi),
\qquad f_\pm(\xi),
\qquad \mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
The longitudinal primitive channel is expected to come from the traceless quadratic \(Q_B\)-response:
\[
S_\xi
:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
Equivalently, in the \(Q_B\)-frame,
\[
(T_\xi)_{ab}:=\langle e_a,\mathcal T_\xi e_b\rangle,
\qquad
S_\xi=T_\xi^2-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(T_\xi^2)\mathbf 1_2.
\]

Write its Pauli decomposition as
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]

The primitive longitudinal transport kernel is then
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
\]

\section{The Three Audit Steps}

\paragraph{Step 1: Nontrivial quadratic traceless response.}
Compute
\[
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
If
\[
S_\xi\equiv 0,
\]
then there is no primitive longitudinal channel at all.

\paragraph{Step 2: Nonvanishing singlet component.}
Decompose
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]
If
\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0,
\]
then the quadratic response has no longitudinal singlet projection, so the primitive longitudinal witness vanishes.

\paragraph{Step 3: Low-mode overlap test.}
Define the longitudinal overlap functional
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
s_3(\xi).
\]
If
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0,
\]
then the projected longitudinal witness is nonzero:
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{Longitudinal Primitive Audit Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[3-step longitudinal audit]
Let
\[
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
and define
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)s_3(\xi).
\]
Then the following implications hold:

\begin{enumerate}
\item If \(S_\xi\equiv 0\), then the primitive longitudinal channel is absent.
\item If \(S_\xi\not\equiv 0\) but \(s_3(\xi)\equiv 0\), then the primitive longitudinal channel has no singlet projection, hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel=0.
\]
\item If \(s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0\) but \(J_\parallel^{(3)}=0\), then the longitudinal singlet exists algebraically but is killed by the graded low-mode overlap.
\item If
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the survival of the longitudinal primitive channel is reduced to the finite chain
\[
\boxed{
T_\xi
\ \longrightarrow\
S_\xi
\ \longrightarrow\
s_3(\xi)
\ \longrightarrow\
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first statement is immediate from the definition of the primitive channel:
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)S_\xi n^\mu.
\]
If \(S_\xi\equiv 0\), then \(V^\mu_{(\parallel)}\equiv 0\).

For the second statement, the longitudinal witness couples only to the singlet \(\sigma_3\)-component of the traceless \(Q_B\)-response.
Hence if \(s_3(\xi)\equiv 0\), the primitive kernel has no longitudinal singlet content.

For the third statement, even when the singlet component exists, the actual projected witness is determined by its overlap with the graded low-mode pair \(f_+,f_-\).
Thus the projected coefficient is exactly
\[
\lambda_\parallel \propto J_\parallel^{(3)}.
\]
If this overlap vanishes, then the projected longitudinal witness vanishes.

For the fourth statement, the same formula shows that any nonzero value of \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) implies
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
This proves the chain.
\end{proof}

\section{Parity Structure and the Necessity of the Odd Upgrade}

A naive singlet source would be
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{naive}}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)^2\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
But then the relevant overlap would be
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
Since
\[
f_+ \text{ is even},\qquad
f_- \text{ is odd},\qquad
\theta'(\xi)^2 \text{ is even},
\]
the integrand is odd, and therefore
\[
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'^2=0.
\]
So the naive even singlet cannot contribute.
This proves that the primitive longitudinal channel must carry one additional odd factor, namely the odd upgrade
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi.
\]

\section{Explicit Toy Representative}

In the explicit seed representative, one has
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]
Therefore
\[
s_1(\xi)=0,\qquad
s_2(\xi)=0,\qquad
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
The primitive transport kernel becomes
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)S_\xi n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Hence
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Using the explicit seed evaluation,
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we obtain
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]
Thus for a nontrivial defect profile \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\),
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{Sharp Honest Status}

The 3-step audit theorem closes the longitudinal problem up to one final microscopic question.

\begin{enumerate}
\item Inside the explicit seed representative, the primitive longitudinal channel survives completely:
\[
S_\xi\neq 0,\qquad
s_3(\xi)\neq 0,\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]
\item Therefore longitudinal witness existence is no longer an abstract issue.
\item What remains open is only whether the \emph{actual complete microscopic TECT linearization} produces a nonzero traceless quadratic \(Q_B\)-response with
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\]
in the physically relevant defect background.
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently, the remaining frontier is the executable finite test:
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)\stackrel{?}{\not\equiv}0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\]

%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the Longitudinal 3-Step Audit}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
The primitive longitudinal carrier problem is reduced to a finite audit chain:
\[
\boxed{
T_\xi
\ \longrightarrow\
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
\ \longrightarrow\
s_3(\xi)
\ \longrightarrow\
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Definitions.}
Write
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
and define
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)s_3(\xi).
\]

\paragraph{Exact implications.}
Then:

\[
S_\xi\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no primitive longitudinal channel},
\]

\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{no longitudinal singlet projection},
\]

\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=0
\Longrightarrow
\text{the graded low-mode overlap kills the longitudinal witness},
\]

\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Toy representative.}
In the explicit seed representative,
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
so
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\theta_0^3\kappa^3
\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
\]
Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\]
in the toy representative.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Therefore the only remaining microscopic question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the complete microscopic TECT linearization produce a nonzero traceless quadratic }Q_B\text{-response with }J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0?
}
\]

So the longitudinal frontier is no longer abstract.
It is exactly the executable 3-step audit:
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi\not\equiv 0,\qquad
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0,\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Quadratic-Response Non-Forbiddance Theorem for the Longitudinal Singlet}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now prove the strongest honest statement available at this stage:
the \(\sigma_3\)-component of the traceless quadratic \(Q_B\)-response is \emph{not} forbidden by the minimal residual symmetry of the defect/shell configuration.
Equivalently, the vanishing of the longitudinal singlet coefficient
\[
s_3(\xi)
\]
cannot be attributed to the basic shell residual symmetry alone; it would require either an additional exchange symmetry or an accidental/dynamical cancellation.

\section{General Quadratic \(Q_B\)-Response}

Let
\[
P_B(\xi)
\]
be the local rank-one projector of the defect background, and let
\[
Q_B(\xi)=\mathbf 1-P_B(\xi)
\]
be the rank-two orthogonal complement bundle.
Choose the adapted local \(Q_B\)-frame
\[
(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)),
\]
where \(e_1\) is the tangent direction singled out by the defect gradient and \(e_2\) is the orthogonal spectator direction.

Consider any Hermitian quadratic response operator restricted to \(Q_B\):
\[
R_\xi:=\Pi_Q \,\mathcal R_\xi\, \Pi_Q \in \mathrm{End}(Q_B),
\]
where \(\mathcal R_\xi\) is built quadratically from the local background response data.
Its traceless part is
\[
S_\xi:=R_\xi-\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}(R_\xi)\mathbf 1_2.
\]
In the adapted frame,
\[
R_\xi=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}(\xi) & r_{12}(\xi)\\
\overline{r_{12}(\xi)} & r_{22}(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
r_{11},r_{22}\in\mathbb R.
\]
Therefore
\[
S_\xi
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
with
\begin{align}
s_1(\xi)&=\Re r_{12}(\xi),\\
s_2(\xi)&=-\Im r_{12}(\xi),\\
s_3(\xi)&=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}(\xi)-r_{22}(\xi)\bigr).
\end{align}

Hence the longitudinal singlet coefficient is exactly the diagonal anisotropy:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:s3_diag_difference}
\end{equation}

\section{Residual Symmetry Does Not Force \(s_3=0\)}

The shell-relevant local symmetry splits both the worldvolume and internal traceless sectors into
\[
1\oplus 2.
\]
The unique longitudinal singlet channel is
\[
p_\parallel \longleftrightarrow \sigma_3,
\]
while the transverse channels are
\[
(p_1,p_2)\longleftrightarrow (\sigma_1,\sigma_2).
\]
Therefore \(\sigma_3\) is not an illegal structure.
It is the unique singlet generator selected by the same residual symmetry that defines the Weyl template.

This immediately implies the following.

\begin{theorem}[Non-forbiddance of the quadratic longitudinal singlet]
Let \(S_\xi\) be the traceless part of any shell-relevant Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response in the adapted frame \((e_1,e_2)\).
Then the minimal residual shell symmetry does not force
\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0.
\]
Equivalently, the longitudinal singlet \(\sigma_3\) is symmetry-allowed.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The residual symmetry distinguishes one longitudinal singlet and one transverse doublet.
The traceless fiber sector decomposes exactly as
\[
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathbb R\,\sigma_3
\oplus
\mathrm{span}\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2\}.
\]
Therefore \(\sigma_3\) is part of the allowed invariant structure.
A vanishing theorem
\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\]
could follow only if there were an additional symmetry exchanging \(e_1\) and \(e_2\) or forcing the quadratic response to act isotropically on \(Q_B\).
But such an exchange symmetry is not contained in the minimal shell residual symmetry itself, because the defect gradient already singles out \(e_1\).
Hence the basic residual symmetry alone does not imply \(s_3\equiv 0\).
\end{proof}

\section{Anisotropy Criterion}

Because \(s_3(\xi)\) is exactly the diagonal anisotropy \eqref{eq:s3_diag_difference}, we get the sharp criterion:

\begin{theorem}[Diagonal-anisotropy criterion]
For a shell-relevant Hermitian quadratic response \(R_\xi\) on \(Q_B\),
\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\langle e_1,R_\xi e_1\rangle
=
\langle e_2,R_\xi e_2\rangle
\quad
\text{for all }\xi.
\]
Therefore a sufficient condition for longitudinal-singlet survival is:
\[
\exists \xi
\text{ such that }
\langle e_1,R_\xi e_1\rangle
\neq
\langle e_2,R_\xi e_2\rangle.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from
\[
s_3(\xi)=\frac12(r_{11}(\xi)-r_{22}(\xi)).
\]
\end{proof}

So the actual microscopic audit is sharply reduced:
to produce a longitudinal primitive seed, it is enough to show that the quadratic \(Q_B\)-response is not isotropic between the defect-selected tangent direction \(e_1\) and the spectator direction \(e_2\).

\section{Why Defect Geometry Naturally Allows Such Anisotropy}

The defect gradient already breaks the symmetry between \(e_1\) and \(e_2\).

Indeed, the basic commutator channel
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B]
\]
is built from the derivative of the defect projector.
It therefore measures variation along the distinguished defect direction.
In the explicit representative, \(\mathcal T_\xi\) exchanges the condensate line \(\mathbb C z_B\) with \(\mathbb C e_1\), while annihilating \(e_2\).
Thus its quadratic action need not be isotropic on \(Q_B\).

This is the structural reason why a \(\sigma_3\)-type splitting is natural rather than exceptional.

\section{Explicit Seed Representative}

In the explicit representative one has
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi\Pi_Q=0,
\]
but
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\]
Hence
\[
S_\xi
:=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\]
Therefore
\[
s_1(\xi)=0,
\qquad
s_2(\xi)=0,
\qquad
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
So for any nontrivial defect profile,
\[
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
\]

This explicit model saturates the general non-forbiddance theorem:
the longitudinal singlet is not only allowed, it is actually realized.

\section{Parity-Allowed Longitudinal Primitive Channel}

The quadratic response \(S_\xi\sim \theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3\) is even in \(\xi\).
To survive the graded low-mode overlap, one must multiply by one additional odd factor \(\theta'(\xi)\).
Thus the primitive longitudinal transport kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu.
\]
In the explicit seed representative,
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Its projected witness is
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Since
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0
\]
for a nontrivial defect profile, the longitudinal witness survives:
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The actual logical position is now clear.

\begin{enumerate}
\item The coefficient \(s_3(\xi)\) is not forbidden by the minimal shell residual symmetry.
\item Its vanishing would require either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional \(e_1\leftrightarrow e_2\) exchange symmetry,
\item an exact isotropy of the quadratic \(Q_B\)-response,
\item or an accidental/dynamical cancellation.
\end{enumerate}
\item The explicit seed representative realizes
\[
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\]
hence
\[
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\]
and
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the remaining microscopic frontier is not a symmetry question.
It is the coefficient-identification question:

\[
\boxed{
\text{does the complete microscopic TECT linearization produce a non-isotropic quadratic }Q_B\text{-response,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{equivalently }s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0\text{ with }J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0\text{?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the Quadratic-Response Non-Forbiddance Step}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
For any shell-relevant Hermitian quadratic response on \(Q_B\),
\[
R_\xi=
\Pi_Q \mathcal R_\xi \Pi_Q,
\qquad
S_\xi=R_\xi-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(R_\xi)\mathbf 1_2,
\]
the traceless part has the Pauli decomposition
\[
S_\xi=s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi e_1\rangle-\langle e_2,R_\xi e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
}
\]

\paragraph{Non-forbiddance theorem.}
The minimal shell residual symmetry does not force
\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0.
\]
The reason is that the defect gradient already singles out \(e_1\), so the longitudinal singlet
\[
\sigma_3
\]
is symmetry-allowed rather than forbidden.

\paragraph{Sharp criterion.}
Thus
\[
s_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\langle e_1,R_\xi e_1\rangle
=
\langle e_2,R_\xi e_2\rangle
\quad
\text{for all }\xi.
\]
So a sufficient condition for longitudinal survival is simply:
\[
\exists \xi:\ 
\langle e_1,R_\xi e_1\rangle
\neq
\langle e_2,R_\xi e_2\rangle.
\]

\paragraph{Explicit seed representative.}
In the explicit representative,
\[
\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}(1+\sigma_3),
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
S_\xi=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
}
\]
Therefore
\[
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\not\equiv 0
\]
for a nontrivial defect.

Multiplying by the required odd factor \(\theta'(\xi)\) gives
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)S_\xi n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and the projected overlap becomes
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Therefore the remaining longitudinal microscopic question is no longer:
\[
\text{``is }\sigma_3\text{ symmetry-forbidden?''}
\]
That question is closed.

The actual remaining question is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the complete microscopic TECT linearization produce a non-isotropic quadratic }Q_B\text{-response}
}
\]
so that
\[
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0?
}
\]


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Diagonal-Anisotropy Sufficient Criterion for \(s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now isolate the sharpest practical sufficient condition for the survival of the longitudinal singlet component in the actual quadratic \(Q_B\)-response.
The point is to replace the vague question
\[
\text{``does the complete microscopic TECT linearization produce }s_3(\xi)\neq 0\text{?''}
\]
by a concrete diagonal-anisotropy test.

\section{General Hermitian Quadratic Response on \(Q_B\)}

Let
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\Pi_Q \mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} \Pi_Q
\in \mathrm{End}(Q_B)
\]
be the actual shell-relevant Hermitian quadratic response extracted from the complete microscopic TECT linearization around the chosen defect background.

Choose the adapted \(Q_B\)-frame
\[
(e_1(\xi),e_2(\xi)),
\]
where \(e_1\) is the defect-selected tangent direction and \(e_2\) is the orthogonal spectator direction.
Then
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}(\xi) & r_{12}(\xi)\\
\overline{r_{12}(\xi)} & r_{22}(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
r_{11},r_{22}\in\mathbb R.
\]
Its traceless part is
\[
S_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
-\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}})\mathbf 1_2
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
with
\[
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\bigl(r_{11}(\xi)-r_{22}(\xi)\bigr).
\]

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:s3_diag_actual}
\end{equation}

\section{Minimal Diagonal-Anisotropy Criterion}

\begin{theorem}[Diagonal-anisotropy sufficient criterion]
Let \(R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\) be the actual Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response.
If there exists at least one \(\xi_0\) such that
\begin{equation}
\langle e_1(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_1(\xi_0)\rangle
\neq
\langle e_2(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_2(\xi_0)\rangle,
\label{eq:min_diag_aniso_condition}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By \eqref{eq:s3_diag_actual},
\[
s_3(\xi_0)
=
\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
\]
If the two diagonal matrix elements differ at \(\xi_0\), then \(s_3(\xi_0)\neq 0\).
Hence \(s_3(\xi)\) cannot vanish identically.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
So the longitudinal singlet survives whenever the actual quadratic \(Q_B\)-response is not isotropic between the defect-selected tangent channel \(e_1\) and the spectator channel \(e_2\).

\section{Canonical Decomposition of the Actual Response}

Every Hermitian \(2\times2\) response may be written as
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
u_0(\xi)\mathbf 1_2
+
u_1(\xi)\sigma_1
+
u_2(\xi)\sigma_2
+
u_3(\xi)\sigma_3.
\]
Then
\[
S_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
u_1(\xi)\sigma_1+u_2(\xi)\sigma_2+u_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
so
\[
s_3(\xi)=u_3(\xi).
\]

Therefore the practical criterion becomes:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
\text{ contains a genuine }\sigma_3\text{-anisotropic component.}
}
\label{eq:u3_sigma3_criterion}
\end{equation}

This makes the final audit especially simple:
one does not need the whole response, only the coefficient of the diagonal anisotropy operator
\[
|e_1\rangle\langle e_1|-|e_2\rangle\langle e_2|
\;\cong\;
\sigma_3.
\]

\section{Structural Origin of Diagonal Anisotropy}

The crucial geometric fact is that the defect already distinguishes the two \(Q_B\)-channels.

Indeed,
\[
e_1(\xi)\propto \partial_\xi z_B(\xi)
\]
is the tangent direction selected by the defect gradient, whereas \(e_2\) is the orthogonal spectator.
So an exact equality
\[
\langle e_1,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} e_1\rangle
=
\langle e_2,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} e_2\rangle
\]
for all \(\xi\) would require more than the minimal shell residual symmetry.
It would require either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional exchange symmetry \(e_1\leftrightarrow e_2\), or
\item an exact dynamical isotropy of the quadratic \(Q_B\)-response.
\end{enumerate}
Neither is forced by the basic defect/shell setup.

Hence the natural expectation is that a generic actual quadratic response should contain a nontrivial \(\sigma_3\)-component unless some extra cancellation is present.

\section{Comparison with Explicit Seed Representative}

In the explicit seed representative,
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3.
\]
Thus
\[
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
This is the model example of the general criterion:
the diagonal matrix element in the \(e_1\)-channel differs from that in the \(e_2\)-channel, so \(s_3\) survives.

Moreover, after multiplying by the required odd prefactor \(\theta'(\xi)\),
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)S_\xi n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and the low-mode overlap gives
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]
So the explicit representative saturates the criterion completely.

\section{Independent Support from the Channel Hessian}

The same structural mechanism also appears in the improved effective projector-Hessian model.
In the adapted \((e_1,e_2)\)-basis, the tangent-space Hessian is
\[
W_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
(\lambda+\mu)\cos^2 2\theta(\xi) & 0\\
0 & \lambda+2\mu\cos^2\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Thus the two diagonal channels are generically unequal:
\[
W_{11}(\xi)\neq W_{22}(\xi)
\]
unless special parameter/profile identities happen to hold.
Therefore the defect geometry naturally generates diagonal anisotropy on \(Q_B\).

This does not by itself prove the final complete TECT coefficient extraction,
but it strongly supports the claim that \(s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0\) is a natural and stable possibility rather than an exceptional fine tuning.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We can now state the strongest honest theorem of this step:

\begin{theorem}[Practical sufficient criterion for longitudinal-singlet survival]
Let \(R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\) be the actual shell-relevant Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response of the complete microscopic TECT linearization.
If
\[
\exists \xi_0\ \text{such that}\ 
\langle e_1(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_1(\xi_0)\rangle
\neq
\langle e_2(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_2(\xi_0)\rangle,
\]
then
\[
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
\]
Hence the only further step needed for longitudinal survival is the overlap test
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)s_3(\xi).
\]
If this is also nonzero, then
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So the longitudinal frontier is no longer:
\[
\text{``derive the whole PDE and solve everything.''}
\]
It is now exactly the finite two-part audit:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) show diagonal anisotropy on }Q_B,
\qquad
\text{(ii) show nonzero graded overlap }J_\parallel^{(3)}.
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the Diagonal-Anisotropy Sufficient Criterion}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
For the actual Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response
\[
R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\Pi_Q\mathcal R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}\Pi_Q,
\]
its traceless part is
\[
S_\xi^{\mathrm{act}}
=
s_1(\xi)\sigma_1+s_2(\xi)\sigma_2+s_3(\xi)\sigma_3,
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi^{\mathrm{act}} e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
}
\]

\paragraph{Practical sufficient criterion.}
Therefore,
\[
\boxed{
\exists \xi_0:\ 
\langle e_1(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_1(\xi_0)\rangle
\neq
\langle e_2(\xi_0),R_{\xi_0}^{\mathrm{act}} e_2(\xi_0)\rangle
\Longrightarrow
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\]

So longitudinal-singlet survival is guaranteed once the quadratic \(Q_B\)-response is not isotropic between the defect-selected tangent channel \(e_1\) and the spectator channel \(e_2\).

\paragraph{Explicit representative.}
In the explicit seed representative,
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,
\]
hence
\[
s_3(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\not\equiv 0.
\]
After the required odd upgrade,
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Independent support.}
The improved projector-Hessian model already exhibits diagonal channel anisotropy:
\[
W_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
(\lambda+\mu)\cos^2 2\theta(\xi) & 0\\
0 & \lambda+2\mu\cos^2\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
so \(e_1\) and \(e_2\) are generically not equivalent dynamically.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Hence the longitudinal frontier is now exactly the finite two-step check:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) verify diagonal anisotropy }s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
\text{(ii) verify }J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]
This is a coefficient-identification problem, not a symmetry problem.



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Generic Nonvanishing Theorem for the Longitudinal Singlet Coefficient \(s_3(\xi)\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now sharpen the previous diagonal-anisotropy criterion to a genericity theorem.
The question is no longer merely whether
\[
s_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\]
is allowed.
The sharper question is:

\[
\text{when is } s_3(\xi)\equiv 0 \text{ forced, and when is it nongeneric?}
\]

\section{Actual Quadratic Response Family}

Let the actual shell-relevant Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-response be a family
\[
R_\xi(c)
=
u_0(\xi;c)\mathbf 1_2
+
u_1(\xi;c)\sigma_1
+
u_2(\xi;c)\sigma_2
+
u_3(\xi;c)\sigma_3,
\]
depending on microscopic coefficients
\[
c=(c_1,\dots,c_m)\in \mathcal P
\]
in some finite-dimensional local parameter space \(\mathcal P\) of symmetry-allowed quadratic response data.

Its traceless part is
\[
S_\xi(c)
=
u_1(\xi;c)\sigma_1
+
u_2(\xi;c)\sigma_2
+
u_3(\xi;c)\sigma_3,
\]
and the longitudinal singlet coefficient is
\[
s_3(\xi;c)=u_3(\xi;c).
\]

Equivalently, in the adapted frame \((e_1,e_2)\),
\[
u_3(\xi;c)
=
\frac12
\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi(c)e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi(c)e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
\]

Thus \(u_3\equiv 0\) means exact diagonal isotropy of the quadratic response on \(Q_B\).

\section{What Can Force \(u_3(\xi)\equiv 0\)}

\begin{theorem}[Forcing mechanisms for \(u_3\equiv 0\)]
The identity
\[
u_3(\xi;c)\equiv 0
\]
can be structurally forced only if at least one of the following occurs:

\begin{enumerate}
\item an additional symmetry exchanges \(e_1\) and \(e_2\);
\item the quadratic response is exactly isotropic on \(Q_B\):
\[
R_\xi(c)=u_0(\xi;c)\mathbf 1_2+u_1(\xi;c)\sigma_1+u_2(\xi;c)\sigma_2
\quad\text{with}\quad
u_3(\xi;c)\equiv 0;
\]
\item the microscopic coefficients are fine-tuned to a cancellation locus.
\end{enumerate}

In particular, the minimal defect/shell residual symmetry alone does not force \(u_3\equiv 0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The longitudinal singlet \(\sigma_3\) is part of the symmetry-allowed shell-reduced structure:
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Hence the basic residual symmetry allows a singlet channel rather than excluding it.

Therefore a vanishing theorem
\[
u_3(\xi;c)\equiv 0
\]
cannot follow from the minimal symmetry alone.
It can only come from a stronger condition that makes the two \(Q_B\)-directions \(e_1,e_2\) exactly equivalent, or from a coefficient cancellation.

But the defect gradient already singles out \(e_1\), so such an equivalence is additional, not intrinsic.
\end{proof}

\section{Generic Nonvanishing in a Finite-Dimensional Microscopic Family}

We now formulate the precise genericity statement.

Fix one point \(\xi_0\).
Assume that
\[
c\longmapsto u_3(\xi_0;c)
\]
is a polynomial, affine, or real-analytic function on \(\mathcal P\).
Define the bad set
\[
\mathcal Z_{\xi_0}
:=
\{c\in\mathcal P:\ u_3(\xi_0;c)=0\}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Generic nonvanishing theorem for \(u_3\)]
Assume there exists at least one admissible benchmark parameter
\[
c^{\mathrm{bench}}\in\mathcal P
\]
such that
\[
u_3(\xi_0;c^{\mathrm{bench}})\neq 0
\]
for some \(\xi_0\).
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(u_3(\xi_0;\cdot)\) is not identically zero on \(\mathcal P\);
\item the bad set \(\mathcal Z_{\xi_0}\) is a proper algebraic/analytic subset of \(\mathcal P\);
\item therefore its complement
\[
\mathcal U_{\xi_0}:=\mathcal P\setminus \mathcal Z_{\xi_0}
\]
is open and dense, and full measure whenever \(\mathcal P\) is equipped with the natural Lebesgue-class measure;
\item hence \(u_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0\) is generic in the actual microscopic family.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(u_3(\xi_0;\cdot)\) is polynomial/analytic and nonzero at \(c^{\mathrm{bench}}\), it is not the zero function.
Therefore its zero locus cannot contain any open set.
Hence
\[
\mathcal Z_{\xi_0}
\]
is a proper algebraic/analytic subset, and its complement is open dense.
The last statement follows because if \(u_3(\xi_0;c)\neq 0\) at one point \(\xi_0\), then \(u_3(\xi;c)\) cannot vanish identically in \(\xi\).
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So once one admissible anisotropic benchmark exists inside the same microscopic operator class,
\[
u_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\]
is no longer a natural outcome.
It becomes a nongeneric cancellation condition.

\section{Explicit Benchmark}

The explicit seed representative provides exactly such a benchmark.
There,
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
\]
hence
\[
u_3(\xi)=s_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
Therefore, for a nontrivial defect profile,
\[
u_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
\]

Moreover, the parity-correct longitudinal kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,S_\xi\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and the overlap is
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)u_3(\xi)
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

Thus the benchmark is not merely anisotropic.
It already lies in the longitudinal-good region:
\[
u_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]

\section{Independent Structural Support}

The same diagonal anisotropy pattern also appears in the explicit local projector-Hessian framework.
In the adapted frame, the tangent-space static Hessian is channel-diagonal and distinguishes the two internal directions:
\[
H^{\mathrm{stat}}_B
=
-\rho\partial_\xi^2
+
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda\cos^2 2\theta(\xi)-2\rho\theta'(\xi)^2 & 0\\
0 & \lambda-\rho\theta'(\xi)^2
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
So the two channels are already dynamically inequivalent in the explicit effective local model.
This strongly supports the claim that diagonal anisotropy on \(Q_B\) is natural rather than exceptional.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We can now state the strongest honest result of this step.

\begin{theorem}[Generic nonvanishing of the longitudinal singlet coefficient]
Let \(R_\xi(c)\) be a finite-dimensional symmetry-allowed family of Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-responses.
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item no additional residual symmetry exchanges \(e_1\) and \(e_2\);
\item the family contains at least one admissible benchmark \(c^{\mathrm{bench}}\) with
\[
u_3(\xi_0;c^{\mathrm{bench}})\neq 0
\]
for some \(\xi_0\).
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
u_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\]
is nongeneric: it defines at most a proper algebraic/analytic subset of the microscopic coefficient space.
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
u_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\text{ is the generic situation.}
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
What still remains open is not the genericity statement itself.
The remaining microscopic task is the identification of the actual complete TECT coefficient point:
\[
c_{\mathrm{TECT}}\in\mathcal P.
\]
One must still check that the actual full quadratic response of complete TECT lies outside the bad subset and also satisfies
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]

So the exact remaining longitudinal audit is:
\[
\boxed{
c_{\mathrm{TECT}}\notin \{u_3\equiv 0\}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0.
}
\]

%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the Generic Nonvanishing Step for \(s_3(\xi)\)}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
Let
\[
R_\xi(c)
=
u_0(\xi;c)\mathbf 1_2
+
u_1(\xi;c)\sigma_1
+
u_2(\xi;c)\sigma_2
+
u_3(\xi;c)\sigma_3
\]
be a finite-dimensional symmetry-allowed family of quadratic \(Q_B\)-responses.
Then
\[
u_3(\xi;c)
=
\frac12\Bigl(
\langle e_1,R_\xi(c)e_1\rangle
-
\langle e_2,R_\xi(c)e_2\rangle
\Bigr).
\]

So
\[
u_3(\xi)\equiv 0
\]
means exact diagonal isotropy between the defect-selected channel \(e_1\) and the spectator channel \(e_2\).

\paragraph{What can force \(u_3\equiv 0\).}
Such a vanishing can be forced only by:
\[
\text{(i) an extra }e_1\leftrightarrow e_2\text{ exchange symmetry,}
\quad
\text{(ii) exact isotropy,}
\quad
\text{or (iii) fine tuning.}
\]
It is \emph{not} forced by the basic defect/shell residual symmetry.

\paragraph{Genericity theorem.}
If the microscopic family contains one admissible benchmark with
\[
u_3(\xi_0)\neq 0
\]
for some \(\xi_0\), then the bad set
\[
\{c:\ u_3(\xi_0;c)=0\}
\]
is a proper algebraic/analytic subset.
Hence
\[
\boxed{
u_3(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\text{ is generic.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Explicit benchmark.}
In the explicit seed representative,
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
\]
so
\[
u_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\not\equiv 0.
\]
After the odd upgrade,
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
and
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Independent support.}
The explicit projector-Hessian model already distinguishes the two \(Q_B\)-channels dynamically, so diagonal anisotropy is natural rather than exceptional.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Therefore the remaining microscopic question is not whether \(u_3\equiv 0\) is generically possible.
That is already settled.

The actual remaining task is to identify the true complete TECT coefficient point
\[
c_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
and verify that
\[
\boxed{
u_3(\xi;c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0.
}
\]


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Generic Nonvanishing Theorem for the Longitudinal Overlap Functional \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the last general genericity step on the longitudinal side.
Previously we reduced the primitive longitudinal survival problem to the finite test
\[
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]
The remaining question is therefore:
when is
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi;c)
\]
generically nonzero in a symmetry-allowed microscopic family?

\section{Definition of the Longitudinal Overlap Functional}

Let
\[
R_\xi(c)
=
u_0(\xi;c)\mathbf 1_2
+
u_1(\xi;c)\sigma_1
+
u_2(\xi;c)\sigma_2
+
u_3(\xi;c)\sigma_3
\]
be a finite-dimensional symmetry-allowed family of Hermitian quadratic \(Q_B\)-responses, depending on microscopic coefficients
\[
c=(c_1,\dots,c_m)\in\mathcal P.
\]
The parity-correct primitive longitudinal transport kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi;c)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi;c)\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\]
Define the longitudinal overlap functional
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)
:=
\int d\xi\,
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi;c).
}
\label{eq:J3_def_generic}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the projected longitudinal witness up to a fixed nonzero normalization factor.
Equivalently,
\[
\lambda_\parallel(c)\propto J_\parallel^{(3)}(c).
\]

\section{Linearity / Analyticity of \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\)}

\begin{theorem}[Functional character of \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\)]
Assume \(u_3(\xi;c)\) depends linearly on the microscopic tensor/response coefficients \(c\), or more generally real-analytically on \(c\).
Then \(J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)\) is respectively:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a linear functional on the finite-dimensional microscopic coefficient space \(\mathcal P\), or
\item a real-analytic scalar function on \(\mathcal P\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The map
\[
u_3(\cdot;c)\longmapsto
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi;c)
\]
is linear in \(u_3\).
Therefore, if \(u_3\) depends linearly on \(c\), then so does \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\).

More generally, if \(u_3(\xi;c)\) is real-analytic in \(c\) for each \(\xi\), then the weighted integral against the fixed profile
\[
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
\]
preserves real-analytic dependence.
Hence \(J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)\) is real-analytic.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
So \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) is not a mysterious nonlocal quantity.
It is a finite-dimensional witness functional of exactly the same kind as the shell-level longitudinal witness \(v_\parallel\) in the earlier genericity theorems.

\section{Generic Nonvanishing Theorem}

Fix the bad set
\[
\mathcal Z_J
:=
\{c\in\mathcal P:\ J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)=0\}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Generic nonvanishing of the longitudinal overlap]
Assume there exists at least one admissible benchmark point
\[
c^{\mathrm{bench}}\in\mathcal P
\]
such that
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c^{\mathrm{bench}})\neq 0.
\]
Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) is not identically zero on \(\mathcal P\);
\item if \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) is linear, then
\[
\mathcal Z_J=\ker J_\parallel^{(3)}
\]
is a proper hyperplane in \(\mathcal P\);
\item if \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) is real-analytic, then \(\mathcal Z_J\) is a proper analytic subset of \(\mathcal P\);
\item in either case, the good set
\[
\mathcal U_J:=\mathcal P\setminus\mathcal Z_J
\]
is open and dense, and full measure in the linear case (and also Lebesgue-null complement in the standard analytic finite-dimensional setting).
\end{enumerate}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)\neq 0
\text{ is generic once one nonzero benchmark exists.}
}
\label{eq:J3_generic_nonzero}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c^{\mathrm{bench}})\neq 0,
\]
the function \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\) is not identically zero.

If it is linear, then its zero set is the kernel of a nonzero linear functional on a finite-dimensional space, hence a proper hyperplane.

If it is real-analytic, then the zero set of a nontrivial analytic function is a proper analytic subset and cannot contain an open set.

Thus in either case the complement is open dense.
In the linear case the bad set has codimension one and measure zero.
This proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\section{Explicit Benchmark from the Seed Representative}

The explicit seed representative already provides a benchmark point in the good set.
Indeed,
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3,
\]
so
\[
u_3(\xi)=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:J3_seed_eval}
\end{equation}
Using the explicit seed evaluation,
\[
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\]
we obtain
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]
Therefore for a nontrivial defect profile,
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\]

So the benchmark hypothesis of the generic nonvanishing theorem is satisfied inside the explicit seed class.

\section{Relation to the Finite Witness Principle}

The earlier finite witness principle states:

\begin{enumerate}
\item if a linear witness vanishes identically on the allowed microscopic space, then the channel is symmetry-forbidden;
\item if it is nonzero on one admissible seed, then it is nonzero on an open dense full-measure subset.
\end{enumerate}

The present longitudinal overlap theorem is exactly the same logic applied to
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}.
\]
Thus the microscopic content of the longitudinal problem is reduced to one yes/no statement:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}|_{\mathcal P}\not\equiv 0\ ?
}
\label{eq:J3_yesno}
\end{equation}

If the answer is yes, then longitudinal overlap nonvanishing is generic.
If the answer is no, then the obstruction is an exact symmetry selection rule or an exact structural cancellation in the microscopic family.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We can now state the strongest honest theorem of this step.

\begin{theorem}[Generic longitudinal-overlap theorem]
Let \(\mathcal P\) be any finite-dimensional symmetry-allowed microscopic parameter space for the actual quadratic \(Q_B\)-response, and define
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi;c).
\]
Assume:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(u_3(\xi;c)\) depends linearly or real-analytically on \(c\);
\item there exists one admissible benchmark \(c^{\mathrm{bench}}\in\mathcal P\) such that
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c^{\mathrm{bench}})\neq 0.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Then
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)\neq 0
\]
holds on an open dense subset of \(\mathcal P\), and in the linear case on a full-measure subset.
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}=0
\text{ is nongeneric once one nonzero benchmark exists.}
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{What remains open.}
The remaining microscopic task is no longer a genericity question.
It is the identification of the actual complete TECT coefficient point
\[
c_{\mathrm{TECT}}\in\mathcal P
\]
and the verification that it lies in the good set:
\[
\boxed{
u_3(\xi;c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0.
}
\]

So the longitudinal frontier has now been reduced to a concrete coefficient-identification problem for the actual full microscopic TECT linearization.

\section{Final Summary of the Generic Nonvanishing Theorem for \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\)}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
Define the longitudinal overlap functional
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,u_3(\xi;c),
\]
where \(u_3(\xi;c)\) is the \(\sigma_3\)-coefficient of the actual quadratic \(Q_B\)-response.

If \(u_3(\xi;c)\) depends linearly (or more generally real-analytically) on the microscopic coefficients \(c\), then \(J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)\) is a linear (respectively analytic) witness functional on the finite-dimensional microscopic parameter space.

\paragraph{Genericity theorem.}
If there exists one admissible benchmark point \(c^{\mathrm{bench}}\) such that
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c^{\mathrm{bench}})\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\not\equiv 0.
\]
Hence its zero set is:
\[
\text{a proper hyperplane, if }J_\parallel^{(3)}\text{ is linear,}
\]
or
\[
\text{a proper analytic subset, if }J_\parallel^{(3)}\text{ is analytic.}
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c)\neq 0
\text{ is generic.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Explicit benchmark.}
In the explicit seed representative,
\[
S_\xi
=
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,

so

and therefore

=

=

\neq 0
\]
for a nontrivial defect profile.

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So once one nonzero benchmark exists, vanishing of the longitudinal overlap is no longer the natural outcome.
It becomes a nongeneric cancellation condition.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
The remaining microscopic task is now reduced to the identification of the actual full TECT coefficient point
\[
c_{\mathrm{TECT}}
\]
and the verification that
\[
\boxed{
u_3(\xi;c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}(c_{\mathrm{TECT}})\neq 0.

\section{Actual Coefficient-Identification Reduction Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now leave the genericity layer and isolate the exact microscopic quantity that must be extracted from the complete TECT linearization in order to determine the actual longitudinal coefficient.
The aim is not to overclaim that the coefficient has already been computed.
Rather, the goal is to prove that the full coefficient-identification problem reduces to the extraction of one scalar profile function \(h_\parallel(\theta)\).

\section{Actual Local Overlap Formulation}

The strongest honest local statement already established in the project is that the first-order projected transport kernel may be written in the form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\mathbf 1_2
+
a_i^\mu(\theta)\sigma_i.
\]
Projecting onto the even/odd low-mode pair \((f_+,f_-)\) gives
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
\]

In the singlet\(\oplus\)doublet \(S2\) decomposition, the shell-compatible reduced symbol is
\[
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\]
Accordingly, the actual local overlap formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:actual_lambda_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{11}(\theta(\xi))+h_{22}(\theta(\xi))\bigr),
}
\label{eq:actual_alpha_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\bigl(h_{21}(\theta(\xi))-h_{12}(\theta(\xi))\bigr).
}
\label{eq:actual_beta_formula}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal coefficient in the actual microscopic theory is controlled by a \emph{single scalar profile function}
\[
h_\parallel(\theta).
\]

\section{Reduction to a Single Longitudinal Profile Function}

\begin{theorem}[Actual longitudinal coefficient-identification reduction]
Assume the complete microscopic TECT linearization admits the local first-order transport form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with shell-compatible singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition.
Then the actual longitudinal witness coefficient is completely determined by the single scalar profile
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),
\]
through the overlap formula
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
\]
In particular, the full microscopic longitudinal coefficient-identification problem is reduced to extracting \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) from the complete TECT linearized transport operator.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By shell symmetry, the reduced symbol has exactly one longitudinal singlet channel:
\[
p_\parallel \sigma_3.
\]
Therefore the projected first-order operator can contribute to the longitudinal witness only through the coefficient multiplying this unique singlet channel.
By the established actual local overlap formulas, that coefficient is
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
\]
Hence once \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) is known, \(\lambda_\parallel\) is known.
No additional microscopic data are needed for the longitudinal coefficient itself.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
So the longitudinal microscopic frontier is not:
\[
\text{``solve the whole PDE and diagonalize everything.''}
\]
It is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{derive }h_\parallel(\theta)\text{ from the actual full TECT linearization.}
}
\]

\section{Matching to the Concrete Seed Normalization}

Inside the concrete seed transport ansatz, one has the explicit witness normalization
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]
Matching this with the actual local formula \eqref{eq:actual_lambda_formula} gives the exact coefficient-identification relation
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c^{\mathrm{act}}
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:gc_actual_extraction}
\end{equation}

This is the actual longitudinal coefficient extraction formula.

\begin{corollary}[Exact actual-longitudinal matching formula]
Once the function \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) is extracted from the complete microscopic TECT linearization, the actual longitudinal shell coefficient is obtained uniquely by \eqref{eq:gc_actual_extraction}.
\end{corollary}

\section{Equivalent Tensor-Contraction Form}

At the shell-tensor level, the local Weyl coefficient formulas read
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_j N^3_{ij},
\]
\[
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\bigl(e_{1j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}+e_{2j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}\bigr),
\]
\[
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\bigl(e_{2j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}-e_{1j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}\bigr).
\]
Therefore the same longitudinal coefficient-identification problem may also be phrased as:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract the actual tensor }N^3_{ij}\text{ from the full TECT linearization and contract it with }\hat n_i\hat n_j.
}
\]
The \(h_\parallel(\theta)\)-formulation and the \(N^3_{ij}\)-contraction formulation are equivalent descriptions of the same actual microscopic coefficient-identification step.

\section{What Is and Is Not Closed Here}

\begin{theorem}[Sharp honest status of actual coefficient-identification]
At the present stage, the following statement is rigorously closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{The actual longitudinal coefficient-identification problem is reduced to the extraction of }h_\parallel(\theta),
}
\end{equation}
or equivalently the extraction of the shell tensor contraction
\[
\hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij}.
\]

However, the following statement is \emph{not yet} closed:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual full microscopic TECT linearization has already yielded the explicit function }h_\parallel(\theta).
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The reduction statement follows from the established actual local overlap formulas and the shell-compatible singlet\(\oplus\)doublet decomposition.
The non-closure statement follows because the existing project documents explicitly state that the actual microscopic values of
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O
\]
and the final full microscopic projector/condensate PDE remain open.
Thus \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) has not yet been derived from the final complete TECT linearized projector equation.
\end{proof}

\section{Practical Extraction Protocol}

The actual longitudinal coefficient-identification step is therefore the following finite protocol:

\paragraph{(C1)}
Write the full microscopic TECT linearization in the local projector/defect frame.

\paragraph{(C2)}
Extract the first-order transport operator \(V^\mu(\xi)\).

\paragraph{(C3)}
Decompose it as
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]

\paragraph{(C4)}
Project \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) onto the shell-compatible singlet channel to identify \(h_\parallel(\theta)\).

\paragraph{(C5)}
Insert \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) into
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\]
and then into
\[
g_c^{\mathrm{act}}
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
\]

Thus the actual coefficient-identification problem has become an executable finite extraction protocol.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The strongest honest conclusion of this step is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual coefficient-identification is no longer an infinite-dimensional mystery.}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{It is exactly the extraction of }h_\parallel(\theta)\text{ (or equivalently } \hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij}\text{).}
}
\]

What remains open is not the logical reduction,
but only the actual derivation of \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) from the final complete TECT microscopic linearization.

The actual longitudinal coefficient-identification problem is reduced to one scalar profile function:

\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=

Equivalently, at shell-tensor level,

\section{Local-Structure Classification Theorem for the Actual Longitudinal Coefficient \(h_\parallel(\theta)\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now identify exactly which local tensor structures inside the actual first-order transport matrix
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
\]
can contribute to the longitudinal shell-reduced coefficient
\[
h_\parallel(\theta).
\]
This is the last structural reduction before any explicit full-TECT coefficient extraction.

\section{Actual Local First-Order Form}

Assume the actual complete TECT linearization admits the local first-order transport structure
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) is a \(2\times2\) Hermitian matrix-valued worldvolume vector in the shell-reduced low sector.

In the Pauli basis, write
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
a_0^\mu(\theta)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
a_1^\mu(\theta)\,\sigma_1
+
a_2^\mu(\theta)\,\sigma_2
+
a_3^\mu(\theta)\,\sigma_3.
\label{eq:Mmu_pauli_full}
\end{equation}

Choose the shell-adapted worldvolume frame
\[
\{n^\mu, e_1^\mu, e_2^\mu\},
\]
and decompose the coefficient vectors as
\begin{align}
a_0^\mu(\theta)
&=
u_0^\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu
+
u_0^1(\theta)\,e_1^\mu
+
u_0^2(\theta)\,e_2^\mu,\\[1ex]
a_3^\mu(\theta)
&=
u_3^\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu
+
u_3^1(\theta)\,e_1^\mu
+
u_3^2(\theta)\,e_2^\mu,\\[1ex]
(a_1^\mu(\theta),a_2^\mu(\theta))
&=
\text{general transverse-doublet data}.
\end{align}

\section{Invariant Shell-Reduced Decomposition}

Under the residual shell symmetry \(H_\perp\cong SO(2)_\perp\), the worldvolume sector and the traceless internal sector both split as
\[
1\oplus 2.
\]
Hence the shell-compatible invariant first-order structures are exactly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the identity singlet channel
\[
n^\mu \mathbf 1_2;
\]
\item the longitudinal Pauli singlet channel
\[
n^\mu \sigma_3;
\]
\item the transverse-even channel
\[
E^\mu{}_a \sigma_a;
\]
\item the transverse-odd channel
\[
J^\mu{}_a \sigma_a.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the invariant part of \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) has the unique decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:Minv_decomposition}
\end{equation}

All other local structures are non-invariant with respect to the shell-compatible \(S2\) branch and project out of the reduced witness problem.

\section{Which Structures Contribute to \(h_\parallel(\theta)\)}

\begin{theorem}[Local-structure classification theorem]
Let \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) be decomposed as in \eqref{eq:Minv_decomposition}. Then:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the longitudinal coefficient is exactly the coefficient of the unique invariant singlet-Pauli structure:
\[
\boxed{
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr];
}
\]

\item the identity singlet term \(h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2\) does not contribute to \(h_\parallel\);

\item the transverse-even and transverse-odd terms contribute only to \(\alpha,\beta\), not to \(h_\parallel\);

\item any mixed non-invariant structures such as
\[
n^\mu\sigma_1,\quad n^\mu\sigma_2,\quad e_a^\mu\sigma_3,\quad e_a^\mu\mathbf 1_2
\]
have zero projection onto the shell-compatible longitudinal witness.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From \eqref{eq:Minv_decomposition},
\[
n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,\sigma_3,
\]
because
\[
n_\mu E^\mu{}_a=0,
\qquad
n_\mu J^\mu{}_a=0.
\]
Multiply by \(\sigma_3\) and take the normalized trace:
\[
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)\bigr]
=
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[h_0(\theta)\sigma_3 + h_\parallel(\theta)\sigma_3^2\bigr].
\]
Since
\[
\mathrm{Tr}(\sigma_3)=0,
\qquad
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}(\sigma_3^2)=1,
\]
this becomes
\[
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)\bigr]
=
h_\parallel(\theta).
\]
This proves item (1).

Item (2) follows from \(\mathrm{Tr}(\sigma_3 \mathbf 1_2)=0\).

Item (3) follows because the transverse structures are orthogonal to \(n^\mu\), so they vanish under contraction with \(n_\mu\).

Item (4) follows from the representation decomposition:
they lie in \(\mathrm{Hom}(1,2)\) or \(\mathrm{Hom}(2,1)\), or in the wrong \(H_\perp\)-channel, and therefore project out of the shell-compatible longitudinal invariant branch.
\end{proof}

\section{Explicit Coefficient Dictionary}

From the previous theorem, the actual local coefficient dictionary is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_\parallel(\theta)=\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr],
}
\label{eq:hparallel_extraction}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_0(\theta)=\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr],
}
\label{eq:h0_extraction}
\end{equation}
and the transverse coefficients are extracted by contraction with the even/odd doublet projectors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_E(\theta)
=
\frac12 E_{\mu a}\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_a \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr],
\qquad
h_O(\theta)
=
\frac12 J_{\mu a}\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_a \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr].
}
\label{eq:hE_hO_extraction}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual shell witness formulas become
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)).
\end{equation}

\section{Classification Table}

The classification of local structures is therefore:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c}
\text{local structure in }\mathcal M^\mu(\theta) & \text{contribution} \\
\hline
n^\mu \mathbf 1_2 & h_0 \text{ only (scalar drift)} \\
n^\mu \sigma_3 & h_\parallel \text{ only} \\
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a & h_E \text{ only} \\
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a & h_O \text{ only} \\
n^\mu \sigma_{1,2} & 0 \text{ in longitudinal S2 witness} \\
e_a^\mu \sigma_3 & 0 \text{ in longitudinal S2 witness} \\
e_a^\mu \mathbf 1_2 & 0 \text{ in longitudinal S2 witness}
\end{array}
\]

So only one local structure matters for the actual longitudinal coefficient:
\[
\boxed{
n^\mu \sigma_3.
}
\]

\section{Matching to the Concrete \(g_c\)-Normalization}

Inside the concrete seed/Class II normalization,
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\]
Matching with
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi))
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c^{\mathrm{act}}
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the entire actual longitudinal coefficient-identification problem is reduced to reading off the coefficient of \(n^\mu \sigma_3\) in \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\).

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

We can now state the strongest honest theorem of this step.

\begin{theorem}[Sharp local classification for the actual longitudinal coefficient]
In the actual shell-compatible first-order local transport operator
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
the actual longitudinal coefficient \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) is contributed by one and only one invariant local tensor structure:
\[
n^\mu \sigma_3.
\]
Equivalently,
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr].
\]
All other local structures either contribute to the scalar drift channel, to the transverse \((\alpha,\beta)\) channels, or project out of the shell-compatible \(S2\) longitudinal witness.
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{Meaning.}
The remaining actual microscopic problem is therefore no longer vague.
It is precisely:

\[
\boxed{
\text{extract the coefficient of }n^\mu \sigma_3\text{ from the full TECT local transport matrix }\mathcal M^\mu(\theta).
}
\]

\section{Final Summary of the Local-Structure Classification for \(h_\parallel(\theta)\)}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
In the actual shell-compatible local transport matrix
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta),
\]
the invariant decomposition is
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

\paragraph{Key theorem.}
The actual longitudinal coefficient is contributed by one and only one local structure:
\[
\boxed{
n^\mu \sigma_3.
}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\frac12 \mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr].
}
\]

\paragraph{Non-contributing structures.}
The following do \emph{not} contribute to \(h_\parallel\):
\[
n^\mu\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
n^\mu\sigma_{1,2},
\qquad
e_a^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
e_a^\mu\mathbf 1_2.
\]
They either belong to the scalar drift channel, the transverse \((\alpha,\beta)\) sector, or project out of the shell-compatible longitudinal witness.

\paragraph{Actual extraction formula.}
Hence
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\]
and matching to the concrete seed normalization gives
\[
\boxed{
g_c^{\mathrm{act}}
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
}
\]

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
So the remaining actual microscopic problem is now completely localized:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract the coefficient of }n^\mu\sigma_3\text{ from the full TECT local transport matrix }\mathcal M^\mu(\theta).
}
\]
Nothing else contributes to the longitudinal coefficient.


%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Microscopic Source Classification Theorem for the Actual Longitudinal Coefficient \(h_\parallel\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We classify, source by source, which microscopic structures can contribute to the actual local longitudinal coefficient
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr].
\]
The purpose is to separate:

\begin{enumerate}
\item source classes that are rigorously excluded from contributing to \(h_\parallel\),
\item source classes that can contribute only indirectly,
\item source classes that provide an explicit longitudinal prototype,
\item source classes that are admissible in principle but not yet extracted from the full complete TECT linearization.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Local Source Decomposition}

Let the actual shell-compatible local transport matrix be decomposed as
\[
\mathcal M^\mu
=
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{drift}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{trans}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{unclosed}},
\]
where:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{drift}}\) is the identity-valued scalar drift sector;
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{trans}}\) is the explicit transverse odd-gradient doublet source;
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{comm}^2}\) is the primitive commutator-square longitudinal source;
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}\) is the source induced only after integrating out heavy projector modes;
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{med}}\) denotes admissible mixed \((i,a)\)-carrier sources of Class I/II/III;
\item \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{unclosed}}\) denotes possible additional kinetic/quartic full-TECT contributions not yet theorem-level extracted.
\end{enumerate}

Then
\[
h_\parallel
=
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{drift}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{trans}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{med}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{unclosed}},
\]
with
\[
h_\parallel^{(S)}
:=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{(S)}\bigr].
\]

\section{Classes That Cannot Contribute Directly}

\begin{theorem}[Direct exclusion theorem]
The following source classes do not contribute directly to \(h_\parallel\):
\[
\text{Type 0A (pure scalar potential),}\quad
\text{Type 0B (pure projector derivative),}\quad
\text{Type 0C (amplitude-only derivative).}
\]
Equivalently,
\[
h_\parallel^{0A}=h_\parallel^{0B}=h_\parallel^{0C}=0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Any direct contribution to the shell-enriched longitudinal witness must contain:

\begin{enumerate}
\item one shell/background derivative factor,
\item one derivative on the test mode sector,
\item one internal triplet/tangent label,
\item and one structure projecting to the longitudinal invariant tensor \(n^\mu\sigma_3\).
\end{enumerate}

Type 0A, 0B, 0C terms fail this requirement:
they do not produce a linear shell--projector/test mixing source with the required \((i,a)\)-carrier.
Hence they cannot contribute directly to the longitudinal coefficient.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Immediate corollary.}
Any direct microscopic source for \(h_\parallel\) must belong to a genuinely mixed shell–internal transport class.

\section{Scalar Drift and Pure Transverse Sources}

\begin{theorem}[Drift/transverse decoupling]
The following structures do not contribute to \(h_\parallel\):

\begin{enumerate}
\item scalar drift terms of the form \(n^\mu \mathbf 1_2\);
\item pure transverse-even terms \(E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\);
\item pure transverse-odd terms \(J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\);
\item non-invariant mixed terms such as \(n^\mu\sigma_{1,2}\), \(e_a^\mu \sigma_3\), \(e_a^\mu \mathbf 1_2\).
\end{enumerate}

Equivalently,
\[
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{drift}}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{trans}}=0.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By the local invariant decomposition,
\[
h_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu\bigr].
\]
Thus:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(n^\mu\mathbf 1_2\) gives zero because \(\mathrm{Tr}(\sigma_3)=0\);
\item \(E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\) and \(J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\) are worldvolume-transverse, so they vanish under contraction with \(n_\mu\);
\item the remaining non-invariant structures project out of the shell-compatible \(S2\) longitudinal branch.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore only the \(n^\mu\sigma_3\) structure can contribute to \(h_\parallel\).
\end{proof}

\section{Primitive Commutator-Square Source}

Let
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].
\]
Then the direct \(Q_B\)-restriction vanishes:
\[
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi \Pi_Q = 0.
\]
However, the induced quadratic channel is
\[
\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^2}{2}\bigl(\mathbf 1_2+\sigma_3\bigr).
\]
Hence its traceless part is
\[
(\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Primitive longitudinal source theorem]
The primitive commutator-square source
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{comm}^2}(\xi)
=
g_c\,(\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
\]
contributes directly and purely to the longitudinal coefficient:
\[
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{comm}^2}(\xi)
=
\frac12 g_c\,\theta'(\xi)^2,
\qquad
h_E^{\mathrm{comm}^2}=h_O^{\mathrm{comm}^2}=0.
\]
After multiplication by the required odd prefactor \(\theta'(\xi)\), it produces the explicit longitudinal seed
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12 g_c\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu \sigma_3.
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The formula for \((\Pi_Q \mathcal T_\xi^2 \Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\) is explicit.
Since the resulting operator is proportional to \(n^\mu\sigma_3\), it contributes only to the longitudinal singlet coefficient.
The extra odd factor \(\theta'(\xi)\) is required so that the overlap with the even/odd low-mode pair does not vanish by parity.
\end{proof}

\section{Projector-Stiffness Source}

Consider the stiffness term
\[
F_{\mathrm{align}}
=
\frac{\chi}{4}\int d^3x\,\rho^2(\partial_iP\partial_iP).
\]

\begin{theorem}[Projector-stiffness source classification]
Around a locked constant-projector background \(P_0=\mathrm{const}\),
the projector stiffness term does not generically generate a new tree-level shell-enriched tensor.
Therefore
\[
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{stiff,tree}}=0.
\]
Its contribution to \(h_\parallel\) can arise only indirectly, after integrating out the heavy projector mode, provided an admissible shell–projector mixing source exists.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Since \(\partial_iP_0=0\), the stiffness term vanishes on the background and begins only at quadratic order in projector fluctuations.
Thus it contains no tree-level term linear in the shell gradient and linear in a test derivative, i.e. no direct source of the shell-enriched tensor.
However, it gives the projector tangent mode a large positive quadratic operator; after Gaussian elimination, it can induce effective corrections to the witness data, but only indirectly.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
So the stiffness sector is not a direct source of \(h_\parallel\); it is a stabilizing/renormalizing sector.

\section{Admissible Mediated Mixed Sources}

A direct mixed source must carry both a shell/worldvolume derivative index and an internal tangent label.
This yields the minimal admissible mixed classes:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Class I: direct shell–projector derivative coupling;
\item Class II: auxiliary internal vector mediator;
\item Class III: connection/gauge-like mediator.
\end{enumerate}

\begin{theorem}[Admissible mixed-source theorem]
Each of Class I, II, III is symmetry-admissible as a potential source for \(h_\parallel\), because each introduces the required \((i,a)\)-carrier.
Among them, Class II is currently the strongest explicit class.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
A direct source for the shell-enriched tensor must couple:

\begin{enumerate}
\item shell/background derivative structure,
\item internal tangent/projector sector,
\item test-mode derivative sector,
\item shell Pauli label.
\end{enumerate}

Classes I, II, III all satisfy this structural requirement.
Class II is explicit because its canonical seed directions are already known:
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0 \Rightarrow g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
c_I\neq 0 \Rightarrow g_E\neq 0,
\qquad
c_J\neq 0 \Rightarrow g_O\neq 0.
\]
So Class II explicitly realizes all three shell witness directions, including the longitudinal one.
\end{proof}

\section{Unclosed Full-TECT Kinetic / Quartic Sources}

There may exist additional direct contributions to \(h_\parallel\) coming from the actual complete microscopic TECT kinetic/quartic linearization.
However, at the present stage these are not theorem-level extracted in the accepted proof chain.

We therefore denote them collectively by
\[
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{unclosed}}.
\]

\begin{theorem}[Honest unclosed-source clause]
The existence of possible kinetic and quartic contributions to \(h_\parallel\) in the full complete TECT linearization is not ruled out.
But their explicit extraction is still open, because the final full microscopic coefficient functions have not yet been derived from the complete TECT projector/condensate linearization.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is exactly the current honest status of the project:
the actual local overlap formulas are known, but the explicit microscopic functions \(h_\parallel,h_{ij}\) have not yet been extracted from the final full operator.
\end{proof}

\section{Final Source Formula for \(h_\parallel\)}

Collecting the classified contributions, the actual longitudinal coefficient has the source decomposition
\[
\boxed{
h_\parallel
=
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{med}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{unclosed}},
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
h_\parallel^{0A}=h_\parallel^{0B}=h_\parallel^{0C}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{drift}}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{trans}}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{stiff,tree}}=0.
}
\]

Thus the only currently closed direct longitudinal prototype is the primitive commutator-square channel, while Class II provides the cleanest explicit admissible mediated realization.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The strongest honest theorem of this step is:

\begin{theorem}[Microscopic source classification for \(h_\parallel\)]
The actual longitudinal coefficient \(h_\parallel\) receives no direct contribution from:

\[
\text{pure scalar terms, pure projector derivative terms, amplitude-only terms,}
\]
\[
\text{scalar drift terms, pure transverse sources, or tree-level projector stiffness on a locked constant-projector background.}
\]

Its currently closed direct prototype source is the primitive commutator-square channel
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu,
\]
and its currently strongest explicit admissible mixed realization is Class II.

What remains open is the explicit extraction of any additional kinetic/quartic contributions from the full complete TECT linearization.
\end{theorem}
