\section{Final Summary of the Microscopic Source Classification for \(h_\parallel\)}

\paragraph{Closed classification.}
The actual longitudinal coefficient decomposes as
\[
h_\parallel
=
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{comm}^2}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{med}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{stiff,ind}}
+
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{unclosed}},
\]
while the following direct contributions vanish:
\[
h_\parallel^{0A}=h_\parallel^{0B}=h_\parallel^{0C}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{drift}}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{trans}}=0,
\qquad
h_\parallel^{\mathrm{stiff,tree}}=0.
\]

\paragraph{Direct longitudinal prototype.}
The currently closed direct prototype for the longitudinal channel is the primitive commutator-square source:
\[
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
\]
Hence the parity-correct primitive transport kernel is
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12 g_c\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
which contributes purely to \(h_\parallel\).

\paragraph{Indirect projector-stiffness role.}
The projector-stiffness term
\[
F_{\mathrm{align}}\propto \int \rho^2(\partial P\partial P)
\]
does not generically generate a new tree-level \(N^a_{ij}\) on a locked constant-projector background.
Its effect on \(h_\parallel\) can only be indirect, after integrating out the heavy projector mode.

\paragraph{Admissible mixed classes.}
Any direct mixed source for \(h_\parallel\) must carry the required \((i,a)\)-structure.
This makes Classes I, II, III admissible in principle.
Among them, Class II is currently the strongest explicit realization, because it provides canonical seed directions for
\[
g_c,\quad g_E,\quad g_O.
\]

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
What remains open is the explicit extraction of any additional kinetic/quartic contribution from the full complete TECT linearization.
So the current theorem-level status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the direct longitudinal prototype source is known,}
}
\qquad
\boxed{
\text{but the full complete TECT source decomposition is not yet fully extracted.}
}
\]



%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%


\section{Actual Longitudinal Extraction Protocol from the Full Microscopic Linearization}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now formulate the exact extraction protocol for the actual longitudinal coefficient.
The purpose is to close the statement that, once the full microscopic TECT linearized operator is available, the longitudinal coefficient is obtained by a finite projector-and-trace computation.

\section{Microscopic Linearization Hypothesis}

Let the full microscopic TECT condensate equation linearized around the condensed background be written in momentum space as
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\Phi = L(-i\nabla)\Phi.
\end{equation}
Fix a selected BCC shell vector
\[
G_*\in S_{\mathrm{BCC}},
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and expand near that shell:
\begin{equation}
k=G_*+p,
\qquad
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1 e_1+p_2 e_2.
\end{equation}

Assume the microscopic operator admits a first-order Taylor expansion
\begin{equation}
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
L_*:=L(G_*),
\qquad
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\label{eq:actual_Taylor_protocol}
\end{equation}

Assume further that \(L_*\) has a two-dimensional low-energy eigenspace
\[
H_*\subset H_{\mathrm{full}},
\]
with orthogonal projector
\[
P_*:H_{\mathrm{full}}\to H_*.
\]
Fix a Pauli basis on \(H_*\cong \mathbb C^2\):
\[
\mathrm{End}(H_*)=\mathrm{span}\{\mathbf 1_2,\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\}.
\]

\section{Projected First-Order Hamiltonian}

The reduced first-order Hamiltonian at the selected shell is
\begin{equation}
h^{\mathrm{lin}}_+(p)
=
P_*(p_iK_i)P_*\big|_{H_*}.
\label{eq:hlin_protocol}
\end{equation}
Since this is a Hermitian \(2\times 2\) matrix, it decomposes uniquely as
\begin{equation}
h^{\mathrm{lin}}_+(p)
=
a_0(p)\mathbf 1_2
+
a_\mu(p)\sigma_\mu,
\qquad
\mu=1,2,3.
\end{equation}
Define the Pauli-resolved coefficient matrix
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}
:=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
\label{eq:Mmui_protocol}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
a_\mu(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i,
\qquad
h^{\mathrm{lin}}_+(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i\sigma_\mu.
\label{eq:hmatrix_protocol}
\end{equation}

Thus all local Weyl data are determined directly by the projected first derivatives \(P_*K_iP_*\).

\section{Extraction of the Longitudinal Coefficient}

In the shell-adapted matched \(S2\) branch, the most general symmetry-compatible reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:S2_axial_protocol}
\end{equation}
Comparing \eqref{eq:hmatrix_protocol} with \eqref{eq:S2_axial_protocol}, the longitudinal coefficient is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\hat n_i\,M_{3i}
=
\frac12\,\hat n_i\,\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3 P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_projector_trace}
\end{equation}

Likewise, the transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\Bigl(e_{1i}M_{1i}+e_{2i}M_{2i}\Bigr),
\qquad
\beta
=
\frac12\Bigl(e_{2i}M_{1i}-e_{1i}M_{2i}\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_projector_trace}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual local Weyl/Dirac witness problem is reduced to the finite projected derivative data \(P_*K_iP_*\).

\section{Equivalent Shell-Tensor Form}

At the shell-tensor level, the same data are encoded by
\[
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\]
Then the shell-matching formulas give
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A
=
\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_j N^3_{ij},
}
\label{eq:lambda_tensor_protocol}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\kappa_*|G_*|B,
\qquad
\beta=\kappa_*|G_*|C.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_tensor_protocol}
\end{equation}
Hence the local Weyl criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:weyl_criterion_tensor_protocol}
\end{equation}

So the projector-trace formulation and the shell-tensor formulation are equivalent descriptions of the same extraction problem.

\section{Actual Longitudinal Extraction Protocol}

We may now state the protocol explicitly.

\begin{theorem}[Actual longitudinal extraction protocol]
Assume the full microscopic TECT linearization satisfies the hypotheses above.
Then the actual longitudinal coefficient is extracted by the following finite procedure:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the shell derivative operators
\[
K_i=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\]

\item Identify the low shell eigenspace \(H_*\) of \(L_*=L(G_*)\) and its projector \(P_*\).

\item Form the projected derivative matrices
\[
P_*K_iP_*\big|_{H_*}.
\]

\item Compute the Pauli-resolved coefficients
\[
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
\]

\item Contract with the shell axis:
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\hat n_iM_{3i}.
\]

\item Equivalently, read the shell tensor coefficient
\[
A=\hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij},
\]
and use
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|A.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus the actual longitudinal coefficient-identification problem is completely reduced to a finite projector-and-contraction computation.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Steps (1)--(4) follow from the first-order Taylor expansion and Pauli decomposition of the reduced \(2\times2\) shell Hamiltonian.
Step (5) follows by comparing the coefficient of the unique shell-compatible singlet term \(p_\parallel\sigma_3\).
Step (6) is the equivalent shell-tensor form already established by the shell-matching formulas.
\end{proof}

\section{Relation to the Local \(h_\parallel(\theta)\)-Formulation}

In the local defect-frame formulation, the projected transport kernel is written as
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
with
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\bigr].
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:lambda_local_protocol}
\end{equation}
Therefore the global shell extraction and the local defect-profile extraction are equivalent:
\[
P_*K_iP_*
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
h_\parallel(\theta).
\]

So the actual longitudinal extraction may be performed either:

\begin{enumerate}
\item globally, through the shell-projected momentum derivative \(P_*K_iP_*\), or
\item locally, through the \(n^\mu\sigma_3\)-coefficient of \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Matching to the Concrete \(g_c\)-Normalization}

Inside the concrete Class II/seed normalization, the longitudinal witness is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:gc_seed_protocol}
\end{equation}
Combining \eqref{eq:lambda_local_protocol} with \eqref{eq:gc_seed_protocol} gives the exact extraction formula
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c^{\mathrm{act}}
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:gc_actual_protocol}
\end{equation}

Thus once \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) is known, the actual longitudinal coefficient \(g_c^{\mathrm{act}}\) is fixed uniquely.

\section{What Is and Is Not Closed}

\begin{theorem}[Sharp honest status of the protocol]
At the present stage, the following statement is fully closed:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the actual longitudinal coefficient is extracted by a finite projector-trace-contraction protocol.}
}
\]

However, the following is still open:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the explicit computation of }K_i,\ P_*,\ M_{3i},
\text{ or equivalently }h_\parallel(\theta),
\text{ from the final complete microscopic TECT operator.}
}
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The closure of the protocol follows from the already established shell-level extraction theorem and the local \(h_\parallel\)-representation.
The non-closure follows from the project’s explicit honest status: the final complete microscopic TECT PDE and the actual microscopic values of \(g_c,g_E,g_O\) have not yet been fully extracted.
\end{proof}

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The actual longitudinal frontier is now completely localized.

It is no longer:
\[
\text{``solve the whole full PDE in one shot.''}
\]
It is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
L(k)\ \to\ K_i=\partial_{k_i}L|_{G_*}\ \to\ P_*K_iP_*\ \to\ M_{3i}\ \to\ \lambda_\parallel.
}
\]

Equivalently:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract } \hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij}
\quad\text{or}\quad
h_\parallel(\theta)
\text{ from the full microscopic TECT linearization.}
}
\]

\section{Unified Actual Extraction Theorem for \(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta\)}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now unify the longitudinal and transverse coefficient-identification problems into a single extraction theorem.
The point is that the full microscopic TECT linearization, once available, determines all three shell coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
through one and the same projected first-derivative dataset.

\section{Microscopic Linearization and Shell Projection}

Let the full microscopic TECT linearized operator around the condensed background be
\begin{equation}
i\partial_t\Phi=L(-i\nabla)\Phi.
\end{equation}
Fix a selected shell point
\[
G_*\neq 0,
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and expand around it:
\begin{equation}
k=G_*+p.
\end{equation}
Assume
\begin{equation}
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\qquad
L_*:=L(G_*),
\qquad
K_i:=\partial_{k_i}L(k)\big|_{k=G_*}.
\label{eq:unified_taylor}
\end{equation}

Assume further that \(L_*\) admits a two-dimensional low shell subspace
\[
H_*\subset H_{\mathrm{full}}
\]
with orthogonal projector
\[
P_*:H_{\mathrm{full}}\to H_*.
\]
Fix a Pauli basis on \(H_*\cong\mathbb C^2\):
\[
\mathrm{End}(H_*)=\mathrm{span}\{\mathbf 1_2,\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\}.
\]

The projected first-order shell Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
P_*(p_iK_i)P_*\big|_{H_*}.
\label{eq:unified_hlin}
\end{equation}

\section{Pauli-Resolved Coefficient Matrix}

Since \(h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)\) is Hermitian on \(H_*\), write
\begin{equation}
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)
=
a_0(p)\mathbf 1_2
+
a_\mu(p)\sigma_\mu,
\qquad
\mu=1,2,3.
\end{equation}
Define the Pauli-resolved projected derivative matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\mu i}
:=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
}
\label{eq:unified_Mmui}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
a_\mu(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i,
\qquad
h_+^{\mathrm{lin}}(p)=M_{\mu i}p_i\sigma_\mu.
\label{eq:unified_hM}
\end{equation}

Therefore all shell-level Weyl data are already contained in the finite set of matrices \(P_*K_iP_*\), equivalently in the numbers \(M_{\mu i}\).

\section{Matched \(S2\) Branch and Unified Coefficient Readout}

Choose the shell-adapted worldvolume frame
\[
p=p_\parallel \hat n+p_1e_1+p_2e_2.
\]
In the matched singlet\(\oplus\)doublet \(S2\) branch, the most general symmetry-compatible local symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\label{eq:unified_S2_symbol}
\end{equation}
Comparing \eqref{eq:unified_hM} with \eqref{eq:unified_S2_symbol}, one obtains the exact unified readout formulas
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\hat n_i\,M_{3i}
=
\frac12\,\hat n_i\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_3P_*K_iP_*\bigr),
}
\label{eq:unified_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac12\Bigl(e_{1i}M_{1i}+e_{2i}M_{2i}\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:unified_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac12\Bigl(e_{2i}M_{1i}-e_{1i}M_{2i}\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:unified_beta}
\end{equation}

Thus the full actual shell-coefficient problem is solved once \(M_{\mu i}\) is known.

\section{Equivalent Shell-Tensor Form}

Equivalently, write the minimal shell tensor ansatz
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=\frac{A}{\kappa_*|G_*|}\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=\frac{1}{\kappa_*|G_*|}(B\hat n_ie_{1j}+C\hat n_ie_{2j}),
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=\frac{1}{\kappa_*|G_*|}(-C\hat n_ie_{1j}+B\hat n_ie_{2j}).
\label{eq:unified_tensor_ansatz}
\end{equation}
Then the shell contractions are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\kappa_*|G_*|\,\hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij}=A,
}
\label{eq:unified_tensor_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\bigl(e_{1j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}+e_{2j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}\bigr)
=
B,
}
\label{eq:unified_tensor_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\frac{\kappa_*|G_*|}{2}
\bigl(e_{2j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}-e_{1j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}\bigr)
=
C.
}
\label{eq:unified_tensor_beta}
\end{equation}

Hence the projector-trace formulation and the shell-tensor formulation are equivalent.

\section{Equivalent Local Defect-Profile Form}

In the local defect/projector formulation, the first-order transport kernel is written as
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\end{equation}
Its shell-compatible invariant decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:unified_local_decomp}
\end{equation}
Then the three actual overlaps are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:unified_local_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:unified_local_alpha}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:unified_local_beta}
\end{equation}

So the global shell extraction and the local defect-profile extraction are the same coefficient-identification problem viewed in two different coordinates:
\[
P_*K_iP_*
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
N^a_{ij}
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O).
\]

\section{Unified Weyl Criterion}

The reduced shell crossing is Weyl exactly when
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:unified_Weyl_condition}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A\neq 0,
\qquad
(B,C)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:unified_ABC_condition}
\end{equation}
or, in shell-tensor form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat n_i\hat n_jN^3_{ij}\neq 0,
\qquad
\Bigl(
e_{1j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}+e_{2j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij},
\,
e_{2j}\hat n_iN^1_{ij}-e_{1j}\hat n_iN^2_{ij}
\Bigr)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:unified_tensor_condition}
\end{equation}

\section{Matching to the Concrete \(g_c,g_E,g_O\) Normalization}

Inside the concrete seed/Class II normalization,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\,g_O.
\label{eq:unified_gcgego_norm}
\end{equation}
Therefore the actual coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c^{\mathrm{act}}
=
-\frac{512}{3\sqrt3\pi\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3}
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
}
\label{eq:unified_gc_extract}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_E^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
g_O^{\mathrm{act}}
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)).
}
\label{eq:unified_gE_gO_extract}
\end{equation}

Thus all three actual shell coefficients are extracted by one unified protocol.

\section{Unified Extraction Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Unified actual extraction theorem]
Assume the full microscopic TECT linearization admits:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a shell expansion
\[
L(G_*+p)=L_*+p_iK_i+O(|p|^2),
\]
\item a two-dimensional low shell subspace \(H_*\) with projector \(P_*\),
\item the matched \(S2\) shell-compatible branch.
\end{enumerate}

Then the three actual shell coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
are determined uniquely and simultaneously by the projected derivative data \(P_*K_iP_*\), equivalently by the shell tensor \(N^a_{ij}\), equivalently by the local profile functions \((h_\parallel,h_E,h_O)\).

In particular:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\hat n_iM_{3i},
\qquad
\alpha
=
\frac12(e_{1i}M_{1i}+e_{2i}M_{2i}),
\qquad
\beta
=
\frac12(e_{2i}M_{1i}-e_{1i}M_{2i}),
\]
with
\[
M_{\mu i}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_iP_*\bigr).
\]
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The proof is immediate by comparing the Pauli decomposition of the projected first-order shell Hamiltonian with the unique symmetry-compatible \(S2\) reduced symbol.
The shell-tensor and local-profile forms follow by the already established shell matching and local overlap identities.
\end{proof}

\section{Sharp Honest Status}

What is now closed is the \emph{protocol}:
\[
\boxed{
L(k)\to K_i\to P_*K_iP_*\to M_{\mu i}\to (\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\]
What is still open is the \emph{actual execution} of this protocol for the final complete microscopic TECT operator:
\[
\boxed{
\text{explicit computation of }K_i,\ P_*,\ M_{\mu i}
\text{ (or equivalently }h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\text{) remains open.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Closed result.}
Once the full microscopic TECT linearization is available, the three shell coefficients

\qquad

g_O^{\mathrm{act}}

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
So what is now closed is the unified protocol.

\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad

\section{First Explicit Trial Calculation from the Minimal Complex-Triplet Brazovskii Candidate}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now perform the first honest explicit trial computation of the unified extraction protocol
\[
L(k)\ \to\ K_i=\partial_{k_i}L|_{G_*}\ \to\ P_*K_iP_*\ \to\ M_{\mu i}.
\]
The purpose is not to overclaim full microscopic closure, but to determine what the \emph{minimal isotropic candidate PDE} actually gives at the most naive shell-projected level.

\section{Minimal Microscopic Candidate}

Within the minimal local, isotropic, \(U(3)\)-invariant truncation, the microscopic TECT candidate is the complex-triplet Brazovskii wave equation
\begin{equation}
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi
+
Z\nabla^2\Psi
-
Y\nabla^4\Psi
-
g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi,
\qquad
\Psi:\mathbb R^{3,1}\to\mathbb C^3,
\label{eq:min_candidate_PDE}
\end{equation}
with
\[
Z<0,\qquad Y>0,\qquad g>0,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y}.
\]
This is the correct minimal microscopic candidate, but the actual shell-enriched witness coefficients are still stated to be open in the project documents. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\section{Naive Free-Shell Derivative Data}

Ignore for the moment the condensate periodicity and internal projector transport, and look only at the linear symbol of the candidate equation:
\begin{equation}
\omega^2(k)=\mu^2+Z|k|^2+Y|k|^4.
\label{eq:omega2_trial}
\end{equation}
Then the first shell derivative is
\begin{equation}
K_i^{\mathrm{free}}
:=
\partial_{k_i}\omega^2(k)\big|_{k=G_*}
=
\Bigl(2Z+4Y|G_*|^2\Bigr)G_{*i}.
\label{eq:Kfree_trial}
\end{equation}
Because \(|G_*|=q_*\) and \(q_*^2=-Z/(2Y)\),
\begin{equation}
2Z+4Yq_*^2
=
2Z+4Y\Bigl(-\frac{Z}{2Y}\Bigr)
=
0.
\label{eq:shell_cancel_1}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{free}}=0.
}
\label{eq:Kfree_zero}
\end{equation}

So at the pure free-shell level, the first derivative data vanish identically at the selected shell.

\section{Projected Consequence}

Let \(H_*\) be any two-dimensional low shell subspace and \(P_*\) its projector.
Then immediately,
\begin{equation}
P_*K_i^{\mathrm{free}}P_*=0.
\label{eq:PKP_free_zero}
\end{equation}
Therefore the Pauli-resolved coefficients
\begin{equation}
M_{\mu i}^{\mathrm{free}}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}_{H_*}\!\bigl(\sigma_\mu P_*K_i^{\mathrm{free}}P_*\bigr)
\end{equation}
all vanish:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\mu i}^{\mathrm{free}}=0.
}
\label{eq:Mfree_zero}
\end{equation}
Hence the shell coefficients extracted from the pure free-shell symbol are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{free}}=0,
\qquad
\alpha^{\mathrm{free}}=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{free}}=0.
}
\label{eq:free_coeffs_zero}
\end{equation}

So the naive free isotropic shell dispersion alone does not generate the Weyl witness.

\section{Stronger Check: Locked One-Mode Slow-Envelope Expansion}

We now refine the same conclusion by keeping the oscillatory shell background but still remaining in the locked one-mode isotropic truncation.

Take the background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0(x)=A\,e^{iG_*\cdot x}z_0,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger z_0=1,
\end{equation}
and a transverse fluctuation
\begin{equation}
\delta\Psi_\perp(x)=A\,e^{iG_*\cdot x}\chi(x),
\qquad
z_0^\dagger\chi=0.
\end{equation}
Introduce
\begin{equation}
D_{G_*}:=\nabla+iG_*.
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\nabla^2(e^{iG_*\cdot x}\chi)
=
e^{iG_*\cdot x}D_{G_*}^2\chi,
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
D_{G_*}^2
=
\nabla^2+2iG_*\cdot\nabla-q_*^2.
\end{equation}
Therefore the linear kinetic operator becomes
\begin{equation}
(Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4)\delta\Psi_\perp
=
A e^{iG_*\cdot x}
\Bigl[
Z D_{G_*}^2-Y(D_{G_*}^2)^2
\Bigr]\chi.
\end{equation}
Keeping only the terms linear in the slow envelope derivative \(\nabla\chi\),
\begin{equation}
D_{G_*}^2
=
-q_*^2+2iG_*\cdot\nabla+O(\nabla^2),
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
(D_{G_*}^2)^2
=
q_*^4-4iq_*^2\,G_*\cdot\nabla+O(\nabla^2).
\end{equation}
So the first-order transport coefficient is
\begin{equation}
2i\Bigl(Z+2Yq_*^2\Bigr)G_*\cdot\nabla.
\end{equation}
Using again \(q_*^2=-Z/(2Y)\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Z+2Yq_*^2=0.
}
\label{eq:shell_cancel_2}
\end{equation}
Hence the entire first-order kinetic transport term vanishes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[Z D_{G_*}^2-Y(D_{G_*}^2)^2\Bigr]_{\text{1st order}}=0.
}
\label{eq:kinetic_first_order_zero}
\end{equation}

Thus even after keeping the oscillatory shell phase, the locked one-mode isotropic kinetic truncation still gives no nontrivial first-order witness data.

\section{Interpretation of the Vanishing Result}

This vanishing result is not a contradiction.
It means that the actual shell witness cannot come from the free isotropic shell dispersion alone.
Therefore the nonzero first-order shell transport data must arise from more structured sectors, namely:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the local projector-defect transport matrix
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
whose coefficient functions \(a_i^\mu(\theta)\) remain open in the full microscopic theory;

\item the primitive longitudinal commutator-square channel
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu,
\]
which gives in the explicit representative
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0;
\]

\item the explicit transverse odd-gradient channels
\[
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
which already realize \((\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)\);

\item admissible mixed \((i,a)\)-carrier sectors such as Class II, whose concrete seed ansatz gives
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\]
\end{enumerate}

All of these structures are already established at the theorem/seed level, whereas the direct extraction from the final complete microscopic TECT operator remains open. :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9} :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\section{Explicit Trial Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[First explicit trial result for the minimal candidate PDE]
For the minimal complex-triplet Brazovskii candidate
\[
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi+Z\nabla^2\Psi-Y\nabla^4\Psi-g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi,
\]
the naive free-shell projected first-derivative data satisfy
\[
K_i^{\mathrm{free}}=0,
\qquad
P_*K_i^{\mathrm{free}}P_*=0,
\qquad
M_{\mu i}^{\mathrm{free}}=0,
\]
at the shell \(|G_*|=q_*\).

Moreover, in the locked one-mode isotropic slow-envelope expansion, the linear kinetic first-order transport coefficient also vanishes identically:
\[
Z+2Yq_*^2=0.
\]

Therefore the actual shell coefficients
\[
\lambda_\parallel,\qquad \alpha,\qquad \beta
\]
cannot be generated by the pure free isotropic shell dispersion alone.
They must come from nontrivial transport sectors beyond this naive truncation.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The free-shell vanishing follows from \eqref{eq:Kfree_trial} and the shell identity \eqref{eq:shell_cancel_1}.
The slow-envelope kinetic vanishing follows from \eqref{eq:shell_cancel_2}.
The projected consequences are immediate from the definitions of \(M_{\mu i}\), \(\lambda_\parallel\), \(\alpha\), and \(\beta\).
\end{proof}

\section{Sharp Honest Status}

This trial calculation proves something genuinely useful:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the first nontrivial microscopic Weyl data are not encoded in the bare isotropic shell dispersion alone.}
}
\]

So the actual microscopic coefficient-identification problem is sharply localized.
The next nontrivial calculation must be performed not on the free symbol \(\omega^2(k)\), but on one of the genuinely structured transport sectors:
\[
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta),
\qquad
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}},
\qquad
\text{or a mixed }(i,a)\text{-carrier realization.}
\]

This matches the current honest status of the project: the minimal candidate PDE is fixed, but the actual shell-enriched witness data extracted from it are still open. :contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of the First Explicit Trial Calculation}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
For the minimal complex-triplet Brazovskii candidate
\[
\partial_t^2\Psi
=
-\mu^2\Psi+Z\nabla^2\Psi-Y\nabla^4\Psi-g(\Psi^\dagger\Psi)\Psi,
\qquad
q_*^2=-\frac{Z}{2Y},
\]
the naive free-shell derivative data vanish at the selected shell:
\[
\boxed{
K_i^{\mathrm{free}}
=
\partial_{k_i}\omega^2(k)\big|_{k=G_*}
=
\bigl(2Z+4Yq_*^2\bigr)G_{*i}
=
0.
}
\]

Hence
\[
\boxed{
P_*K_i^{\mathrm{free}}P_*=0,
\qquad
M_{\mu i}^{\mathrm{free}}=0,
}
\]
so the pure free-shell dispersion gives
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{free}}=\alpha^{\mathrm{free}}=\beta^{\mathrm{free}}=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Stronger locked one-mode result.}
Even in the locked one-mode slow-envelope expansion,
\[
Z\nabla^2-Y\nabla^4
\]
produces a first-order transport coefficient proportional to
\[
Z+2Yq_*^2,
\]
which also vanishes exactly at the shell:
\[
\boxed{
Z+2Yq_*^2=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Meaning.}
Therefore the actual shell witness coefficients do \emph{not} come from the bare isotropic free-shell dispersion alone.
They must arise from more structured transport sectors, such as:

\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu,
\]
or an admissible mixed \((i,a)\)-carrier sector such as Class II.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
So the first explicit trial calculation closes the following statement:
\[
\boxed{
\text{free isotropic shell data alone are insufficient.}
}
\]
The next real microscopic calculation must therefore target the structured transport sector, not the bare shell dispersion.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{First Nontrivial Transport Trial Calculation in the Actual-Local Operator Class}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now perform the first nontrivial coefficient calculation inside the already-established actual-local transport class
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]
The purpose is not to claim that the final complete microscopic TECT coefficients have been extracted.
Rather, we compute what the leading shell witnesses look like under the most general invariant local transport ansatz.

\section{Actual-Local Structural Input}

The strongest honest local result already established is that the shell witness coefficients admit the overlap formulas
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:trial_lambda_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:trial_alpha_actual}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:trial_beta_actual}
\end{equation}
where the actual local transport matrix has the shell-compatible invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:trial_Minv}
\end{equation}

Thus the coefficient-identification problem is already reduced to the three scalar profile functions
\[
h_\parallel(\theta),\qquad h_E(\theta),\qquad h_O(\theta).
\]

\section{Leading Invariant Trial Ansatz}

Assume that the actual local transport matrix is real-analytic in the even defect profile \(\theta(\xi)\), so that the invariant coefficients admit expansions of the form
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta^4),
\label{eq:hparallel_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_E(\theta)
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_E^{(2)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta^4),
\label{eq:hE_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_O(\theta)
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_O^{(2)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta^4).
\label{eq:hO_expand}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
O(\theta^2).
}
\label{eq:M_trial_leading}
\end{equation}

This is the most general leading shell-compatible invariant trial ansatz inside the actual-local operator class.

\section{Leading-Order Witness Extraction}

Substituting \eqref{eq:hparallel_expand}--\eqref{eq:hO_expand} into \eqref{eq:trial_lambda_actual}--\eqref{eq:trial_beta_actual} gives
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
\underbrace{\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)}_{I_\theta}
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}
\underbrace{\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\theta(\xi)^2}_{I_{\theta^2\theta'}}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:lambda_trial_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)} I_\theta
+
\Lambda_E^{(2)} I_{\theta^2\theta'}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:alpha_trial_expand}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)} I_\theta
+
\Lambda_O^{(2)} I_{\theta^2\theta'}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa).
\label{eq:beta_trial_expand}
\end{equation}

The leading overlap integral
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
:=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
\end{equation}
has already been evaluated explicitly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\neq 0
\qquad
(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0).
}
\label{eq:Itheta_trial}
\end{equation}

Therefore the leading trial coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)} I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
}
\label{eq:lambda_trial_leading}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)} I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)} I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
}
\label{eq:ab_trial_leading}
\end{equation}

\section{Leading Weyl Criterion in the Trial Local Ansatz}

The shell-reduced Weyl condition is
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]
Using \eqref{eq:lambda_trial_leading}--\eqref{eq:ab_trial_leading}, one gets the leading-order criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\qquad
\bigl(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)}\bigr)\neq (0,0)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\ (\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
}
\label{eq:leading_trial_Weyl}
\end{equation}
for a nontrivial defect profile \(\theta_0\kappa\neq 0\).

Thus the first nontrivial transport trial shows that a nonzero invariant constant coefficient in the actual-local transport matrix is already sufficient to generate the shell Weyl witness at leading order.

\section{Relation to the Explicit Seed Branch}

The explicit seed representative obtained earlier is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:seed_parallel_trial}
\end{equation}
This corresponds not to a constant leading \(h_\parallel\), but to an even profile behaving schematically as
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)\sim \theta'(\xi)^2,
\]
hence its overlap is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
\label{eq:seed_parallel_I3_trial}
\end{equation}

So there are two logically distinct branches:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the \textbf{leading constant-invariant trial branch}, where
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta^2),
\]
and therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta+O(\theta_0^3\kappa);
\]

\item the \textbf{primitive commutator-square branch}, where
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)\sim \theta'^2,
\]
and therefore
\[
\lambda_\parallel\sim I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
\end{enumerate}

The first branch is the most general leading local transport trial.
The second branch is the explicit geometrically natural primitive seed already constructed inside the concrete ansatz space.

\section{What This Trial Does and Does Not Prove}

\begin{theorem}[First nontrivial transport trial theorem]
Inside the actual-local transport class
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
the most general leading shell-compatible invariant ansatz
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
O(\theta^2)
\]
gives the leading-order shell witnesses
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\]
Hence a nonzero leading invariant coefficient already yields a nontrivial Weyl witness.

However, this does \emph{not} prove that the actual full microscopic TECT linearization produces nonzero values of
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\quad \Lambda_E^{(0)},\quad \Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]
That microscopic coefficient extraction remains open.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The coefficient formulas follow immediately from the actual local overlap formulas and the explicit nonvanishing of \(I_\theta\).
The final caveat follows from the current honest project status: the actual microscopic functions \(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\) have not yet been extracted from the final full TECT operator.
\end{proof}

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The first nontrivial transport trial calculation proves the following:

\[
\boxed{
\text{if the actual local transport matrix has a nonzero leading invariant coefficient,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{then the shell Weyl witness already appears at order }I_\theta\sim \theta_0\kappa.
}
\]

This is stronger than the free-shell trial, where all first-derivative shell data vanished identically.
But it still does not identify the true microscopic TECT coefficient point.

So the next real microscopic task is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{determine whether the actual complete TECT linearization produces }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\ \Lambda_E^{(0)},\ \Lambda_O^{(0)}
\text{ or instead starts only at higher even order in }\theta.
}
\]

\section{Final Summary of the First Nontrivial Transport Trial}

\paragraph{Closed result.}
Inside the actual-local transport class
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
take the most general leading shell-compatible invariant ansatz
\[
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
\Lambda_0^{(0)}\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E^{(0)}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
O(\theta^2).
\]
Then the leading shell witnesses are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
}
\]
Since
\[
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa
\neq 0,
\]
a nonzero leading invariant coefficient already yields a nontrivial Weyl witness.

\paragraph{Important distinction.}
This leading transport trial is \emph{not} the same as the explicit primitive longitudinal seed branch.
In the primitive branch,
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
so
\[
\lambda_\parallel\sim I_{\theta'^3},
\]
not \(I_\theta\).

Thus:
\[
\boxed{
\text{constant-leading local transport branch } \neq \text{ primitive commutator-square branch.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Honest status.}
What is now proved is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{if nonzero leading invariant coefficients are present, the Weyl witness appears already at order }I_\theta.
}
\]
What is still open is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the actual complete TECT linearization produce }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\ \Lambda_E^{(0)},\ \Lambda_O^{(0)}
\text{, or does it begin only at higher even order?}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Leading-Order Selection Theorem for the Actual Local Transport Branch}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now determine, as sharply as the current documents allow, whether the actual shell-compatible local transport matrix begins at constant invariant order
\[
\Lambda^{(0)}
\]
or whether some channels are forced to begin only at higher primitive order.

The correct answer is branch-sensitive:
the broad actual-local operator class and the concrete exact Class II transport branch do \emph{not} impose the same leading-order selection.

\section{Broad Actual-Local Operator Class}

The strongest general local form already justified is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\in \mathrm{Herm}(Q_B).
\label{eq:LOST_Vmu}
\end{equation}
With the minimal even-\(\theta\) expansion,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)
=
\Lambda_0^{\ \mu}\mathbf 1_2
+
\Lambda_i^{\ \mu}\sigma_i
+
O(\theta^2),
\label{eq:LOST_Mmu_expand}
\end{equation}
the shell-compatible invariant decomposition reads
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:LOST_Minv}
\end{equation}
Hence the corresponding leading coefficients are
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta^2),
\qquad
h_E(\theta)=\Lambda_E^{(0)}+O(\theta^2),
\qquad
h_O(\theta)=\Lambda_O^{(0)}+O(\theta^2).
\label{eq:LOST_h_expand}
\end{equation}

The actual overlap formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)),
\label{eq:LOST_lambda}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_E(\theta(\xi)),
\qquad
\beta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,h_O(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:LOST_ab}
\end{equation}
Therefore, at leading order,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\alpha
=
\Lambda_E^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\qquad
\beta
=
\Lambda_O^{(0)} I_\theta + O(\theta_0^3\kappa),
\label{eq:LOST_leading_general}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\theta_0\kappa
\neq 0.
\label{eq:LOST_Itheta}
\end{equation}

Thus, in the broad actual-local operator class, none of the three leading invariant coefficients is symmetry-forbidden.

\begin{theorem}[Non-forbiddance of constant leading coefficients]
Inside the broad shell-compatible actual-local operator class \eqref{eq:LOST_Vmu}--\eqref{eq:LOST_Mmu_expand}, the coefficients
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\qquad \Lambda_E^{(0)},\qquad \Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]
are all allowed by the residual local symmetry.
In particular, the general local structure does not force any of them to vanish.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The matched local \(S2\) branch contains the invariant singlet and doublet structures
\[
n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]
Therefore constant coefficients multiplying these structures are symmetry-allowed.
Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\), any nonzero such coefficient contributes بالفعل to the corresponding shell witness at leading order.
\end{proof}

\paragraph{Explicit realizable point in the same operator class.}
The same actual-local operator class already contains an explicit full-rank realizable point:
\begin{equation}
M^1=I_g\sigma_1,\qquad
M^2=I_g\sigma_2,\qquad
M^3=I_g\sigma_3,
\qquad
I_g\neq 0.
\label{eq:LOST_explicit_fullrank}
\end{equation}
This shows that the local operator class itself certainly allows a nonzero constant-leading \(\sigma_3\) coefficient. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

\section{Concrete Exact Class II Branch}

The exact concrete Class II witness formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:LOST_ClassII_exact}
\end{equation}
The transverse seeds are
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:LOST_transverse_seeds}
\end{equation}
so the transverse witness lives at \(I_\theta\)-order.

By contrast, the longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:LOST_long_seed}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3\neq 0.
\label{eq:LOST_Itheta3}
\end{equation}

Therefore the concrete Class II branch exhibits a genuine mismatch of origin:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{transverse sector: }I_\theta\text{-type leading branch;}
\qquad
\text{longitudinal sector: primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{-type branch.}
}
\label{eq:LOST_mismatch}
\end{equation}

\begin{theorem}[Exact leading-order selection inside the concrete Class II branch]
Inside the exact concrete Class II transport realization,
\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse witness sector begins at \(I_\theta\)-order:
\[
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,\qquad \beta=g_O I_\theta;
\]
\item the longitudinal witness does \emph{not} begin at \(I_\theta\)-order;
instead its first nonzero contribution is the primitive channel
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
\end{enumerate}
Equivalently, the \(I_\theta\)-type constant-leading longitudinal branch is absent in the exact concrete Class II witness formulas.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
This is exactly the content of \eqref{eq:LOST_ClassII_exact}, together with the explicit primitive longitudinal seed \eqref{eq:LOST_long_seed}.
The transverse sector is generated by the odd-gradient seeds \eqref{eq:LOST_transverse_seeds}, while the longitudinal sector is generated by the commutator-square seed and therefore starts at \(\theta'^3\).
\end{proof}

\section{Branch-Sensitive Honest Conclusion}

We may now state the sharpest honest leading-order selection statement available at present.

\begin{theorem}[Branch-sensitive leading-order selection theorem]
At the current stage of the TECT proof chain:

\begin{enumerate}
\item In the broad actual-local operator class,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)},\ \Lambda_E^{(0)},\ \Lambda_O^{(0)}
\]
are all symmetry-allowed and none is forced to vanish.

\item In the exact currently constructed concrete Class II branch, the transverse coefficients begin at \(I_\theta\)-order, while the longitudinal coefficient begins only at the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\)-order.

\item Therefore the documents do \emph{not} yet determine whether the actual complete microscopic TECT coefficient point lies in:
\[
\text{(A) a constant-leading local branch,}
\qquad
\text{or}
\qquad
\text{(B) the primitive longitudinal branch.}
\]
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Item (1) follows from the general local invariant decomposition and the explicit realizable full-rank point inside the same operator class.
Item (2) follows from the exact concrete Class II witness formulas.
Item (3) follows from the project’s explicit honest status: the actual microscopic functions \(a_i^\mu(\theta)\), equivalently \(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\), have not yet been extracted from the final complete TECT linearization.
\end{proof}

\section{Interpretation for the Actual Full TECT Frontier}

The remaining microscopic question is now much sharper than before.

\quad\text{or}\quad

\text{ with first nonzero term in the primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{ branch.}

\label{eq:LOST_actual_audit}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{What is now closed.}

\paragraph{Broad actual-local operator class.}

\quad\text{or}\quad

\section{Two-Branch Longitudinal Decision Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now convert the longitudinal leading-order ambiguity into an explicit decision protocol.
The issue is not whether a longitudinal witness can exist in principle.
That is already established.
The actual unresolved question is only which branch the complete microscopic TECT transport extraction realizes:

\[
\text{Branch A: constant-leading }I_\theta\text{-type longitudinal branch},
\]
or
\[
\text{Branch B: primitive }I_{\theta'^3}\text{-type longitudinal branch}.
\]

\section{General Actual-Local Longitudinal Expansion}

The strongest honest local transport form already established is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\,\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\end{equation}
with shell-compatible invariant decomposition
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_0(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_\parallel(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_E(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_O(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:TB_hdecomp}
\end{equation}
The actual longitudinal overlap is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)\,h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
\label{eq:TB_lambda_general}
\end{equation}

Assume the even-\(\theta\) expansion
\begin{equation}
h_\parallel(\theta)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}\theta^2
+
O(\theta^4).
\label{eq:TB_hpar_expand}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta
+
\Lambda_\parallel^{(2)}I_{\theta^2\theta'}
+
O(\theta_0^5\kappa),
\label{eq:TB_lambda_expand}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
I_\theta
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)
\neq 0.
\label{eq:TB_Itheta}
\end{equation}

Thus, if
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\label{eq:TB_const_nonzero}
\end{equation}
then the longitudinal witness already survives on the constant-leading branch:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
}
\label{eq:TB_branchA}
\end{equation}

\section{Primitive Longitudinal Branch}

The exact primitive longitudinal seed already established in the concrete seed/Class II construction is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:TB_primitive_seed}
\end{equation}
Its projected witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:TB_branchB}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the concrete Class II coefficients,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{g_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\label{eq:TB_gc_branch}
\end{equation}

This is the exact primitive branch.
It does \emph{not} begin at \(I_\theta\)-order.

\section{Transverse Sector Is Already Resolved}

The transverse witness sector is already explicitly realized in the same concrete seed/Class II framework:
\begin{equation}
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
\label{eq:TB_transverse}
\end{equation}
Hence the actual remaining branch ambiguity is purely longitudinal.

\section{Decision Functional for the Constant-Leading Branch}

Define the constant-leading longitudinal projector by
\begin{equation}
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
:=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].
\label{eq:TB_const_projector}
\end{equation}
This is the unique shell-compatible constant longitudinal invariant coefficient.

If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\), then the decision is finished:
the actual full TECT local transport extraction lies in the constant-leading longitudinal branch.

If instead
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
one must continue to the primitive-channel audit.

\section{Decision Functional for the Primitive Branch}

If the constant-leading coefficient vanishes, define the primitive longitudinal coefficient \(\lambda_c\) by the factorization
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu.
\label{eq:TB_lambda_c_factor}
\end{equation}
Then the primitive overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:TB_lambda_c_overlap}
\end{equation}
Hence:

\begin{equation}
\lambda_c\neq 0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
\quad\text{on the primitive branch.}
\label{eq:TB_primitive_nonzero}
\end{equation}

\section{Two-Branch Decision Theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Two-branch longitudinal decision theorem]
Assume the actual full microscopic TECT transport extraction has already been reduced to the shell-compatible local form
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)).
\]
Then the longitudinal witness decision is the following finite branch test:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the constant-leading longitudinal invariant coefficient
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].
\]

\item If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
then the actual longitudinal witness lies on the constant-leading branch:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta
+
O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\]

\item If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
then inspect the primitive longitudinal channel
\[
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\lambda_c\,
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu.
\]

\item If
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\]
then the longitudinal witness lies on the primitive branch:
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\item If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\quad\text{and}\quad
\lambda_c=0,
\]
then the currently established two branches both fail, and one must either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item search for a higher even-order longitudinal branch, or
\item conclude that the longitudinal witness is absent in that microscopic realization.
\end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The constant-leading branch follows from the general local expansion
\[
h_\parallel(\theta)=\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}+O(\theta^2)
\]
and the overlap identity
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta' h_\parallel(\theta(\xi)).
\]
Since \(I_\theta\neq 0\), a nonzero \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\) produces a nonzero longitudinal witness at leading order.

If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\), the first currently established concrete longitudinal realization is the primitive channel
\[
\theta'(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}n^\mu,
\]
whose projected overlap is exactly
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]
Since \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), nonzero \(\lambda_c\) implies nonzero longitudinal witness on the primitive branch.

If both coefficients vanish, the current theorem-level construction does not determine a nonzero longitudinal witness, so further higher-order structure would need to be audited explicitly.
\end{proof}

\section{Branch-Sensitive Honest Status}

The strongest honest conclusion is not that one of the branches has already been microscopically selected by complete TECT.
Rather, the documents imply:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the broad actual-local operator class allows a constant-leading longitudinal branch;
\item the exact currently constructed concrete Class II witness formulas realize the primitive longitudinal branch;
\item the actual full microscopic TECT coefficient point has not yet been extracted, so the final branch choice remains open.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the actual remaining microscopic audit is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\stackrel{?}{\neq}0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\text{ with }\lambda_c\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\label{eq:TB_final_audit}
\end{equation}

\section{Practical Decision Protocol}

The concrete execution order is:

\paragraph{Step A.}
Extract the shell-compatible local transport matrix \(\mathcal M^\mu(\theta)\) from the full microscopic linearization.

\paragraph{Step B.}
Compute
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].
\]

\paragraph{Step C.}
If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\), stop.
The actual longitudinal witness is already present at \(I_\theta\)-order.

\paragraph{Step D.}
If \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\), project onto the primitive channel
\[
\theta'(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}n^\mu
\]
and extract \(\lambda_c\).

\paragraph{Step E.}
If \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), stop.
The actual longitudinal witness is present on the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\)-branch.

\paragraph{Step F.}
If both vanish, the current theorem-level branch audit remains inconclusive and one must inspect higher-order longitudinal channels explicitly.

If

Define the quadratic traceless \(Q_B\)-response

:=

S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\sigma_3,

on the primitive branch.

\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0

=

\section{Unified Decision Tree}

The two branches combine into one finite decision tree.

\begin{theorem}[Unified longitudinal audit protocol]
Assume the actual full microscopic TECT transport kernel has been reduced to the local shell-compatible form \eqref{eq:ULAP_Vmu}--\eqref{eq:ULAP_Minv}.
Then the longitudinal audit is performed in the following order:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the constant-leading coefficient
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\,\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].
\]

\item If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,
\]
stop:
the actual theory is on Branch A, and
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}I_\theta+O(\theta_0^3\kappa).
\]

\item If
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
compute the primitive quadratic \(Q_B\)-response \(S_\xi\) and the primitive coefficient \(\lambda_c\).

\item If
\[
\lambda_c\neq 0,
\]
stop:
the actual theory is on Branch B, and
\[
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
\]

\item If both
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\lambda_c=0,
\]
then the current theorem-level audit is inconclusive at these two established branches, and one must inspect higher even-order longitudinal channels explicitly.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Branch A follows from the even expansion of \(h_\parallel(\theta)\) and the nonvanishing of \(I_\theta\).
Branch B follows from the primitive commutator-square seed and the nonvanishing of \(I_{\theta'^3}\).
If both fail, the currently established branch library contains no nonzero longitudinal seed, so additional higher-order structures must be audited separately.
\end{proof}

\section{What Is Actually Closed and What Remains Open}

\begin{theorem}[Sharp honest status]
At the present stage, the following is closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the longitudinal witness problem is reduced to a two-branch finite decision protocol.}
}
\label{eq:ULAP_closed}
\end{equation}

What remains open is the actual full microscopic input:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the complete microscopic TECT transport extraction has not yet determined whether }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\text{ or instead }
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
\text{ with }
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:ULAP_open}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The broad actual-local operator class allows a constant-leading longitudinal coefficient.
The exact concrete Class II formulas realize the primitive longitudinal branch.
But the actual full microscopic coefficient functions \(h_\parallel,h_E,h_O\) have not yet been extracted from the final complete TECT operator, so the actual branch selection remains open.
\end{proof}

\]
to extract \(\lambda_c\).

\paragraph{(U5)}
If \(\lambda_c\neq 0\), conclude Branch B and stop.

\paragraph{(U6)}
If both vanish, inspect higher-order longitudinal channels.

\section{Final Microscopic Witness Audit Protocol}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now combine the transverse audit and the branch-sensitive longitudinal audit into a single final microscopic witness protocol.
The purpose is to state the exact finite test that the complete microscopic TECT linearization must satisfy in order for the selected shell crossing to be Weyl.

\section{Witness Criterion at the Shell-Reduced Level}

The local shell-reduced Weyl criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_weyl_criterion}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, in the shell-tensor language,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(W_I,W_J)\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_witness_criterion}
\end{equation}
and the corresponding local Weyl determinant is
\begin{equation}
\det M
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
W_\parallel\bigl(W_I^2+W_J^2\bigr).
\label{eq:FMWAP_detM}
\end{equation}

Thus the microscopic witness audit is complete exactly when one longitudinal witness and one transverse witness survive.

\section{Actual Microscopic Extraction Chain}

The full microscopic extraction chain is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_B(\xi)
\ \Longrightarrow\
V^\mu(\xi)
\ \Longrightarrow\
u_a^\pm
\ \Longrightarrow\
(M^\mu)_{ab}
\ \Longrightarrow\
P_*K_iP_*
\ \Longrightarrow\
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_protocol_chain}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, one may formulate the same extraction at the tensor level:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{\mathrm{micro}}
\subset
W=\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}\otimes \mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}\otimes U_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\end{equation}
and for each required channel \(\alpha\in\{\parallel,I,J\}\), define the shell target covector
\[
T^{(\alpha)}.
\]
Then the channel survives iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
P_VT^{(\alpha)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_projection_test}
\end{equation}

So the witness problem is no longer an infinite-dimensional PDE mystery.
It is a finite projection / seed-embedding audit.

\section{Transverse Audit}

The exact currently established concrete Class II formulas give
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=g_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=g_O I_\theta,
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_transverse_exact}

Therefore the transverse sector survives iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_transverse_condition}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, it is enough to produce one admissible transverse seed tensor \(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp)}\in V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det T_\perp\bigl(N_{\mathrm{seed}}^{(\perp)}\bigr)\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:FMWAP_transverse_seed}
\end{equation}
or in explicit witness language,
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

Inside the concrete seed space, two canonical transverse seeds are already known:
\[
N^{(\perp,E)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\qquad
N^{(\perp,O)}_{\mathrm{seed}},
\]
giving
\[
\alpha=I_\theta,\ \beta=0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
\alpha=0,\ \beta=I_\theta.
\]

Hence the transverse witness sector is already explicitly closed inside the concrete ansatz space.

\section{Longitudinal Audit: Two-Branch Decision}

The longitudinal sector is branch-sensitive.

\subsection*{Branch A: constant-leading branch}

From the actual local transport extraction
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)\mathcal M^\mu(\theta(\xi)),
\]
define the constant-leading longitudinal coefficient
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}
=
\frac12\mathrm{Tr}\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\mathcal M^\mu(0)\bigr].

If

\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0,

then the longitudinal witness is already present at \(I_\theta\)-order:

=

+

\subsection*{Branch B: primitive branch}

If
\[

V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu,

\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B].

Factor its actual coefficient as

=

\label{eq:FMWAP_branchB_result}

Hence if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq 0,

\label{eq:FMWAP_branchB_cond}
\end{equation}
the longitudinal witness survives on the primitive branch.

\subsection*{Longitudinal decision rule}

Therefore the longitudinal sector survives iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\bigl[\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\ \text{and}\ \lambda_c\neq 0\bigr].

\label{eq:FMWAP_longitudinal_condition}
\end{equation}

\section{Unified Final Witness Protocol}

Combining the transverse and longitudinal conditions, the full microscopic witness audit succeeds iff
\begin{equation}

(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\quad\text{and}\quad
\bigl[\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0
\ \text{or}\

Equivalently, in seed language, it is sufficient to find:
\begin{enumerate}

\item one admissible longitudinal seed direction, either:
\begin{enumerate}

\item a primitive commutator-square seed with \(\lambda_c\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}

\begin{theorem}[Final microscopic witness audit theorem]
Let \(V_{\mathrm{micro}}\) be the actual symmetry-allowed transport tensor space extracted from the full microscopic TECT linearization.
Assume:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the transverse sector contains one admissible seed with \((\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)\);
\item the longitudinal sector satisfies either:
\begin{enumerate}
\item Branch A: \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0\), or
\item Branch B: \(\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0\) and \(\lambda_c\neq 0\).
\end{enumerate}
\end{enumerate}

Then the shell-reduced Weyl witness condition
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)
\]
holds, and the selected shell crossing is Weyl.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The transverse part is immediate from \eqref{eq:FMWAP_transverse_exact}.
The longitudinal part follows from the two-branch decision theorem:
either a constant-leading \(I_\theta\)-type longitudinal coefficient survives, or else the primitive \(I_{\theta'^3}\)-type coefficient survives.
In either case \(\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\).
Combining the two gives the Weyl condition \eqref{eq:FMWAP_weyl_criterion}.
\end{proof}

\section{Practical Output of the Protocol}

The full microscopic witness protocol produces four logically distinct outputs:

V(0)=0,\qquad
\Delta>0,\qquad
\text{mass protection},\qquad
M_Z.

\section{Opposite-Valley Matching Theorem}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now close the exact relation between the two shell valleys \(+G_*\) and \(-G_*\).
The point is to show that opposite-valley pairing is not an additional vague dynamical requirement, but a finite matched-frame equality of the witness triples.

\section{Local Weyl Blocks at the Two Valleys}

Let \(h_+(p)\) and \(h_-(p)\) denote the shell-projected \(2\times 2\) Weyl blocks at the two opposite valleys \(+G_*\) and \(-G_*\), respectively.

Choose an adapted frame at \(+G_*\):
\[
\hat n_+ = \frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_{1+},e_{2+},\hat n_+\}.
\]
At the opposite valley we choose the matched frame
\[
\hat n_- = -\hat n_+,
\qquad
e_{1-}=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}=e_{2+},
\]
or any equivalent consistently matched choice.

Then the two local Weyl blocks have the form
\begin{equation}
h_+(p)
=
W^+_\parallel\,p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
W^+_I\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
W^+_J\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:OVM_hplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
h_-(p)
=
W^-_\parallel\,p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
W^-_I\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
W^-_J\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:OVM_hminus}
\end{equation}
where the coefficients are the witness triples extracted in the matched frames.

\section{Matched Witness Triples}

Define the positive-valley witness functionals by
\begin{equation}
W^+_\parallel[N]
:=
\hat n_{+i}\hat n_{+j}N^3_{ij}(+),
\label{eq:OVM_Wp_par}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^+_I[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1+j}\hat n_{+i}N^1_{ij}(+)
+
e_{2+j}\hat n_{+i}N^2_{ij}(+)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:OVM_Wp_I}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^+_J[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1+j}\hat n_{+i}N^2_{ij}(+)
-
e_{2+j}\hat n_{+i}N^1_{ij}(+)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:OVM_Wp_J}
\end{equation}
and analogously the negative-valley matched-frame witness functionals
\begin{equation}
W^-_\parallel[N]
:=
\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j}N^3_{ij}(-),
\label{eq:OVM_Wm_par}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^-_I[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N^1_{ij}(-)
+
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N^2_{ij}(-)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:OVM_Wm_I}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W^-_J[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1-j}\hat n_{-i}N^2_{ij}(-)
-
e_{2-j}\hat n_{-i}N^1_{ij}(-)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:OVM_Wm_J}
\end{equation}

The opposite-valley matching condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W^-_\parallel,W^-_I,W^-_J)
=
(W^+_\parallel,W^+_I,W^+_J).
}
\label{eq:OVM_match_condition}
\end{equation}

\section{Why Matched Equality Implies Opposite-Valley Pairing}

\begin{theorem}[Matched witness equality implies opposite-valley pairing]
Assume the two shell-projected Weyl blocks are written in matched opposite-valley frames and satisfy
\[
(W^-_\parallel,W^-_I,W^-_J)
=
(W^+_\parallel,W^+_I,W^+_J).
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_-(p)=-\,h_+(-p).
}
\label{eq:OVM_pairing_relation}
\end{equation}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Using \eqref{eq:OVM_hplus},
\begin{align}
-h_+(-p)
&=
- \Bigl[
W^+_\parallel(-p_\parallel)\sigma_3
+
W^+_I\bigl((-p_1)\sigma_1+(-p_2)\sigma_2\bigr)
+
W^+_J\bigl(-(-p_2)\sigma_1+(-p_1)\sigma_2\bigr)
\Bigr]
\\
&=
W^+_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
W^+_I(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
W^+_J(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
\end{align}
If the matched witness triples are equal,
\[
W^-_\parallel=W^+_\parallel,
\qquad
W^-_I=W^+_I,
\qquad
W^-_J=W^+_J,
\]
then the right-hand side is exactly \(h_-(p)\) as written in \eqref{eq:OVM_hminus}.
Hence
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p).
\]
\end{proof}

\section{Dirac Doubling}

Define the doubled valley spinor
\[
\Phi=
\begin{pmatrix}
\phi_+\\
\phi_-
\end{pmatrix}\in\mathbb C^4.
\]
Then the doubled local Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
h_+(p) & 0\\
0 & h_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:OVM_HD}
\end{equation}
Under the pairing relation \eqref{eq:OVM_pairing_relation}, after a suitable basis choice this becomes
\begin{equation}
H_D(q)=
\begin{pmatrix}
q_i\sigma_i & 0\\
0 & -q_i\sigma_i
\end{pmatrix}
=
\sum_{i=1}^3 q_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\label{eq:OVM_Dirac_block}
\end{equation}
which is the massless Dirac Hamiltonian.

\begin{corollary}[Opposite-valley matching yields local Dirac doubling]
If each valley is Weyl and the matched witness triples are equal, then the doubled local shell block is Dirac.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Weyl at each valley gives the two \(2\times2\) blocks.
The matching relation gives the standard opposite-valley doubling
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
\]
and then \eqref{eq:OVM_HD} is exactly a doubled Dirac block.
\end{proof}

\section{Concrete Class II Seed Family}

Inside the concrete Class II seed family, the induced shell tensors at \(+G_*\) and \(-G_*\) take the matched-frame forms
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}(+)
=
-\mu c_\parallel\,\hat n_{+i}\hat n_{+j},
\qquad
\delta N^1_{ij}(+)
=
-\mu\bigl(c_I\hat n_{+i}e_{1+j}+c_J\hat n_{+i}e_{2+j}\bigr),
\qquad
\delta N^2_{ij}(+)
=
-\mu\bigl(-c_J\hat n_{+i}e_{1+j}+c_I\hat n_{+i}e_{2+j}\bigr),
\label{eq:OVM_plus_seed}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}(-)
=
-\mu c_\parallel\,\hat n_{-i}\hat n_{-j},
\qquad
\delta N^1_{ij}(-)
=
-\mu\bigl(c_I\hat n_{-i}e_{1-j}+c_J\hat n_{-i}e_{2-j}\bigr),
\qquad
\delta N^2_{ij}(-)
=
-\mu\bigl(-c_J\hat n_{-i}e_{1-j}+c_I\hat n_{-i}e_{2-j}\bigr).
\label{eq:OVM_minus_seed}
\end{equation}
Therefore the witness triples agree identically in the matched frames:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W^-_\parallel,W^-_I,W^-_J)
=
(W^+_\parallel,W^+_I,W^+_J).
}
\label{eq:OVM_seed_matching}
\end{equation}

So opposite-valley matching is already closed inside the concrete seed/Class II realization.

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The opposite-valley matching problem has now been reduced to a finite equality test.

\begin{theorem}[Opposite-valley matching theorem]
At the shell-reduced level, opposite-valley pairing is equivalent to the matched-frame equality of the witness triples:
\[
\boxed{
(W^-_\parallel,W^-_I,W^-_J)
=
(W^+_\parallel,W^+_I,W^+_J).
}
\]
When this holds, one has
\[
\boxed{
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
}
\]
and therefore the doubled local shell block is Dirac.

Inside the concrete Class II seed family, this matching is already satisfied identically.
\end{theorem}

\paragraph{What remains open.}
What is still not yet fully extracted microscopically is whether the \emph{actual full microscopic TECT} realization produces the same matched witness triple at both valleys.
So the remaining audit is not conceptual; it is the explicit finite comparison:
\[
\boxed{
(W^-_\parallel,W^-_I,W^-_J)\stackrel{?}{=}(W^+_\parallel,W^+_I,W^+_J)
}
\]
in the final complete microscopic extraction.
