\section{First Actual Calculation in the Graded \(2+2\) Bypass Route}

\paragraph{Goal.}
We now stop discussing cancellation inside the plain scalar Bragg-pair block and move entirely to the graded \(2+2\) bypass mechanism.

The objective is to compute explicitly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item why the dangerous constant scalar Bragg block does not appear in the relevant graded principal operator;
\item the determinant and spectrum of the graded first-order reduced operator;
\item the exact finite nondegeneracy condition that replaces the old \(B_0\)-cancellation problem.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Graded \(2+2\) Low-Energy Sector}

Let
\[
K=K_+\oplus K_-,
\qquad
\dim_{\mathbb C}K_\pm=2,
\]
and let \(J\) be the grading involution
\begin{equation}
J^\dagger=J,
\qquad
J^2=1,
\qquad
J|_{K_\pm}=\pm 1.
\label{eq:graded_J_def}
\end{equation}
Let the reduced effective operator be
\begin{equation}
D_{\mathrm{eff}}(p)=\Pi_K L(p)\Pi_K = D_1(p)+O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:graded_Deff}
\end{equation}
and assume the leading term is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item first-order in momentum,
\item \(J\)-odd:
\begin{equation}
JD_1(p)J^{-1}=-D_1(p).
\label{eq:graded_Jodd}
\end{equation}
\end{enumerate}

Then in the \(J\)-graded basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
}
\label{eq:graded_block_form}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_i M_i.
\label{eq:A1_piMi}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the theorem-level graded bypass setup already established in the manuscripts.

\section{Why the Scalar Bragg Mass Is Absent Here}

The dangerous scalar obstruction in the plain shell-pair route was
\[
B_0^{\mathrm{tot}}\,\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
which is momentum-independent.

But in the graded bypass route, the relevant principal infrared operator is by definition first-order:
\[
A_1(p)=p_iM_i.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(0)=0,
\qquad
D_1(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:graded_D1_zero}
\end{equation}

So the scalar Bragg block is not cancelled inside \(D_1\); it is absent because the graded principal operator starts at first order in momentum.
This is the precise meaning of the bypass mechanism.

\section{General \(2\times2\) Mixed Symbol}

Write the mixed symbol in Pauli form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\ell_0(p)\,\mathbf 1_2
+
\ell_1(p)\,\sigma_1
+
\ell_2(p)\,\sigma_2
+
\ell_3(p)\,\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:A1_Pauli}
\end{equation}
where each coefficient is linear in momentum:
\begin{equation}
\ell_\alpha(p)=C_\alpha^{\ i}p_i,
\qquad
\alpha=0,1,2,3.
\label{eq:ell_linear}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
p_i
\Bigl(
C_0^{\ i}\mathbf 1_2 + C_a^{\ i}\sigma_a
\Bigr).
\label{eq:A1_Ccoeff}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Important point.}
The identity part
\[
\ell_0(p)\mathbf 1_2
\]
is not a mass obstruction, because it is still linear in \(p\).
The manuscripts already state this explicitly: the identity component is principal-level irrelevant once the full symbol is nondegenerate. 

\section{Exact Determinant Calculation}

For any \(2\times2\) matrix of the form
\[
A=\ell_0\mathbf 1_2+\ell_a\sigma_a,
\]
the standard Pauli identity gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A=\ell_0^2-\ell_1^2-\ell_2^2-\ell_3^2.
}
\label{eq:detA_Pauli}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)
=
\ell_0(p)^2-\ell_1(p)^2-\ell_2(p)^2-\ell_3(p)^2.
}
\label{eq:detA1_explicit}
\end{equation}

Now define the symmetric matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
:=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a^{\ i}C_a^{\ j}
-
C_0^{\ i}C_0^{\ j}.
}
\label{eq:Gij_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)
=
-\,p_iG_{ij}p_j.
}
\label{eq:detA1_Gij}
\end{equation}

So the entire nondegeneracy problem is reduced to a finite quadratic form.

\section{Determinant of the Full Graded Principal Operator}

Since
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one has
\begin{equation}
\det D_1(p)=\det\!\bigl(A_1(p)A_1(p)^\dagger\bigr)=|\det A_1(p)|^2.
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det D_1(p)
=
\bigl(p_iG_{ij}p_j\bigr)^2.
}
\label{eq:detD1_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the graded principal operator is nondegenerate for generic \(p\neq 0\) iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
p_iG_{ij}p_j\neq 0
\qquad
\text{for generic }p\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G_nonzero_generic}
\end{equation}

A particularly clean sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\quad\text{(positive definite)}.
}
\label{eq:G_positive_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
p_iG_{ij}p_j>0
\qquad
(\forall p\neq 0),
\]
so
\[
\det A_1(p)<0,
\qquad
\det D_1(p)>0
\qquad
(\forall p\neq 0).
\]

\section{Spectrum of the Graded Principal Operator}

Assume for simplicity that the coefficients \(\ell_\alpha(p)\) are real.
Then \(A_1(p)\) is Hermitian and its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\pm(A_1)=\ell_0(p)\pm |\vec\ell(p)|,
\qquad
|\vec\ell|:=\sqrt{\ell_1^2+\ell_2^2+\ell_3^2}.
\label{eq:A1_eigs}
\end{equation}
Therefore the eigenvalues of \(D_1(p)\) are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
E(p)=\pm\bigl(\ell_0(p)\pm |\vec\ell(p)|\bigr).
}
\label{eq:D1_spectrum}
\end{equation}

So the zero-energy cone is determined by
\[
\ell_0(p)^2=|\vec\ell(p)|^2,
\]
equivalently
\[
p_iG_{ij}p_j=0.
\]

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
The identity coefficient \(C_0^{\ i}\) produces a tilt, not a constant mass.
The true load-bearing data are the traceless coefficient vectors \(C_a^{\ i}\), together with the effective quadratic form \(G_{ij}\).

\section{Canonical Dirac Reduction}

If \(G_{ij}\) is nondegenerate and has Euclidean signature in the spatial momenta, then by an invertible linear change of coordinates in \(p\) and a unitary change of basis in \(K_\pm\), the mixed symbol can be brought to the canonical form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)\sim p_i\sigma_i.
}
\label{eq:A1_canonical}
\end{equation}
Consequently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)\sim
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & p_i\sigma_i\\
p_i\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix}
=
p_i\alpha_i,
}
\label{eq:D1_Dirac_canonical}
\end{equation}
with
\[
\alpha_i=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \sigma_i\\
\sigma_i & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\{\alpha_i,\alpha_j\}=2\delta_{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

Thus the graded bypass produces the massless Dirac principal operator once the finite nondegeneracy test on \(G_{ij}\) passes.

\section{What This Calculation Actually Achieves}

This is the first actual computation in the graded bypass route.

It proves explicitly that:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the dangerous scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant principal operator because
\[
D_1(0)=0;
\]
\item the identity part of the mixed symbol is not a constant mass, but only a linear tilt contribution;
\item the entire Dirac nondegeneracy problem is reduced to the finite quadratic-form test
\[
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a^{\ i}C_a^{\ j}-C_0^{\ i}C_0^{\ j};
\]
\item if \(G_{ij}\) is positive definite, then the graded principal operator is nondegenerate and canonically Dirac.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Sharp Honest Conclusion}

The graded/projection mechanism has now been pushed one step further than the theorem statement alone.

The real remaining microscopic question is no longer
\[
\text{“how do we cancel }B_0\text{?”}
\]
but rather
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the actual projected TECT low-energy }2+2\text{ sector produce }C_\alpha^{\ i}
\text{ such that }G_{ij}>0?
}
\label{eq:graded_remaining_question}
\end{equation}

So the graded bypass route is now reduced to an explicit finite coefficient-extraction problem:
\[
\boxed{
\text{extract }C_0^{\ i},\,C_1^{\ i},\,C_2^{\ i},\,C_3^{\ i}
\text{ from the projected microscopic transport operator.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary of the First Actual Calculation in the Graded Bypass Route}

\paragraph{What was actually computed.}
In the graded \(2+2\) bypass, the relevant principal infrared operator is
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_iM_i.
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
D_1(0)=0,
}
\]
so the dangerous constant scalar Bragg block is absent from the relevant graded principal operator.

\paragraph{General mixed symbol.}
Writing
\[
A_1(p)=\ell_0(p)\mathbf 1_2+\ell_a(p)\sigma_a,
\qquad
\ell_\alpha(p)=C_\alpha^{\ i}p_i,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)=\ell_0^2-\ell_1^2-\ell_2^2-\ell_3^2.
}
\]

\paragraph{Finite nondegeneracy matrix.}
Defining
\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3 C_a^{\ i}C_a^{\ j}
-
C_0^{\ i}C_0^{\ j},
}
\]
we obtain
\[
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)=-p_iG_{ij}p_j,
\qquad
\det D_1(p)=\bigl(p_iG_{ij}p_j\bigr)^2.
}
\]

\paragraph{Meaning.}
So the graded bypass route is no longer about cancelling \(B_0\).
It is about extracting the coefficient vectors \(C_\alpha^{\ i}\) and checking whether
\[
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
}
\]
(or more generally whether \(p_iG_{ij}p_j\neq0\) for generic \(p\neq0\)).

\paragraph{If this holds.}
Then the graded principal operator is nondegenerate and can be reduced to
\[
\boxed{
D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha_i,
}
\]
i.e. the massless Dirac principal operator.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Therefore the real remaining microscopic question in the graded route is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{does the actual projected TECT }2+2\text{ sector produce coefficients }C_\alpha^{\ i}
\text{ with }G_{ij}>0?
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Extraction of \(C_\alpha{}^{i}\) in the Graded \(2+2\) Route}

\subsection{Goal}

We continue from the previous graded \(2+2\) bypass calculation.
The abstract principal operator was
\[
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
A_1(p)=\ell_0(p)\mathbf 1_2+\ell_a(p)\sigma_a,
\qquad
\ell_\alpha(p)=C_\alpha{}^{i}p_i.
\]
The next real task is to extract the coefficient vectors
\[
C_0{}^{i},\qquad C_1{}^{i},\qquad C_2{}^{i},\qquad C_3{}^{i}
\]
from the actual projected transport operator.

\subsection{Projected overlap matrices}

Let the graded low modes be
\[
u_a^+(\xi)=f_+(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
u_a^-(\xi)=f_-(\xi)e_a(\xi),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\]
The projected mixed overlap matrices are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle
=
\int d\xi\,
(u_a^+)^\dagger V^\mu(\xi)u_b^-.
}
\label{eq:graded_Mmu_overlap}
\end{equation}
This is the actual local projector-defect extraction formula.

The reduced mixed symbol is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
}
\label{eq:graded_A1_from_Mmu}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Pauli decomposition and exact coefficient extraction}

Every Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix \(M^\mu\) decomposes uniquely as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
C_0{}^{\mu}\mathbf 1_2
+
C_i{}^{\mu}\sigma_i,
\qquad i=1,2,3.
}
\label{eq:graded_Mmu_Pauli}
\end{equation}
The coefficients are extracted by traces:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_0{}^{\mu}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(M^\mu),
\qquad
C_i{}^{\mu}
=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_iM^\mu).
}
\label{eq:graded_C_extract}
\end{equation}
Substituting into \eqref{eq:graded_A1_from_Mmu},
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
p_\mu
\Bigl[
C_0{}^{\mu}\mathbf 1_2
+
C_i{}^{\mu}\sigma_i
\Bigr].
\label{eq:graded_A1_Cform}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\[
\ell_0(p)=p_\mu C_0{}^{\mu},
\qquad
\ell_i(p)=p_\mu C_i{}^{\mu}.
\]

This closes the extraction map
\[
V^\mu(\xi)
\Longrightarrow
M^\mu
\Longrightarrow
C_\alpha{}^{\mu}.
\]

\subsection{Actual local minimal transport class}

For the actual local projector-defect operator class already identified in the TECT chain, the projected matrices take the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\mu
=
I_\theta
\Bigl[
\Lambda_\parallel\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:graded_Mmu_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the reduced S2 symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
}
\label{eq:graded_A1_S2}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:graded_lambda_alpha_beta}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Adapted-basis coefficient vectors}

Choose the shell/worldvolume momentum basis
\[
p=(p_1,p_2,p_\parallel).
\]
Comparing \eqref{eq:graded_A1_Cform} with \eqref{eq:graded_A1_S2}, the Pauli coefficients are read off explicitly.

For the \(p_1\)-direction:
\[
A_1(p)\supset p_1(\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2),
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_0{}^{1}=0,
\qquad
C_1{}^{1}=\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
C_2{}^{1}=\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
C_3{}^{1}=0.
}
\label{eq:C_for_p1}
\end{equation}

For the \(p_2\)-direction:
\[
A_1(p)\supset p_2(-\beta\sigma_1+\alpha\sigma_2),
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_0{}^{2}=0,
\qquad
C_1{}^{2}=-\beta=-I_\theta\Lambda_O,
\qquad
C_2{}^{2}=\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
C_3{}^{2}=0.
}
\label{eq:C_for_p2}
\end{equation}

For the longitudinal direction:
\[
A_1(p)\supset p_\parallel\,\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\]
thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_0{}^{\parallel}=0,
\qquad
C_1{}^{\parallel}=0,
\qquad
C_2{}^{\parallel}=0,
\qquad
C_3{}^{\parallel}=\lambda_\parallel=I_\theta\Lambda_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:C_for_pparallel}
\end{equation}

Therefore, in the minimal actual local transport class,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_0{}^{i}=0
\qquad
\text{for all }i=1,2,\parallel.
}
\label{eq:C0_zero_minimal_transport}
\end{equation}

\subsection{The finite nondegeneracy matrix \(G_{ij}\)}

Recall
\begin{equation}
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3C_a{}^{i}C_a{}^{j}
-
C_0{}^{i}C_0{}^{j}.
\label{eq:Gij_def_again}
\end{equation}
Since \(C_0{}^{i}=0\), this reduces to
\begin{equation}
G_{ij}
=
\sum_{a=1}^3C_a{}^{i}C_a{}^{j}.
\label{eq:Gij_noC0}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:C_for_p1}, \eqref{eq:C_for_p2}, and \eqref{eq:C_for_pparallel}, we get:

\paragraph{Diagonal entries}
\begin{align}
G_{11}
&=
(C_1{}^{1})^2+(C_2{}^{1})^2+(C_3{}^{1})^2
\nonumber\\
&=
\alpha^2+\beta^2
=
I_\theta^2(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2),
\label{eq:G11}
\\
G_{22}
&=
(C_1{}^{2})^2+(C_2{}^{2})^2+(C_3{}^{2})^2
\nonumber\\
&=
\beta^2+\alpha^2
=
I_\theta^2(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2),
\label{eq:G22}
\\
G_{\parallel\parallel}
&=
(C_1{}^{\parallel})^2+(C_2{}^{\parallel})^2+(C_3{}^{\parallel})^2
\nonumber\\
&=
\lambda_\parallel^2
=
I_\theta^2\Lambda_\parallel^2.
\label{eq:Gpp}
\end{align}

\paragraph{Off-diagonal entries}
\begin{align}
G_{12}
&=
C_1{}^{1}C_1{}^{2}
+
C_2{}^{1}C_2{}^{2}
+
C_3{}^{1}C_3{}^{2}
\nonumber\\
&=
\alpha(-\beta)+\beta(\alpha)+0=0,
\label{eq:G12}
\\
G_{1\parallel}
&=
C_1{}^{1}C_1{}^{\parallel}
+
C_2{}^{1}C_2{}^{\parallel}
+
C_3{}^{1}C_3{}^{\parallel}
=0,
\label{eq:G1p}
\\
G_{2\parallel}
&=
C_1{}^{2}C_1{}^{\parallel}
+
C_2{}^{2}C_2{}^{\parallel}
+
C_3{}^{2}C_3{}^{\parallel}
=0.
\label{eq:G2p}
\end{align}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}
=
I_\theta^2
\begin{pmatrix}
\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2 & 0 & 0\\
0 & \Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2 & 0\\
0 & 0 & \Lambda_\parallel^2
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Gij_final_diagonal}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Equivalence with the witness condition}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
I_\theta\neq 0,\quad
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,\quad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G_positive_iff}
\end{equation}
Since the explicit defect profile already gives
\[
I_\theta\neq 0,
\]
we conclude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G_positive_iff_reduced}
\end{equation}

But by \eqref{eq:graded_lambda_alpha_beta}, this is equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G_positive_iff_witness}
\end{equation}

So the graded nondegeneracy criterion is exactly the actual witness criterion in the local projector-defect operator class.

\subsection{Determinant and Dirac reduction}

From the previous graded calculation,
\[
\det A_1(p)=-p_iG_{ij}p_j,
\qquad
\det D_1(p)=\bigl(p_iG_{ij}p_j\bigr)^2.
\]
Using \eqref{eq:Gij_final_diagonal},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)
=
-I_\theta^2
\Bigl[
(\Lambda_E^2+\Lambda_O^2)(p_1^2+p_2^2)
+
\Lambda_\parallel^2 p_\parallel^2
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:detA1_actual}
\end{equation}
Hence for generic \(p\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det A_1(p)\neq 0
\iff
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:detA1_nonzero_iff}
\end{equation}
Therefore the graded principal operator is nondegenerate exactly when the actual witness coefficients are nondegenerate.

After unitary basis changes in \(K_\pm\) and an invertible linear redefinition of \((p_1,p_2,p_\parallel)\), this yields the canonical Dirac symbol
\[
D_1(p)\sim p_i\alpha_i.
\]

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

The next step beyond the abstract graded theorem is now fully explicit:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
\Longrightarrow
M^\mu
\Longrightarrow
C_\alpha{}^{i}
\Longrightarrow
G_{ij}
}
\label{eq:graded_actual_chain}
\end{equation}
and in the actual local projector-defect operator class this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{ij}>0
\iff
\Lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:graded_final_equivalence}
\end{equation}

Thus the real remaining microscopic problem in the graded bypass route is simply:
extract the actual transport coefficients
\[
\Lambda_\parallel,\qquad \Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O
\]
from the full TECT defect-projector transport kernel.

\paragraph{What was actually computed.}
The abstract coefficient vectors

of the graded \(2+2\) principal symbol can be extracted directly from the projected overlap matrices
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^-\rangle,

\paragraph{Key equivalence.}

Equivalently,

\paragraph{Meaning.}

Inside the actual local projector-defect operator class, it reduces exactly to the same three transport coefficients

\]
that already control the witness problem.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Therefore the true remaining microscopic task is now sharply localized:

\text{ from the full TECT dynamics.}

\section{Quadratic Class II Reduction and Explicit Projection to \texorpdfstring{$(g_c,g_E,g_O)$}{(g_c,g_E,g_O)}}

\subsection{Scope and honest input}

We start from the Class II UV action
\begin{equation}
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha\,X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta\,X_i^a K_i^a[P,\psi].
\label{eq:CII_UV}
\end{equation}
At the current document level, the full unreduced closed forms of
\(J_i^a[\Psi]\) and \(K_i^a[P,\psi]\) are not yet available in the complete TECT action.
What \emph{is} available is the shell-relevant quadratic reduction template and its induced tensor summary:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}.
}
\label{eq:CII_master_deltaN}
\end{equation}
The task is therefore to derive \eqref{eq:CII_master_deltaN} from the reduced quadratic Class II structure and then project it to the shell-adapted coefficients \((A,B,C)\), equivalently \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\).

\subsection{Background and fluctuations}

Fix the refined locked background
\begin{equation}
\Psi_0=\phi_0\,z_0,
\qquad
P_0=z_0z_0^\dagger,
\qquad
z_0^\dagger z_0=1,
\label{eq:CII_bg}
\end{equation}
and write the shell-relevant fluctuations as
\[
\Psi=\Psi_0+\psi,
\qquad
P=P_0+\delta P.
\]
For the projector fluctuation, parameterize
\begin{equation}
\delta P=\xi^b T^b+\cdots,
\label{eq:CII_deltaP}
\end{equation}
where \(b=1,2,3\) labels the shell-relevant internal tangent directions.

\subsection{Reduced quadratic Class II ansatz}

At shell-relevant quadratic order, the only pieces needed for the induced first-order enriched tensor are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a background source linear in \(X_i^a\) and \(\partial_i\phi_0\),
\item a shell-fluctuation source linear in \(X_i^a\), \(D_j\psi\), and \(\xi^b\).
\end{enumerate}

Thus the reduced quadratic Class II Lagrangian has the form
\begin{equation}
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^a\,X_i^a\,(\partial_i\phi_0)
+
g_X\,X_i^a\,C^{ab}_{ij}\,(D_j\psi)\,\xi^b
+\text{h.c.}
\label{eq:CII_reduced_quadratic}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(m^a\) is the internal background orientation source,
\item \(C^{ab}_{ij}\) is the shell-relevant carrier tensor,
\item \(\lambda\) and \(g_X\) are reduced couplings inherited from \(\alpha,\beta\) and the reduction of \(J_i^a[\Psi]\), \(K_i^a[P,\psi]\).
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Integrating out the heavy mediator}

Because \(X_i^a\) is heavy, its leading equation of motion is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
M_X^2 X_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
=0.
\label{eq:CII_Xeom}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\lambda\,m^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
\Bigr]
+O(M_X^{-4}).
\label{eq:CII_Xsolve}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:CII_Xsolve} back into \eqref{eq:CII_reduced_quadratic}, the mixed bilinear term is
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,
m^a\,C^{ab}_{ij}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(D_j\psi)\,\xi^b
+\text{h.c.}
\label{eq:CII_mixed_bilinear}
\end{equation}
Therefore the induced shell-enriched tensor is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}.
}
\label{eq:CII_deltaN_derived}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Shell-adapted minimal Class II seed family}

Choose the shell frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal},
\]
and the minimal shell-adapted Class II seed family
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:CII_m3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:CII_C33}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}
=
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:CII_C31C32}
\end{equation}
All other shell-irrelevant components are set to zero in the minimal seed truncation.

Define
\begin{equation}
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
\label{eq:CII_Gamma}
\end{equation}
Then \eqref{eq:CII_deltaN_derived} gives
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}
=
-\Gamma\,c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:CII_deltaN3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^1_{ij}
=
-\Gamma\,
\bigl(
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j}
\bigr),
\label{eq:CII_deltaN1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^2_{ij}
=
-\Gamma\,
\bigl(
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}
\bigr).
\label{eq:CII_deltaN2}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Projection to the axial shell basis}

Compare \eqref{eq:CII_deltaN3}--\eqref{eq:CII_deltaN2} with the canonical axial shell basis
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:CII_ABCbasis}
\end{equation}
Reading off coefficients directly:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta A=-\Gamma\,c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma\,c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma\,c_J.
}
\label{eq:CII_deltaABC}
\end{equation}

Thus the induced Class II correction preserves the exact shell-axial structure and only renormalizes the three coefficients.

\subsection{Dictionary to \texorpdfstring{$(g_c,g_E,g_O)$}{(g_c,g_E,g_O)}}

Using the already established shell/defect dictionary
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_c,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_E,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_O,
\]
equation \eqref{eq:CII_deltaABC} implies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c \propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E \propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O \propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:CII_gcgego}
\end{equation}
The overall proportionality is controlled by \(\Gamma\) and by the defect-overlap normalization.

\paragraph{Important honest point.}
At the current document level, \eqref{eq:CII_gcgego} is the strongest fully honest result.
The nonzero witness directions are extracted explicitly, but the final absolute numerical normalization of \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) still depends on the detailed completion of the shell/defect overlap dictionary in the full complete TECT action.

\subsection{Immediate seed consequences}

From \eqref{eq:CII_gcgego} one gets the three canonical witness directions:

\paragraph{Longitudinal seed.}
If
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
c_I=c_J=0,
\]
then
\[
g_c\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Even transverse seed.}
If
\[
c_\parallel=0,
\qquad
c_I\neq 0,
\qquad
c_J=0,
\]
then
\[
g_E\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Odd transverse seed.}
If
\[
c_\parallel=0,
\qquad
c_I=0,
\qquad
c_J\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
g_O\neq 0.
\]

Thus, provided the full complete TECT action actually realizes a nontrivial Class II sector in the relevant defect background, the witness channels are present on an open dense full-measure subset of the allowed Class II parameter space.

\subsection{What is now really closed}

The actual quadratic Class II computation closes the chain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
\Longrightarrow
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^aC^{ab}_{ij}
\Longrightarrow
(\delta A,\delta B,\delta C)
=
-\Gamma(c_\parallel,c_I,c_J).
}
\label{eq:CII_closed_chain}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\label{eq:CII_final_result}
\end{equation}

\subsection{What still remains open}

What remains open is not the shell-adapted projection itself, but:
\begin{enumerate}
\item the exact microscopic realization of the Class II carrier sector in the true complete TECT action;
\item the final absolute normalization of \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) in the full dynamics.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary of the Class II Quadratic Projection Calculation}

\paragraph{What was actually done.}
Starting from the Class II UV action
\[
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+

\]
and reducing it to the shell-relevant quadratic sector around the locked background \((\Psi_0,P_0)\), one obtains
\[
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda m^a X_i^a\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X X_i^a C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b+\text{h.c.}
\]
Integrating out \(X_i^a\) yields the induced enriched tensor
\[
\boxed{
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Shell-adapted minimal Class II seed.}

m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,

\[
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\hat n_i e_{2j},
\]
this gives
\[
\boxed{
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J,
\qquad
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Witness coefficients.}
Using the shell/defect dictionary
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_c,\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_E,\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_O,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E\propto c_I,
\qquad
g_O\propto c_J.
}
\]

\paragraph{Honest status.}
So the corrected Path C is no longer merely schematic:
its shell-adapted induced tensor and witness directions are explicitly derived at the quadratic template level.

What remains open is:

\boxed{
\text{whether the full complete TECT action really realizes the Class II carrier sector,}
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final absolute normalization of }(g_c,g_E,g_O)\text{ in the complete dynamics.}

\section{Normalization Extraction and Effective Witness Audit for the Class II Route}

\section{Part I. Strongest Honest Normalization Extraction Available Now}

\paragraph{Scope.}
At the present document level, the complete unreduced microscopic forms of
\[
J_i^a[\Psi],\qquad K_i^a[P,\psi]
\]
are not yet available in the final full TECT action.
Therefore the absolute microscopic values of
\[
g_c,\qquad g_E,\qquad g_O
\]
cannot yet be extracted to the very end from first principles.

What \emph{is} already closed is the shell-relevant quadratic Class II reduction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta N^b_{ij}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,m^a C^{ab}_{ij}.
}
\label{eq:deltaN_master}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Quadratic reduction and raw normalization scale}

Starting from the shell-relevant quadratic Class II template
\begin{equation}
L_X^{(2)}
=
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^a X_i^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,X_i^a C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
+\text{h.c.},
\label{eq:LX2}
\end{equation}
the heavy mediator equation is
\begin{equation}
M_X^2 X_i^a
+
\lambda\,m^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
=0.
\label{eq:Xeom}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\lambda\,m^a\,\partial_i\phi_0
+
g_X\,C^{ab}_{ij}(D_j\psi)\xi^b
\Bigr]
+O(M_X^{-4}),
\label{eq:Xsol}
\end{equation}
and substituting back gives the induced mixed bilinear
\begin{equation}
\delta L_{\mathrm{mix}}^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}\,
m^a C^{ab}_{ij}\,
(\partial_i\phi_0)(D_j\psi)\xi^b
+\text{h.c.}
\label{eq:mixedbilinear}
\end{equation}
Hence \eqref{eq:deltaN_master} follows.

Define the raw Class II normalization scale
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma:=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:Gamma_def}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Shell-adapted minimal seed family}

Take the axial shell frame
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}\ \text{orthonormal},
\]
and the minimal Class II seed parameterization
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\,\delta^{a3},
\label{eq:m3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:C33}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C^{31}_{ij}
=
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}
=
-\,c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}
+
c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:C31C32}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\delta N^3_{ij}=-\Gamma\,c_\parallel\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\label{eq:dN3}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^1_{ij}
=
-\Gamma\,
(c_I\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J\,\hat n_i e_{2j}),
\label{eq:dN1}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\delta N^2_{ij}
=
-\Gamma\,
(-c_J\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I\,\hat n_i e_{2j}).
\label{eq:dN2}
\end{equation}

Comparing with the canonical axial shell basis
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}=A\,\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=B\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+C\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
N^2_{ij}=-C\,\hat n_i e_{1j}+B\,\hat n_i e_{2j},
\label{eq:ABC_basis}
\end{equation}
we read off
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta A=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
\delta B=-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
\delta C=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\label{eq:dABC}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Reduced witness normalization}

Using the already established dictionary
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_c,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_E,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\leftrightarrow g_O,
\]
the strongest honest current extraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\nu_\parallel\,\Gamma\,c_\parallel,
\qquad
g_E=\nu_\perp\,\Gamma\,c_I,
\qquad
g_O=\nu_\perp\,\Gamma\,c_J,
}
\label{eq:gcgego_norm}
\end{equation}
where \(\nu_\parallel,\nu_\perp\) are the remaining shell/defect-overlap normalization constants of the complete microscopic reduction.

Equivalently, at the transport-symbol level,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,g_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\label{eq:lambda_norm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,g_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
\label{eq:ab_norm}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:gcgego_norm} into \eqref{eq:lambda_norm}--\eqref{eq:ab_norm},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\nu_\parallel\,\Gamma\,c_\parallel\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:lambda_cpar}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\nu_\perp\,\Gamma\,c_I\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\nu_\perp\,\Gamma\,c_J\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:ab_cIJ}
\end{equation}

Therefore the maximum honest normalization extraction currently available is:
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}
}
\]
at the mediator-reduction level, together with the universal defect-overlap factors
\[
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa.
\]

\section{Part II. Effective Witness Audit}

\subsection{General effective coefficients}

Math12 gives the canonical Class II effective shell coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\mu c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\mu c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\mu c_J,
}
\label{eq:AeffBeffCeff}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\mu=\frac{\lambda g_X}{M_X^2}m=\Gamma.
\label{eq:muGamma}
\end{equation}
The corresponding reduced Weyl coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel^{\mathrm{eff}}=\kappa_*|G_*|A_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}=\kappa_*|G_*|B_{\mathrm{eff}},
\qquad
\beta_{\mathrm{eff}}=\kappa_*|G_*|C_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\label{eq:eff_lab}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
\left(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2\right).
}
\label{eq:detMeff_general}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact shell-level nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\neq 0,
\qquad
(B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nondeg_general}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Obstruction baseline + Class II correction}

For the minimal locked obstruction baseline, the currently honest shell input is
\begin{equation}
A_0=0,
\qquad
B_0=\kappa_Z=\frac{4Z}{A},
\qquad
C_0=0,
\label{eq:baseline_ABC}
\end{equation}
because the locked minimal PDE supplies the identity-channel transverse witness but no longitudinal Pauli witness.

Substituting \eqref{eq:baseline_ABC} into \eqref{eq:AeffBeffCeff},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\label{eq:ABCeff_obstruction}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
(-\Gamma c_\parallel)
\left[
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I\right)^2
+
(\Gamma c_J)^2
\right].
}
\label{eq:detMeff_obstruction}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Nondegeneracy region}

From \eqref{eq:detMeff_obstruction}, the effective shell is Weyl iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,\ \Gamma c_J\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nondeg_region_obstruction}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, assuming \(\Gamma\neq 0\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A\Gamma}-c_I,\ c_J\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:nondeg_region_scaled}
\end{equation}

So the bad set is the codimension-one tuned locus
\begin{equation}
c_\parallel=0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\Bigl(c_J=0,\ c_I=\frac{4Z}{A\Gamma}\Bigr).
\label{eq:bad_locus}
\end{equation}
Away from that tuned locus, the shell is nondegenerate.

\subsection{Interpretation}

This gives two complementary viewpoints.

\paragraph{Viewpoint 1: obstruction baseline plus Class II repair.}
Because \(B_0=\kappa_Z\neq0\) already survives from the identity channel, the Class II sector does not need to generate transverse witness from scratch.
It is sufficient to generate a nonzero longitudinal coefficient:
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0
\]
already gives a Weyl shell generically, except on the tuned cancellation locus for the transverse factor.

\paragraph{Viewpoint 2: pure Class II local transport sector.}
If one works in the purely reduced local S2 transport normalization, one sets the baseline to the Class II transport coefficients themselves and obtains the stricter condition
\[
g_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(g_E,g_O)\neq(0,0),
\]
equivalently
\[
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_I,c_J)\neq (0,0),
\]
inside the concrete Class II truncation.

So the two descriptions are not contradictory:
they are two different normalizations of the same shell problem.

\subsection{What is now honestly closed}

The combination of normalization extraction and witness audit closes the following chain:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{UV}}^{(II)}
\Longrightarrow
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}
\Longrightarrow
(\delta A,\delta B,\delta C)=(-\Gamma c_\parallel,-\Gamma c_I,-\Gamma c_J)
}
\label{eq:closed_chain_1}
\end{equation}
and therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
A_{\mathrm{eff}}
(B_{\mathrm{eff}}^2+C_{\mathrm{eff}}^2),
}
\label{eq:closed_chain_2}
\end{equation}
with the explicit obstruction-baseline realization
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M_{\mathrm{eff}}
=
(\kappa_*|G_*|)^3
(-\Gamma c_\parallel)
\left[
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I\right)^2
+
(\Gamma c_J)^2
\right].
}
\label{eq:closed_chain_3}
\end{equation}
Hence the effective shell is Weyl on the open region
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A\Gamma}-c_I,\ c_J\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:closed_chain_4}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Honest frontier}

What still remains open is not the shell projection or the effective determinant formula.
It is only:

\begin{enumerate}
\item whether the true complete TECT action actually realizes a nontrivial Class II carrier sector in the relevant defect background;
\item the final absolute values of the normalization constants \(\nu_\parallel,\nu_\perp\) entering the exact transport coefficients.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Dirac Step 2: Opposite-Valley Witness Matching with Obstruction Baseline + Class II Correction}

\subsection{Goal}

We now continue from the previously obtained effective shell coefficients

\qquad

\subsection{Matched opposite-valley frames}

Let
\begin{equation}
\hat n_+ := \frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
\hat n_- := -\hat n_+.
\label{eq:matched_n}
\end{equation}
Choose a positively oriented orthonormal frame at \(+G_*\):
\begin{equation}
\{e_{1+},e_{2+},\hat n_+\},
\qquad
e_{1+}\times e_{2+}=\hat n_+.
\label{eq:frame_plus}
\end{equation}
Define the matched opposite-valley frame at \(-G_*\) by
\begin{equation}
e_{1-}:=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}:=-e_{2+},
\qquad
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+.
\label{eq:frame_minus}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
e_{1-}\times e_{2-}
=
e_{1+}\times(-e_{2+})
=
-\hat n_+
=
\hat n_-,
\label{eq:minus_orientation}
\end{equation}
so \(\{e_{1-},e_{2-},\hat n_-\}\) is again positively oriented.

This is the standard matched opposite-valley convention already used in the notes.

\subsection{Effective shell tensor family at the two valleys}

Write the effective shell-enriched tensor family at each valley in the canonical axial basis:
\begin{equation}
N^3_{ij}(\pm)=A_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}\hat n_{\pm j},
\label{eq:N3_pm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N^1_{ij}(\pm)
=
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}
+
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j},
\label{eq:N1_pm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
N^2_{ij}(\pm)
=
-\,C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}
+
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}.
\label{eq:N2_pm}
\end{equation}

The crucial point is that the scalar amplitudes
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad B_{\mathrm{eff}},\qquad C_{\mathrm{eff}}
\]
are assumed to be even under the matched opposite-valley transformation.
In the canonical Class II seed family this is exactly the statement that
\[
c_\parallel^- = c_\parallel^+,
\qquad
c_I^- = c_I^+,
\qquad
c_J^- = c_J^+,
\]
hence the same effective amplitudes are read at both valleys.

\subsection{Witness functionals at the two valleys}

Define the matched-frame witness functionals:
\begin{equation}
W_{\parallel}^\pm[N]
:=
\hat n_{\pm i}\hat n_{\pm j}N^3_{ij}(\pm),
\label{eq:Wpar_pm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_I^\pm[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}N^1_{ij}(\pm)
+
e_{2\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}N^2_{ij}(\pm)
\Bigr),
\label{eq:WI_pm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
W_J^\pm[N]
:=
\frac12
\Bigl(
e_{1\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}N^2_{ij}(\pm)
-
e_{2\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}N^1_{ij}(\pm)
\Bigr).
\label{eq:WJ_pm}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:N3_pm}--\eqref{eq:N2_pm}:

\paragraph{Longitudinal witness}
\begin{align}
W_\parallel^\pm
&=
\hat n_{\pm i}\hat n_{\pm j}
\bigl(
A_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}\hat n_{\pm j}
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&=
A_{\mathrm{eff}}(\hat n_\pm^2)^2
=
A_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\label{eq:Wpar_result}
\end{align}

\paragraph{Even transverse witness}
\begin{align}
W_I^\pm
&=
\frac12
\Bigl[
e_{1\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}
\bigl(
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}
+
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
+
e_{2\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}
\bigl(
-\,C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}
+
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}
\bigr)
\Bigr]
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac12(B_{\mathrm{eff}}+B_{\mathrm{eff}})
=
B_{\mathrm{eff}}.
\label{eq:WI_result}
\end{align}

\paragraph{Odd transverse witness}
\begin{align}
W_J^\pm
&=
\frac12
\Bigl[
e_{1\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}
\bigl(
-\,C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}
+
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}
\bigr)
\nonumber\\
&\qquad\qquad
-
e_{2\pm j}\hat n_{\pm i}
\bigl(
B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}
+
C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j}
\bigr)
\Bigr].
\end{align}
Depending on the sign convention used for the \(O_J\)-basis, this equals either \(+C_{\mathrm{eff}}\) or \(-C_{\mathrm{eff}}\).
What matters physically is that the same convention is used at both valleys.
Fixing the shell basis once and for all, we may write simply
\begin{equation}
W_J^\pm=C_{\mathrm{eff}}
\label{eq:WJ_result}
\end{equation}
up to that global convention.

Thus the witness triples are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^\pm,W_I^\pm,W_J^\pm)
=
(A_{\mathrm{eff}},B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}}).
}
\label{eq:triple_same_eff}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Obstruction baseline + Class II correction}

From the previous step,
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\Gamma c_J.
\label{eq:ABCeff_prev}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W_\parallel^\pm=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
W_I^\pm=\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
W_J^\pm=-\Gamma c_J,
}
\label{eq:Wpm_obstruction_plus_CII}
\end{equation}
again up to the fixed sign convention for \(W_J\).

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
}
\label{eq:opp_match_main}
\end{equation}

So the obstruction baseline does not spoil opposite-valley matching.
It merely shifts the common transverse scalar amplitude \(B_{\mathrm{eff}}\).

\subsection{Consequence for opposite-valley pairing}

By the previously established witness-pairing theorem, equality of the witness triples in the matched opposite-valley frames is equivalent to the standard reduced pairing relation
\begin{equation}
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p)
\label{eq:pairing_relation}
\end{equation}
after subtraction of the common scalar part.

Therefore the obstruction-baseline + Class II corrected representative already satisfies the Step-2 pairing criterion inside the concrete truncation.

\subsection{Combined Step 1 + Step 2}

From the previous witness audit, the shell is Weyl iff
\begin{equation}
\Gamma c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,\ \Gamma c_J\right)\neq (0,0).
\label{eq:step1_condition}
\end{equation}
From \eqref{eq:opp_match_main}, Step 2 is automatically satisfied in the same concrete family.

Hence, inside the obstruction-baseline + Class II corrected truncation, we obtain:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Step 1 (Weyl nondegeneracy) + Step 2 (opposite-valley matching) are closed simultaneously.}
}
\label{eq:step12_closed}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Honest frontier}

What remains open is stronger than the above statement:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the full complete TECT action must still be shown to realize the required opposite shell pair } \pm G_*
\text{ as actual low-energy valleys.}
}
\label{eq:opp_pair_open}
\end{equation}
So the exact honest conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete Class II witness truncation, Step 2 is closed;}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the full microscopic existence of the opposite shell-pair valleys remains to be verified.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of Opposite-Valley Matching with Obstruction Baseline + Class II Correction}

\paragraph{What was actually computed.}
Using the matched opposite-valley frames
\[
\hat n_-=-\hat n_+,
\qquad
e_{1-}=e_{1+},
\qquad
e_{2-}=-e_{2+},
\]
and the effective axial shell tensor
\[
N^3_{ij}(\pm)=A_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}\hat n_{\pm j},
\]
\[
N^1_{ij}(\pm)=B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}+C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j},
\]
\[
N^2_{ij}(\pm)=-C_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{1\pm j}+B_{\mathrm{eff}}\hat n_{\pm i}e_{2\pm j},
\]
one finds
\[
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^\pm,W_I^\pm,W_J^\pm)
=
(A_{\mathrm{eff}},B_{\mathrm{eff}},C_{\mathrm{eff}}).
}
\]

\paragraph{With the obstruction baseline plus Class II correction.}
Since
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=-\Gamma c_J,
\]
the witness triples at both valleys are
\[
\boxed{
W_\parallel^\pm=-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
W_I^\pm=\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
W_J^\pm=-\Gamma c_J.
}
\]

\paragraph{Matching result.}
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
(W_\parallel^-,W_I^-,W_J^-)
=
(W_\parallel^+,W_I^+,W_J^+).
}
\]
So Step 2 is closed inside the same concrete truncation.

\paragraph{Combined Step 1 + Step 2.}
The shell is Weyl iff
\[
\boxed{
\Gamma c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,\ \Gamma c_J\right)\neq (0,0),
}
\]
and in the same region opposite-valley witness matching already holds.

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
Thus, inside the concrete obstruction-baseline + Class II corrected truncation,
\[
\boxed{
\text{Step 1 and Step 2 are closed together.}
}
\]
What remains open is only whether the full complete TECT action actually realizes the required opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) as physical low-energy valleys.

\section{Dirac Step 3: Zero Constant Mixing in the Obstruction-Baseline + Class II Truncation}

\subsection{Goal}

After Step 1 (effective Weyl nondegeneracy) and Step 2 (opposite-valley witness matching),
the next local Dirac closure condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:goal_V0}
\end{equation}
Here \(V(p)\) is the off-diagonal mixing block between the local doubled Dirac carrier and the remote sector in
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Hfull_V0}
\end{equation}

The symbol \(V(0)=0\) means absence of \emph{constant inter-sector hybridization} at the shell crossing.

\subsection{The actual local Dirac carrier}

The correct shell-relevant local carrier is not an ordinary cubic 2D irrep.
Rather, the actual local Dirac block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
}
\label{eq:HD_actual}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\) is the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\) is the shell-relevant enriched internal/transverse doublet.
\end{itemize}

This is crucial: the zero-mixing question must be asked relative to the actual carrier \(\mathcal H_D\), not relative to ordinary little-group irreducibility.

\subsection{The theorem-level zero-mixing statement}

Let \(H_*\) denote the little group at the crossing \(p=0\), and assume:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}=\mathcal H_D\oplus \mathcal H_R
\label{eq:Hsplit}
\end{equation}
is \(H_*\)-invariant, and that the microscopic Hamiltonian is \(H_*\)-equivariant at \(p=0\).
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
}
\label{eq:V0_Hom}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:Hom_to_V0}
\end{equation}

This theorem-level statement is already closed.

\subsection{Practical remote-sector decomposition}

Decompose the remote sector into \(H_*\)-invariant pieces:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
\label{eq:HR_decomp}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)
\cong
\bigoplus_a \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D).
\label{eq:Hom_sum}
\end{equation}
Hence it is enough to prove
\begin{equation}
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(K_a,\mathcal H_D)=0
\qquad
\forall a.
\label{eq:Ka_zero}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Shell-relevant mismatch labels}

A remote sector \(K_a\) is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of the following shell-relevant labels:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{presence of enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved microscopic label}.
}
\label{eq:label_list}
\end{equation}

Thus the microscopic \(V(0)=0\) problem is reduced to a finite label-audit problem.

\subsection{Minimal dangerous truncation}

In the minimal dangerous truncation, write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}.
}
\label{eq:minimal_truncation}
\end{equation}
Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\mathcal H_D\): the local doubled Dirac carrier,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\): volumetric sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\): higher-shell sector,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\): same shell but lacking the enriched internal doublet,
\item \(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\): wrong internal representation.
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Sectorwise mismatch table}

We now check the shell-relevant labels sector by sector.

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}\).}
This sector fails the transverse/non-volumetric character condition.
Hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}\).}
This sector lies on a different shell orbit, so it fails the shell-pair label \(\pm G_*\).
Hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}\).}
Even if it shares the same shell pair, it lacks the enriched internal doublet \(\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}\).
Hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

\paragraph{\(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}\).}
This sector carries the wrong internal representation content.
Hence
\[
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},\mathcal H_D)=0.
\]

Therefore every dangerous remote sector in \eqref{eq:minimal_truncation} mismatches \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label.

\subsection{Conclusion of the audit}

By \eqref{eq:Hom_sum},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0.
}
\label{eq:Hom_zero_final}
\end{equation}
Then by \eqref{eq:Hom_to_V0},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:V0_final}
\end{equation}

Thus, in the obstruction-baseline + Class II corrected truncation, zero constant mixing is established once the above finite mismatch table is accepted.

\subsection{Compatibility with Class II}

The canonical minimal Class II data
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}
\label{eq:ClassII_data}
\end{equation}
renormalize the shell-level witness coefficients \(A,B,C\), but do not change the representation content of the remote sector classification itself.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with }V(0)=0,
\text{ but does not by itself prove it.}
}
\label{eq:ClassII_compatible}
\end{equation}

The actual proof of \(V(0)=0\) remains the sectorwise mismatch audit above.

\subsection{Combined Step 1 + Step 2 + Step 3}

From the previous steps, the concrete obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation gives:
\begin{equation}
\Gamma c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,\ \Gamma c_J\right)\neq (0,0)
\label{eq:step123_weyl}
\end{equation}
for Weyl nondegeneracy, and opposite-valley witness matching is already closed in the same truncation.

Now Step 3 adds:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\label{eq:step3_condition}
\end{equation}

Thus the concrete truncation has now closed:
\[
\text{Step 1: Weyl nondegeneracy},
\qquad
\text{Step 2: opposite-valley matching},
\qquad
\text{Step 3: zero constant mixing}
\]
at the theorem-reduction level, with Step 3 requiring only the finite mismatch audit.

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

The strongest honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the concrete obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation, }V(0)=0
\text{ is not automatic,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its verification is fully reduced to a finite shell-relevant remote-sector label audit.}
}
\label{eq:step3_honest}
\end{equation}

So Step 3 is now closed at the reduction-theorem level in exactly the same sense as the current TECT notes.

%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of Dirac Step 3 in the Obstruction-Baseline + Class II Truncation}

\paragraph{What was actually established.}
The local Dirac carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
and the constant mixing block satisfies
\[
V(0)\in \mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D).
\]
Therefore
\[
\boxed{
\mathrm{Hom}_{H_*}(\mathcal H_R,\mathcal H_D)=0
\Longrightarrow
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Practical finite audit.}
Decompose the remote sector as
\[
\mathcal H_R=\bigoplus_a K_a.
\]
A sector \(K_a\) is excluded from constant mixing if it differs from \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one of:
\[
\pm G_*,
\quad
\text{transverse/non-volumetric character},
\quad
\text{enriched internal doublet},
\quad
\text{grading/parity/chirality},
\quad
\text{extra conserved labels}.
\]

\paragraph{Minimal dangerous truncation.}
In the truncation
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{full}}^{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\mathcal H_D
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{vol}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{high}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}},
\]
every remote sector mismatches \(\mathcal H_D\) in at least one shell-relevant label, hence
\[
\boxed{
V(0)=0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Compatibility with Class II.}
The canonical Class II data renormalize the shell-level witness coefficients \(A,B,C\), but do not by themselves prove \(V(0)=0\).
So:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with }V(0)=0,\text{ and }V(0)=0\text{ is proved by the independent mismatch audit.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Combined status.}
Inside the concrete obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Step 1 (Weyl nondegeneracy), Step 2 (opposite-valley matching), and Step 3 (zero constant mixing) are all closed at the reduction-theorem level.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
What remains open microscopically is only whether the full complete TECT action realizes the required remote-sector decomposition and mismatch table exactly as assumed in the finite audit.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Dirac Step 4: Remote Spectral Gap in the Obstruction-Baseline + Class II Truncation}

\subsection{Goal}

After Step 1 (local Weyl nondegeneracy), Step 2 (opposite-valley matching), and Step 3 (\(V(0)=0\)),
the next remaining local Dirac closure condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta>0.
}
\label{eq:goal_gap}
\end{equation}
This means that the remote block \(H_R(p)\) is spectrally separated from zero near the selected shell crossing.

The correct theorem-level point is that \(\Delta>0\) is an \emph{independent spectral input}.
It is not implied by shell nondegeneracy.

\subsection{Why \texorpdfstring{$\det M\neq0$}{det M ≠ 0} does not prove the remote gap}

The shell-reduced local Dirac symbol has the form
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)
=
\lambda_\parallel p_\parallel \sigma_3
+
\alpha(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2),
\label{eq:local_symbol_gap}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
M=
\begin{pmatrix}
\alpha & -\beta & 0\\
\beta & \alpha & 0\\
0 & 0 & \lambda_\parallel
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\det M=\lambda_\parallel(\alpha^2+\beta^2).
\label{eq:detM_gap}
\end{equation}
This controls only the nondegeneracy of the local shell Dirac block.
It says nothing by itself about the complementary spectrum of \(H_R(p)\).

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M\neq 0
\ \not\Rightarrow\
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing.
}
\label{eq:detM_not_gap}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Remote block decomposition}

Write the full microscopic Hamiltonian as
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
H_D(p) & V(p)\\
V(p)^\dagger & H_R(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hfull_gap}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{itemize}
\item \(H_D(p)\) is the isolated local doubled Dirac block,
\item \(H_R(p)\) is the remote sector,
\item \(V(p)\) is the inter-sector mixing.
\end{itemize}

The remote-gap condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing
\qquad
(|p|\le \rho)
}
\label{eq:remote_gap_cond}
\end{equation}
for some \(\rho>0\) and \(\Delta>0\).

\subsection{Route A: direct finite spectral inequality}

At the minimal dangerous truncation level, write
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=D_R(p)+R_R(p),
\label{eq:HR_DR_RR}
\end{equation}
where \(D_R(p)\) is the diagonal/sector-center benchmark part and \(R_R(p)\) is the residual remote--remote mixing.

Define the pointwise sector-center lower bound
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p):=
\min\{
|\mu_{\mathrm{vol}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{high}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}(p)|,\,
|\mu_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int}}(p)|
\},
\label{eq:delta0p}
\end{equation}
and the remote residual norm
\begin{equation}
\eta_R(p):=\|R_R(p)\|.
\label{eq:etaRp}
\end{equation}
Then the pointwise estimate is
\begin{equation}
\|H_R(p)\psi\|
\ge
(\delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p))\|\psi\|.
\label{eq:pointwise_bound}
\end{equation}
Therefore, if
\begin{equation}
\delta_0(p)>\eta_R(p),
\label{eq:pointwise_gap_cond}
\end{equation}
then
\begin{equation}
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta(p),\Delta(p))=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta(p)\ge \delta_0(p)-\eta_R(p)>0.
\label{eq:pointwise_gap}
\end{equation}

On the neighborhood
\[
N_\rho:=\{p:|p|\le \rho\},
\]
define
\begin{equation}
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\eta_R(p).
\label{eq:delta0rho_etaRrho}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta_\rho,\Delta_\rho)=\varnothing
\quad(|p|\le \rho),
}
\label{eq:uniform_gap_cond}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\label{eq:uniform_gap_value}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Explicit benchmark version for the minimal dangerous truncation}

A sufficient explicit benchmark is obtained by sectorwise lower bounds:
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)}>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)}>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)}>0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}>0.
\label{eq:sector_bench}
\end{equation}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}
:=
\min\Bigl\{
\Delta_{\mathrm{vol},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{high},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(0)},
\Delta_{\mathrm{wrong\text{-}int},\rho}^{(0)}
\Bigr\}.
}
\label{eq:bench_delta}
\end{equation}
Then a sufficient finite gap condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:bench_gap_cond}
\end{equation}
This proves
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_\rho>0.
}
\label{eq:bench_gap_positive}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Route B: bounded perturbation from an already-gapped benchmark}

Assume instead that there exists an unperturbed realization
\begin{equation}
H_R^{(0)}(p)
\qquad\text{with}\qquad
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\qquad
(\Delta_0>0),
\label{eq:HR0_gap}
\end{equation}
for all sufficiently small \(p\), and that the actual remote block is
\begin{equation}
H_R(p)=H_R^{(0)}(p)+\delta H_R(p),
\qquad
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|\le \varepsilon.
\label{eq:pert_gap}
\end{equation}
Then the bounded-perturbation theorem gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon<\Delta_0
\Longrightarrow
\operatorname{spec}(H_R(p))\cap(-\Delta,\Delta)=\varnothing,
\qquad
\Delta:=\Delta_0-\varepsilon>0.
}
\label{eq:bounded_gap}
\end{equation}
Under the stronger bound
\[
\varepsilon<\frac{\Delta_0}{2},
\]
one gets the convenient estimate
\[
\Delta>\frac{\Delta_0}{2}>0.
\]

\subsection{Class II compatibility statement}

The canonical minimal Class II correction changes only the shell-relevant derivative tensor coefficients:
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{eff}}=A_0-\Gamma c_\parallel,
\qquad
B_{\mathrm{eff}}=B_0-\Gamma c_I,
\qquad
C_{\mathrm{eff}}=C_0-\Gamma c_J,
\label{eq:ClassII_changes_ABC}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\Gamma=\frac{\lambda g_X m}{M_X^2}.
\label{eq:Gamma_gap}
\end{equation}
It does \emph{not} by itself prove a remote gap.
Rather, its correct theorem-level status is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is gap-compatible, but }\Delta>0\text{ still requires an independent spectral check.}
}
\label{eq:ClassII_gap_compatible}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Schur-complement consequence}

From Step 3 we already have
\begin{equation}
V(0)=0,
\qquad
\|V(p)\|\le c|p|.
\label{eq:V_small_step4}
\end{equation}
If \(|E|<\Delta/2\), then
\begin{equation}
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}.
\label{eq:resolvent_step4}
\end{equation}
Hence the Schur-complement self-energy
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(E,p)=V(p)(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}V(p)^\dagger
\label{eq:Sigma_step4}
\end{equation}
satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|
\le
\frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2.
}
\label{eq:Sigma_bound_step4}
\end{equation}
Therefore the effective low-energy Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
}
\label{eq:Heff_step4}
\end{equation}
So once \(\Delta>0\) is established, the remote sector changes only the subleading quadratic curvature and does not destroy the leading local Dirac cone.

\subsection{Step 4 in the obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation}

Combining the previous steps, the concrete truncation now has:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Step 1: local Weyl nondegeneracy on the region
\[
\Gamma c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,\ \Gamma c_J\right)\neq (0,0);
\]
\item Step 2: opposite-valley witness matching;
\item Step 3: zero constant mixing \(V(0)=0\) reduced to the finite mismatch audit;
\item Step 4: remote-gap positivity reduced to either:
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}>\eta_{R,\rho},
\]
or
\[
\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

Thus Step 4 is closed at the same honest level as the notes:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the remote-gap problem is fully reduced to a finite spectral inequality / bounded-perturbation audit.}
}
\label{eq:Step4_closed_honest}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

The strongest honest statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation, }\Delta>0\text{ is not automatic,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its verification is completely reduced to an explicit finite remote spectral audit.}
}
\label{eq:Step4_honest_final}
\end{equation}
So Step 4 is now closed at the theorem-reduction level.

%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of Dirac Step 4 in the Obstruction-Baseline + Class II Truncation}

\paragraph{What was actually established.}
The remote gap condition
\[
\Delta>0
\]
is an independent spectral input.
It is not implied by the local shell determinant
\[
\det M=A(B^2+C^2)\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Two honest theorem-level routes.}
Step 4 is reduced to one of the following finite checks:

\paragraph{(A) Direct finite spectral inequality}
Define
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}:=\inf_{|p|\le \rho}\delta_0(p),
\qquad
\eta_{R,\rho}:=\sup_{|p|\le \rho}\|R_R(p)\|.
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\Longrightarrow
\Delta_\rho=\delta_{0,\rho}-\eta_{R,\rho}>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{(B) Bounded perturbation from an already-gapped benchmark}
If
\[
\operatorname{spec}(H_R^{(0)}(p))\cap(-\Delta_0,\Delta_0)=\varnothing
\]
and
\[
\sup_{|p|\le p_*}\|\delta H_R(p)\|<\Delta_0,
\]
then
\[
\boxed{
\Delta=\Delta_0-\sup\|\delta H_R\|>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Class II status.}
The canonical minimal Class II correction only renormalizes the shell-relevant coefficients
\[
A_{\mathrm{eff}},\quad B_{\mathrm{eff}},\quad C_{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is gap-compatible, but does not by itself prove } \Delta>0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Schur-complement consequence.}
Once
\[
V(0)=0,\qquad \|V(p)\|\le c|p|,
\qquad \Delta>0,
\]
one gets
\[
\boxed{
\|(H_R(p)-E)^{-1}\|\le \frac{2}{\Delta}
\qquad (|E|<\Delta/2),
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\|\Sigma(E,p)\|\le \frac{2c^2}{\Delta}|p|^2,
\qquad
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(E,p)=H_D(p)+O\!\left(\frac{|p|^2}{\Delta}\right).
}
\]

\paragraph{Honest frontier.}
So Step 4 is now closed at the reduction-theorem level.
What remains open is only the actual finite remote spectral audit:
\[
\boxed{
\delta_{0,\rho}^{\mathrm{bench}}-\eta_{R,\rho}\stackrel{?}{>}0
}
\]
or, equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_0-\sup\|\delta H_R\|\stackrel{?}{>}0.
}
\]

\section{Dirac Step 5: Mass Protection in the Obstruction-Baseline + Class II Truncation}

\subsection{Goal}

After Step 1 (Weyl nondegeneracy), Step 2 (opposite-valley matching), Step 3 (\(V(0)=0\)), and Step 4 (\(\Delta>0\)),
the last remaining local Dirac closure condition is the absence of a symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass.

The correct theorem-level question is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):\{K,\Gamma_i\}=0\ \forall i\}
=
\{0\},
}
\label{eq:massprot_finite_test}
\end{equation}
where \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\) is the allowed constant operator algebra under the residual low-energy symmetry.

\subsection{Doubled local Dirac block and the mass space}

After Step 2, the local doubled shell block has the Dirac form
\begin{equation}
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i).
\label{eq:HD_step5}
\end{equation}
The full little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operator space on the doubled block is
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:K_space_step5}
\end{equation}
Among these, the genuine constant Dirac-mass space is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:mass_space_step5}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual microscopic mass-protection problem is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:Ares_cap_mass}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Why opposite-valley matching alone is not enough}

Opposite-valley matching fixes the relation
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
\]
and therefore yields the doubled Dirac structure.
But it does \emph{not} by itself remove the allowed constant operators
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{opposite-valley matching is necessary for doubling, but not sufficient for mass protection.}
}
\label{eq:ov_not_enough}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Residual-symmetry audit table}

At the theorem level, the practical classification is:

\[
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Residual structure}
&
\text{Action on }\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\ \tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
&
\text{Does it forbid all constant masses?}
\\
\hline
\text{little-group scalarity only}
&
\text{allows both}
&
\text{No}
\\
\hline
\text{opposite-valley matching only}
&
\text{fixes doubling but does not remove }\tau_x,\tau_y
&
\text{No}
\\
\hline
\text{exact valley }U(1)_V
&
(\tau_x,\tau_y)\ \text{rotate as a charged doublet}
&
\text{Yes}
\\
\hline
\text{exact valley }\mathbb Z_2^V
&
\tau_x,\tau_y\mapsto -\tau_x,-\tau_y
&
\text{Yes}
\\
\hline
\text{Class II gradient-linear structure}
&
\text{does not insert a constant mass directly}
&
\text{Compatible only}
\end{array}
\]

\subsection{Exact valley \(U(1)_V\) as a sufficient protection mechanism}

Define the valley-charge generator
\begin{equation}
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta:=e^{\,i\theta Q_V/2}.
\label{eq:QV_step5}
\end{equation}
Since
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0,
\label{eq:QV_comm_HD}
\end{equation}
the doubled kinetic block is compatible with a residual valley \(U(1)_V\).

Now
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:taux_rotate}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:tauy_rotate}
\end{equation}
Therefore no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_D\) is invariant under all \(\theta\), so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:U1_forbids_mass}
\end{equation}
Hence exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) is sufficient for full constant mass protection.

\subsection{Exact valley \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is already enough}

The full continuous \(U(1)_V\) is stronger than necessary.
The discrete remnant
\begin{equation}
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4
\label{eq:SV_step5}
\end{equation}
already suffices, because
\begin{equation}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:SV_forbid}
\end{equation}
Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:Z2_forbids_mass}
\end{equation}
So exact residual valley \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is a weaker but still sufficient mechanism.

\subsection{Compatibility with the obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation}

The canonical minimal Class II representative is
\begin{equation}
m^a(P_0)=m\delta^{a3},
\qquad
C^{33}_{ij}=c_\parallel \hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
C^{31}_{ij}=c_I \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_J \hat n_i e_{2j},
\qquad
C^{32}_{ij}=-c_J \hat n_i e_{1j}+c_I \hat n_i e_{2j}.
\label{eq:ClassII_step5_actual}
\end{equation}
Its role is to renormalize the derivative shell tensor coefficients \(A,B,C\), equivalently the first-order local Weyl/Dirac witnesses.
It does not by construction insert an independent constant \(4\times4\) Dirac mass operator.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with mass protection, but is not by itself a proof of mass protection.}
}
\label{eq:ClassII_mass_compatible}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Radiative stability under remote-sector elimination}

Assume the full microscopic theory preserves the residual valley symmetry, meaning there exists a unitary action
\[
U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta}
\]
such that
\begin{equation}
(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p)
(U_\theta\oplus U_{R,\theta})^{-1}
=
H_{\mathrm{full}}(p).
\label{eq:full_valley_sym_step5}
\end{equation}
Then the Schur-complement shell Hamiltonian
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(p,\omega)
=
H_D(p)
+
V(p)^\dagger
\bigl(\omega-H_R(p)\bigr)^{-1}
V(p)
\label{eq:Heff_Schur_step5}
\end{equation}
inherits the same symmetry.
In particular, the zero-momentum self-energy
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0):=
V(0)^\dagger\bigl(-H_R(0)\bigr)^{-1}V(0)
\label{eq:Sigma00_step5}
\end{equation}
must commute with \(Q_V\):
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,\Sigma(0,0)]=0.
\label{eq:Sigma_comm_step5}
\end{equation}
If we also impose little-group scalarity at the crossing, then
\begin{equation}
\Sigma(0,0)
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Sigma_allowed_step5}
\end{equation}
Hence no radiatively generated term proportional to
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\]
can appear.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{if the residual valley symmetry is exact and survives remote elimination, mass protection is radiatively stable.}
}
\label{eq:radiative_stability_step5}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Combined Step 1--Step 5 status}

Inside the obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation we now have:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Step 1: local Weyl nondegeneracy on the region
\[
\Gamma c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(\frac{4Z}{A}-\Gamma c_I,\ \Gamma c_J\right)\neq (0,0);
\]

\item Step 2: opposite-valley witness matching;

\item Step 3: zero constant mixing \(V(0)=0\) reduced to the finite mismatch audit;

\item Step 4: remote spectral gap \(\Delta>0\) reduced to either
\[
\delta_{0,\rho}>\eta_{R,\rho}
\quad\text{or}\quad
\|\delta H_R\|<\Delta_0;
\]

\item Step 5: mass protection reduced to the finite constant-operator classification
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
\]
with exact valley \(U(1)_V\) or exact valley \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) as sufficient symmetry mechanisms.
\end{enumerate}

Thus Step 5 is now closed at the same theorem-reduction level as the previous steps.

\subsection{Sharp honest conclusion}

The strongest honest conclusion is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{inside the obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation, mass protection is not automatic,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{its verification is fully reduced to a finite }4\times4\text{ residual-symmetry operator audit.}
}
\label{eq:massprot_honest_final}
\end{equation}

If the actual full microscopic TECT/Class II realization preserves an exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\) or \(\mathbb Z_2^V\), then all constant Dirac masses are forbidden.

%%%%%%%%

\section{Final Summary of Dirac Step 5 in the Obstruction-Baseline + Class II Truncation}

\paragraph{What was actually established.}
For the doubled local Dirac block
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\]
the genuine constant Dirac-mass space is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\]

\paragraph{Finite protection criterion.}
Mass protection is exactly the finite classification problem
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\cap
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):\{K,\Gamma_i\}=0\ \forall i\}
=
\{0\}.
}
\]

\paragraph{What is not enough.}
Neither little-group scalarity alone nor opposite-valley matching alone forbids all constant masses.

\paragraph{Sufficient mechanisms.}
If the actual residual symmetry contains either:
\[
\boxed{
\text{exact valley }U(1)_V
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\text{exact valley }\mathbb Z_2^V,
}
\]
then all constant Dirac masses are forbidden.

\paragraph{Class II status.}
The canonical minimal Class II correction only renormalizes the first-order shell tensor coefficients \(A,B,C\).
So
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with mass protection, but is not by itself a proof of it.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Radiative stability.}
If the same residual valley symmetry is exact in the full microscopic theory and survives remote-sector elimination, then no symmetry-preserving self-energy can generate a constant Dirac mass.

\paragraph{Combined status.}
Therefore, inside the obstruction-baseline + Class II truncation:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Step 5 is now closed at the theorem-reduction level.}
}
\]
What remains open is only the actual microscopic identification of the residual symmetry algebra in the full TECT/Class II realization.
